# Standing and Answerability Ethics Wiki Context

This file is generated from the canonical page manifest and `src/app/wiki/mdx/*.mdx` for use as LLM context.
Only canonical pages are included. Alias routes are recorded with their targets but are not duplicated. Each page is included as context-ready MDX inside a fenced block: visible generated components are expanded into Markdown, theory-metadata tags are omitted because their values appear in page headers, and hidden contract source markers are omitted because the theory contract records their definition sites above.
Read theory positions on independent axes: layer identifies a claim's work, support identifies its warrant, provenance identifies how it entered the corpus, and page dependencies identify immediate premise pages. Comma-separated values within one axis are unordered page-level inventories; local prose assigns them to subclaims. A dependency does not make every conclusion on the dependent page derived. Navigation groups and related-page routes are editorial only.

Release status: active
Page count: 56

## Theory contract

The contract records the canonical source principles and later corpus extensions. Each principle has one definition site in the page sources. Refusal tests reject defended, proposed, and optional premises individually; derived conclusions fall when their premises are refused rather than being reclassified. The contract is an inventory, not a complete principle-level proof graph: follow local dependency statements at the linked definition sites.

### Refusal tests

- **Reject Six-stage pipeline:** Cost: Verdicts revert to case-by-case and their dependencies become less visible. Survives: The conceptual core, diagnostic claims, and any independently accepted operational modules survive.
- **Reject G1 imposition and the protected-exercise filter:** Cost: The claim roster overgenerates or loses directedness where another holder's exercise causes a setback. Survives: Standing, answerability, and the other claim grounds survive; imposition cases return to narrower source-specific arguments.
- **Reject G2 initiation:** Cost: Beginnings claims lose their general form outside the inherited source asymmetry. Survives: The source asymmetry and the remaining claim grounds survive.
- **Reject Controlled-route evidential burden:** Cost: Formal exit or consultation can count as evidence against holding or nullity without a shifted burden even where the arrangement controls the route and its record. Survives: The holding ground, possession marks, open practical-availability and effective-contest thresholds, and need for empirical assessment survive under ordinary evidential allocation.
- **Reject G6 need:** Cost: Urgent rescue returns to supererogation and institutionally grounded provision rather than a situational directed claim. Survives: Imposition, initiation, holding, exercise, responsiveness, and institutional provision claims survive.
- **Reject General means-bound:** Cost: Claims may demand another party's conversion, special relations may force such means into option sets, and scale-invariant exclusion falls. Survives: Standing, the claim grounds, and the possession diagnosis survive, but possession becomes potentially selectable.
- **Reject G6 sacrifice cap:** Cost: The need ground becomes unbounded in demandingness. Survives: The proposed need ground and the general means-bound survive.
- **Reject Provision grounds, function-set limit, and anti-relabeling check:** Cost: The distinction between claims and preferences either collapses or constricts ordinary public provision. Survives: Holding and exercise grounds survive, but no general institutional provision module remains.
- **Reject Working account of the holder's good:** Cost: Claim contents and comparative gravities lose their common metric. Survives: The conceptual core and claim grounds survive, but the diagnostic and operational systems lack a content measure.
- **Reject Proxy discipline and beneficiary bar:** Cost: Interested beneficiaries may certify descriptions of holders who cannot contest them. Survives: The holder's good and valid performed exercises survive; stewardship loses its independence discipline.
- **Reject Genuine-reason candidacy threshold:** Cost: This candidacy threshold and conduct conclusions that depend on it fall unless another precautionary rule is supplied for uncertain sentience. Survives: The sentience criterion, full standing of established someones, and ordinary claims and risk duties toward known parties survive.
- **Reject Modal dischargeability of candidacy:** Cost: The route ground needs another anti-ratchet exit rule; requiring practical discharge can make present opacity defeat candidacy rather than prolong it. Survives: The differential floor, parity, expression ground, conditional route ground, and standing of established someones survive.
- **Reject Priority rules across time:** Cost: The theory tends toward biographical paternalism or toward treating directives as absolute in every respect. Survives: Authorization, settlement, and the holder's good survive without a complete priority order.
- **Reject Present implementation constraint:** Cost: Present suffering either ceases to count or automatically repeals prior directives. Survives: Valid exercises, scope interpretation, and the unresolved diachronic-weight question survive.
- **Reject Adequacy conditions (a), (c), and (e):** Cost: Justifiability to a holder reverts to an unfilled placeholder. Survives: Answerability and the demand for an account survive without a complete adequacy criterion.
- **Reject Relevance-band silencing:** Cost: Comparison loses its categorical exclusion of sufficiently lesser claims at every multiplier and requires another account of relevance. This refusal alone selects neither unrestricted aggregation nor any particular rival. Survives: Claim identification, pairwise address, the defended same-order counting rule, and the open admission of unresolved comparison survive unless a replacement rule revises them.
- **Reject Counting claims of the same order:** Cost: Equal-order ties return to equal-chance lotteries or another rival rule. Survives: Silencing, pairwise expression, and the open cell survive.
- **Reject Duties in the open comparison cell:** Cost: An unresolved comparison can be filled by pretense or unannounced discretion. Survives: The admission that the comparison is unresolved survives.
- **Reject Prospective risk claims:** Cost: Ordinary risk imposition lacks a route to justification before harm materializes. Survives: Materialized imposition, response, and repair claims survive.
- **Reject Pairwise materialized priority:** Cost: Materialized and probability-discounted claims can be treated as level in pairwise comparison. Survives: Prospective claims, materialization, and the open many-claim comparison survive.
- **Reject Possession marks, tests, jointness, and level rule:** Cost: Classification returns to disputes over labels or to level-shopping. Survives: The source diagnostic vocabulary and the underlying standing claims survive.
- **Reject Possession's address argument:** Cost: Possession's categorical ineligibility reverts to assertion or becomes a weighable burden. Survives: The three-mark possession diagnosis survives.
- **Reject Scale-invariant exclusion:** Cost: The joint presence of many claims can force possession into the option set. Survives: Each holder's separate standing, the possession diagnosis, and the single-claim means-bound case survive.
- **Reject Catastrophe amendment:** Cost: No canonical claim is lost; declining the amendment is the canonical position. Survives: The means-bound and the unresolved pairwise-exhaustion dispute survive; scale-invariant exclusion follows only conditional on pairwise exhaustion.
- **Reject Constraint of persons:** Cost: The framework lacks a general account of constraint against non-culpable threats. Survives: Possession, claim protection, and source claims about wrongdoers survive.
- **Reject Forced sets, four statuses, and necessity-justified wronging:** Cost: Forced sets return to silence or to a verdict that blurs required action with harmless action. Survives: The underlying claims, wrongs, and comparison limits survive without a complete deontic classification.
- **Reject Blame, excuse, and prior fault:** Cost: Agent-level and act-level questions collapse back together. Survives: The four act classifications and residue survive.
- **Reject Exit categories and the forced-transition frontier:** Cost: Gradual exit can become the default even where immediate cessation was available. Survives: The possession verdict, necessity architecture, and residue claims survive without a transition rule.
- **Reject Controlled-function participation bridge:** Cost: Purchasing, investment, consumption, and other external support cannot be classified as participation without a separate argument, so no withdrawal duty follows for those cases from Exit alone. Survives: Possession, the exit duty for established operators, maintainers, and administrators, and the necessity-governed frontier survive.
- **Reject Differentiated residue and concentration conditions:** Cost: Every burden tends to become compensable, or formal reciprocity defeats claims from those who bear concentrated loss. Survives: G5 responsiveness and the open account survive without this taxonomy.
- **Reject Claim-protection requirement for enforcement:** Cost: Perfectionist enforcement reopens. Survives: Adequacy, answerable-enforcer, and instrument requirements survive.
- **Reject Differentiated bodily structures:** Cost: Bodily cases are forced into one formula or reopened case by case. Survives: The general enforcement gate and each independently accepted source-domain bodily rule survive.
- **Reject Authority legs, finalities, and reopening discipline:** Cost: Institutional authority remains under-grounded and closure tends toward unlimited reopening or moral closure. Survives: The conceptual distinction between adjudication and settlement survives.
- **Reject Institutional answerability rows:** Cost: The recursion objection stands and the political half of the framework falls. Survives: Directed claims against institutions and diagnostic wrongs survive without a viable answerability design.
- **Reject Foreclosure-minimizing default for unresolved comparison:** Cost: Delay and the status quo can escape audit unless a rival default replaces it. Survives: The open cell and the requirement to state unresolved comparison survive.
- **Reject Present, transition, and historical statuses:** Cost: Historical classification becomes permanent or reform can occur by announcement. Survives: The present three-mark diagnosis and historical residue survive.
- **Reject Necessity-order conditions and role-obligation limits:** Cost: Institutions may compel wrongs on their own certification, and role acceptance can become settlement against officials. Survives: Necessity-justified wronging, the enforcement gate, officials' standing, and institutional answerability claims survive without an ordering rule; necessity does not become enforcement adequacy.
- **Reject Completeness module:** Cost: The framework does not claim all of morality and remains silent about impersonal wrongs. Survives: Everything else in the framework survives unchanged.

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics.mdx

- Title: Standing and Answerability Ethics
- Slug: Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics
- Aliases: /wiki/Numean-Ethics
- Navigation group: Corpus orientation

````mdx
# Standing and Answerability Ethics

## Summary

**Standing and Answerability Ethics**, or **the Standing Framework**, is a theory of directed obligation among sentient parties developed by Nume. It asks how claims arise against particular addressees, what those claims require, when conduct can be justified to a holder whose claim remains unsatisfied, what no party may be made into, what remains owed afterward, and how institutions can decide and enforce while remaining answerable to those they bind.

The foundation is that every sentient being is a [someone](/wiki/Someone): a party, never a quantity. That foundation does not make every effect a directed obligation. Claims arise through identifiable [grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds), and their contents are fixed before conflict by [the holder's own good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good), the ground, and the situation. The framework then distinguishes diagnosis from operation: what is owed and what wrongs are not the same question as what to do when claims cannot all be satisfied.

This is not a complete moral theory. It has no theory of desert, its account of the good is a working account for claim content and gravity, and it remains silent about impersonal value unless an optional completeness module is adopted. Where its comparison or institutional machinery runs out, the result is stated as open rather than completed by implication.

## The doctrinal spine

The framework has three theory-building layers: conceptual core, diagnostic theory, and operational system. Application and orientation remain separate values on the layer axis because they perform different work, but they do not add further stages to the theory's load-bearing sequence.

### Conceptual core

The **conceptual core** identifies the theory's parties and fixed relations.

- A [someone](/wiki/Someone) is any sentient being, and someones remain separate parties rather than components of an aggregate claimant.
- [Standing](/wiki/Standing) is the equal status of being eligible to hold claims. It distinguishes demands from exercises without turning standing itself into a universal claim-generator.
- [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) is the relation of owing a holder an [account](/wiki/Account); [authorization](/wiki/Authorization) is a valid grant performed by the holder. A standard is not a grantor.
- [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) is prohibited closure entered in another's name, without the holder's governing exercise and in the closer's favor. Justification can leave an account open; authorization and acceptance cannot be manufactured to close it.

The core is source-framework material. Rejecting its foundation dissolves the theory; rejecting a later reconstruction does not retroactively alter the core.

### Diagnostic theory

The **diagnostic theory** identifies claims, wrongs, and limits on justification. Its first module is [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds): imposition, initiation, holding, exercise, responsiveness, and need. These six grounds have mixed support and provenance. They are not presented as a single derivation, and their exhaustiveness remains open.

Two qualifications enter at this stage. The defended [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) holds that no claim contains another party's conversion. [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) reconstructs when shared benefits and institutional functions are genuinely owed rather than merely wanted.

[The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) proposes a working account of claim content and gravity across experiential, agential, and relational-biographical dimensions, while [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) governs present exercises, prior exercises, inferred ordering, and present claims. [Possession](/wiki/Possession) supplies the three-mark party-preserving test. [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) then consolidates whether routes invoked by holding, nullity, ongoing adequacy, and institutional answerability operate from the holder's position. [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) states the mixed-register conditions proposed for every holder whose claim remains unsatisfied, and [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) governs restraint at possession's boundary.

The source framework's diagnostic vocabulary remains important: [Possession](/wiki/Possession), [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use), [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization), and [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) identify recurring forms of conversion and refusal. Their reconstructed tests and dependencies must retain the registers marked on their pages.

### Operational system

The **operational system** begins with the [Six-Stage Pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline): identify claims, fix their contents, map options, compare, classify each unsatisfied claim, and determine [residue](/wiki/Residue). [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) filters and ranks where it can while preserving its relevance-band and open-cell limits. [Risk](/wiki/Risk) distinguishes prospective due care from materialized response, and [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) distinguishes a required act from the wrong it can still do.

[Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) confines gradual transition to genuine forced sets. [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) supplies the joint gate for turning standards into coercion, including the differentiated rules for bodies. [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) then reconstructs authority, adjudication, finality, review, and institutional necessity orders. These modules are mixed-register operational proposals, not implications concealed inside the foundation.

Refusing an operational proposal does not weaken it into an intuition while preserving its verdict. It restores the gap the proposal was built to fill. The framework can therefore retain a diagnostic conclusion while lacking a complete method for selecting conduct in a conflict.

## Claims and diagnosis

The directed-obligation structure begins with a roster: who holds what claim against whom, on which [claim ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds), and with what content fixed by [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good). The grounds prevent two opposite errors: treating every valuable outcome as owed, and treating only consent or comparative harm as capable of directing an obligation.

Diagnosis then asks whether each option can be justified to every holder whose claim it leaves unsatisfied. [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) states the criteria, [Possession](/wiki/Possession) identifies conduct categorically unavailable to its target, and the [Six-Stage Pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline) keeps those questions distinct from comparison and residue.

## Beginnings and applications

The beginnings line operates within the grounds architecture. [Newness](/wiki/Newness) states that no prior holder authorizes, claims, or settles a beginning. [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) applies the initiation ground once a someone exists. Neither conclusion alone establishes [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework), which depends on the further defended origination anti-bootstrapping principle.

The applications address parenthood, reproductive jurisdiction, animal use, labor, administration, punishment, end-of-life decisions, artificial minds, movements, and institutions. Each identifies its grounds and distinguishes source claims from reconstructed diagnostics and proposed operational rules. A result survives only through the dependencies it can actually state.

## Guardrails

- **No aggregate claimant.** Counts and comparisons do not create a further someone to whom the total is owed.
- **No external life-verdict.** No party may use the premise that another's life is not worth living or continuing.
- **No counterfeit exercise.** Silence, prediction, later approval, or manufactured endorsement is not authorization.
- **No closure by the answerable party.** Reasons can justify without becoming the holder's release or acquittal.
- **No reproductive coercion from defended doctrine.** A position about procreation supplies no authority over another holder's body.
- **Standing survives wrongdoing.** Culpability can change claims and residue; it does not turn a someone into material.

## Optional completeness

The framework is complete within its domain of directed obligation. The **optional completeness module** is a completion the canonical theory does not adopt. It holds that all moral requirements are owed to someones: adequacy to each affected party is sufficient as well as necessary for justified action. Adopted, the module extends the framework to claim all of morality and denies independent impersonal wrongs. Refused, insentient nature, desecration without living claimants, and wholly self-regarding corruption remain outside the framework unless they can be redescribed through claims held by someones. Nothing else in the theory depends on adopting the module.

## Registers and refusal

[Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) separates layer, support, and provenance, then records immediate dependencies. Concept and doctrine pages state a visible theory position and dependency line. Orientation, inventory, rival-view, and practical-orientation pages may omit doctrinal metadata where their role is not to advance a claim within the framework.

Refusal follows actual dependencies. Rejecting a defended, proposed, or optional premise removes the conclusions that depend on it without weakening independent foundational or reconstructed claims. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) records unresolved premises, missing theory, empirical dependencies, and principled indeterminacies. [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) governs circulation: a dependency map is an aid to refusal and correction, not a tribunal certifying its own labels.

## Corpus map

The groups below organize navigation, not claim strength. On doctrinal pages, the visible theory-position and dependency lines govern. Orientation and rival pages may appear in the sequence without acquiring doctrinal standing.
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Points-of-Entry.mdx

- Title: Points of Entry
- Slug: Points-of-Entry
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Corpus orientation

````mdx
# Points of Entry

## Summary

**Points of entry** is a problem-oriented index to [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics). The main page maps the corpus by conceptual architecture; this page routes readers by the work they need the framework to do or by the domain in which a question arises. [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) should be kept beside either route because usefulness does not strengthen a page's premises.

Entry is not endorsement. A reader may use one diagnostic while rejecting its operational completion, or use an application to locate the premise at which disagreement begins. The dependency entries on rebuilt pages identify where that refusal propagates.

## By theoretical task

**Identifying the parties and relations.** Begin with [Someone](/wiki/Someone), [Standing](/wiki/Standing), [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability), [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization), [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement), and [Account](/wiki/Account). This route supplies the conceptual core without yet claiming a complete roster of obligations or a conflict method.

**Identifying directed claims.** Begin with [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds), then [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound), [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims), [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good), and [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time). This route asks who owes what to whom before asking which option should be selected.

**Diagnosing conversion and constraint.** Begin with [Possession](/wiki/Possession), then use [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use), [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization), [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession), and [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons). These pages distinguish a grave burden from making a party into material, and stopping a party from consuming them.

**Deciding among conflicting claims.** Begin with the [Six-Stage Pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline), followed by [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline), [Risk](/wiki/Risk), [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity), [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures), and [Residue](/wiki/Residue). The route includes the relevance band's missing metric and the open cell; it is not an algorithm disguised as a sequence.

**Auditing authority and coercion.** Begin with [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest), [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification), [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement), and [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability). This route distinguishes nominal from usable routes, a standard from a grantor, enforceability from correctness, adjudicative finality from settlement, and formal safeguards from demonstrated circulation.

**Testing or refusing the system.** Begin with [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim), [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions), and [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context). [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) supplies the strongest rival framing of beginnings; [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) separates framework doctrine from Nume's personal practical orientation.

## By applied problem

| Problem | Starting pages | Boundary to preserve |
|---|---|---|
| Procreation and non-identity | [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure), [Newness](/wiki/Newness), [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) | The antinatalist conclusion depends on a defended bridge and supplies no reproductive enforcement. |
| Pregnancy and bodily jurisdiction | [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics), [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) | Jurisdiction does not settle fetal sentience or rank lives. |
| Parenthood, adoption, and formation | [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood), [Adoption and Relinquishment](/wiki/Adoption-and-Relinquishment) | Initiation grounds responsibility without creating ownership or a repayment claim. |
| Future people and institutions | [Mixed Intergenerational Cases](/wiki/Mixed-Intergenerational-Cases), [Risk](/wiki/Risk), [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) | Identity-affecting action does not erase future claims, but concrete policy still requires evidence and design. |
| Animal use and rescue | [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics), [Possession](/wiki/Possession), [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) | Sentience establishes a party; the possession marks and transition facts establish the verdict and response. |
| Labor and engineered options | [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity), [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) | Contract form does not certify a survivable exit or an answerable arrangement. |
| Administration and public systems | [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility), [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability), [Residue](/wiki/Residue) | Records can protect and expose; institutional effectiveness is empirical. |
| Punishment and restraint | [Standing-Based Punishment Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics), [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons), [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) | Protection claims can justify constraint; culpability does not erase standing, and desert remains open. |
| End-of-life decisions | [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics), [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time), [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) | First-person exercises and third-party life-worth verdicts remain distinct. |
| Artificial minds | [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds), [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) | Precaution is conditional and does not establish sentience. |
| Disability policy | [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention), [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) | Provision claims concern existing parties; prevention cannot become a verdict on their lives. |
| Family, gratitude, and exit | [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt), [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) | Gratitude and attachment do not themselves authorize debt, capture, or punitive exit costs. |
| Advocacy and movements | [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice), [Grievance and Capture](/wiki/Grievance-and-Capture), [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) | Speaking for others performs no exercise for them; practical orientation remains distinct from doctrine. |

## By critical pressure

**Against the foundation.** A reader who denies that sentient beings are parties rather than quantities should begin at [Someone](/wiki/Someone). The later machinery does not derive the foundation it uses.

**Against non-aggregation.** A reader who accepts separate parties but rejects counting, silencing, pairwise exhaustion, or the means-bound should begin at [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline), [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound), and [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions). The corpus states the catastrophe alternative and the costs of each refusal.

**Against categorical possession.** A reader who treats possession as a weighable burden should begin at [Possession](/wiki/Possession) and [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification). The dispute is over justification-as-address, not over whether subordination, nullity, and extraction are serious.

**Against the operational system.** A reader can retain directed claims and diagnostic wrongs while rejecting the proposed pipeline, necessity statuses, residue differentiation, or institutional design. [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) explains why refusal restores a gap rather than silently preserving the same verdict.

## Limits

- The page maps routes, not audiences or movements to which the framework claims to belong.
- Starting pages are not sufficient premises. Their `Depends on` entries identify what a conclusion inherits.
- A problem can cross several routes; the table selects a useful first page rather than declaring ownership of the subject.

## Related pages

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) · [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context) · [Six-Stage Pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Registers-of-Claim.mdx

- Title: Registers of Claim
- Slug: Registers-of-Claim
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Corpus orientation

````mdx
# Registers of Claim

## Summary

The Standing Framework classifies claims on three independent axes: **layer**, **support**, and **provenance**. Layer identifies the work a claim performs in the theory; support identifies what warrants it; provenance identifies how it entered the corpus. The axes are kept separate because a reconstruction is not thereby a derivation, an operational rule is not thereby optional, and an application can contain claims at several strengths. Where a page lists several values on one axis, the list is an unordered inventory of positions present on that page, not a priority ranking or a claim that every value applies to every conclusion; local prose assigns the values to subclaims.

Registers describe warrant and dependency; they do not certify truth. **Refusal** traces what survives when a reader declines a refusable premise. **Defeat** shows that a claim is false, invalid, contradictory, misclassified, or unfaithfully reconstructed and therefore requires revision rather than treatment as a reader's optional exit.

This page is an orientation and inventory page rather than a doctrinal module. It defines the register vocabulary, explains how pages display dependencies, and distinguishes refusal from evidence or argument that defeats a claim.

## Layer

**Conceptual core.** The source framework's foundation and fixed conceptual relations: [someone](/wiki/Someone), [standing](/wiki/Standing), demands and exercises, [answerability](/wiki/Answerability) against [authorization](/wiki/Authorization), the [settlement](/wiki/Settlement) prohibition, and the [account](/wiki/Account). The core identifies the parties and relations the rest of the theory uses; it does not by itself produce a complete roster of claims or a method for resolving conflicts.

**Diagnostic theory.** The account of what is owed, what wrongs, and what cannot justify itself to its target. It includes [claim grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds), [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good), [authority across time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time), [adequate justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification), [possession](/wiki/Possession), and [constraint](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons). Diagnostic claims may be reconstructed, generalized, clarified, derived, defended, proposed, open, or empirical; membership in the layer does not settle support.

**Operational system.** The architecture for acting when claims interact: the [six-stage pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline), [comparison](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline), [risk](/wiki/Risk), [necessity](/wiki/Necessity), [exit](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures), [residue](/wiki/Residue), [enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement), and [institutional decision](/wiki/Standing-Answerability). Much of this layer is proposed rather than derived. Refusing one of its rules removes the capacity that rule supplied; it does not leave the same verdict in place by a weaker route.

**Application.** A domain-specific use of the earlier layers. Applications inherit only the premises they state. They do not acquire the support status of a layer as a whole, and a defended application does not weaken the premises it validly uses.

**Orientation.** Indexes, intellectual context, practical orientation, rival views, and editorial maps. These pages help readers locate claims without giving the orientation itself doctrinal authority.

The layers are load-ordered, not ranked by importance. The conceptual core can remain while a diagnostic interpretation is refused; diagnostic verdicts can remain while an operational proposal is refused; an application fails only where one of its actual dependencies fails.

Navigation groups are separate from these layers. They place pages in a usable reading sequence, including orientation pages, rival views, and practical-orientation material, without assigning those pages a theory position.

## Support

**Foundational.** A commitment the framework presents but does not derive. The foundation is that every sentient being is a party rather than a quantity. Bedrock inherited from that commitment is marked rather than redescribed as proof.

**Derived.** A conclusion that follows from stated premises and inferences. Every indispensable premise, including bridge premises, must be visible. A conclusion can be derived *given* a defended or proposed premise; the inference is valid without promoting the premise, and refusing the premise removes the conditional conclusion.

**Defended.** A substantive position argued for but not entailed by the accepted foundations and derivations. Defended claims are refusable at the cost stated on their pages.

**Proposed.** Architecture or completion offered because the prior theory needs a rule, distinction, or procedure that it did not already contain. A proposal may be well supported and still remain a proposal. Refusing it restores the earlier gap.

**Optional.** A module not adopted by the canonical theory but specified as a coherent amendment. Optional differs from proposed: a proposal belongs to the canonical construction while remaining refusable; an optional module is an alternative the construction declines unless expressly adopted.

**Open.** A question the framework does not resolve, together with the premise, evidence, or conceptual work a resolution would require. The inventory is at [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions).

**Empirical.** A claim whose truth depends on evidence rather than the framework's conceptual machinery. Empirical support can be necessary to an application without becoming philosophical doctrine.

## Provenance

**Source framework** marks material developed by Nume before the present reconstruction. **Reconstruction** organizes or interprets that material without claiming that the organization was already explicit. **Generalization** extends a source claim beyond its original domain. **Clarification** resolves an ambiguity or supplies explicit content to an inherited formula. **Completion** adds machinery where the inherited framework stopped. **Application** carries prior machinery into a domain. **Rival** presents a position the framework does not adopt. **Personal orientation** records Nume's own refusable practice or stance. **Editorial** marks navigation, history, or corpus administration.

Provenance is not ownership by itself. A reconstructed or completed claim can still belong to the current Standing Framework; the label records its route into the theory so that a reader can refuse the addition without pretending it was present from the beginning.

## How pages expose position

Concept and doctrine pages state their axes in a fixed order:

> **Theory position:** diagnostic theory · defended · generalization.

They then name immediate dependencies:

> **Depends on:** [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization).

Composite pages may name more than one support or provenance value, then classify important subclaims where they occur. Values within an axis form an unordered page-level inventory; their display order carries no priority, and only local prose determines which value governs a particular claim. Both entries are rendered from the page manifest, which is their sole page-level record for display, validation, and navigation. A dependency means that the page uses the cited module as a premise, not merely that the two pages are related, and does not make every conclusion on the dependent page derived.

Orientation and inventory pages deliberately omit these lines where they classify or route other pages rather than advance doctrine. Rival-view and practical-orientation pages may likewise omit them where their role is to present a position outside the framework's dependency structure. Absence of metadata is intentional only for those roles; it must not be read as an unstated layer, support level, or provenance.

## Refusal and exit

- Rejecting the **foundation** dissolves the directed-obligation theory built on it.
- Rejecting a **derived premise or inference** removes every conclusion that actually depends on it.
- Rejecting a **defended claim** leaves independent core and derived material standing, but removes conclusions derived only given that claim.
- Rejecting a **proposal** returns the problem to the point at which the proposal supplied missing architecture.
- Rejecting an **optional module** leaves the canonical theory unchanged.
- An **open** or **empirical** classification identifies work or evidence still needed; it is not a request to assent.

Refusal propagates by dependency, not by page proximity or rhetorical centrality. [Points of Entry](/wiki/Points-of-Entry) gives the complementary map of where readers may arrive.

### Refusal is not defeat

Refusal records a disagreement while leaving the refused claim represented as the framework actually holds it. A reader can reject a defended premise, decline a proposal, or adopt an optional alternative; the dependency graph then shows the cost without declaring the premise false.

Defeat instead identifies a defect in the corpus or its support. A counterexample can defeat a universal claim; evidence can falsify an empirical classification; an inference can fail or conceal an indispensable bridge; two retained commitments can contradict; a reconstruction can misstate its source; or a register can claim more or less support than the argument supplies. These findings require correction at the definition site and propagation through dependencies, applications, summaries, and metadata. They may not be converted into another refusal row merely to preserve the existing text.

A surprising or unwelcome verdict is not by itself a defeat, just as an intuitive convergence is not confirmation. Either can identify where to test the premises. The register system supplies no commitment that ethical theories are only navigated rather than assessed for truth, coherence, evidence, and validity; it records the support and consequences needed to conduct that assessment without hiding disagreement.

## Limits

- The classification is corrigible. A critic may show that a claimed derivation hides a bridge premise, that a proposed rule follows from accepted premises, or that a reconstruction changes rather than recovers the source.
- Page-level labels are summaries. Where a page contains claims at different positions, local labels and stated dependencies govern.
- Accurate registers do not prevent prose from producing the felt force of a stronger claim. [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) treats presentation as an answerability problem rather than a metadata problem alone.

## What refusal changes

The rules above are enough to interpret a page's register. The audit below is for readers testing a particular refusable premise against the corpus. Each row rejects one defended, proposed, or optional premise, then records what no longer follows and what remains independently supported. It does not certify the premise as true.

### Premise-by-premise refusal audit

| Premise refused | What no longer follows | What remains |
|---|---|---|
| Six-stage pipeline | Verdicts revert to case-by-case and their dependencies become less visible. | The conceptual core, diagnostic claims, and any independently accepted operational modules survive. |
| G1 imposition and the protected-exercise filter | The claim roster overgenerates or loses directedness where another holder's exercise causes a setback. | Standing, answerability, and the other claim grounds survive; imposition cases return to narrower source-specific arguments. |
| G2 initiation | Beginnings claims lose their general form outside the inherited source asymmetry. | The source asymmetry and the remaining claim grounds survive. |
| Controlled-route evidential burden | Formal exit or consultation can count as evidence against holding or nullity without a shifted burden even where the arrangement controls the route and its record. | The holding ground, possession marks, open practical-availability and effective-contest thresholds, and need for empirical assessment survive under ordinary evidential allocation. |
| G6 need | Urgent rescue returns to supererogation and institutionally grounded provision rather than a situational directed claim. | Imposition, initiation, holding, exercise, responsiveness, and institutional provision claims survive. |
| General means-bound | Claims may demand another party's conversion, special relations may force such means into option sets, and scale-invariant exclusion falls. | Standing, the claim grounds, and the possession diagnosis survive, but possession becomes potentially selectable. |
| G6 sacrifice cap | The need ground becomes unbounded in demandingness. | The proposed need ground and the general means-bound survive. |
| Provision grounds, function-set limit, and anti-relabeling check | The distinction between claims and preferences either collapses or constricts ordinary public provision. | Holding and exercise grounds survive, but no general institutional provision module remains. |
| Working account of the holder's good | Claim contents and comparative gravities lose their common metric. | The conceptual core and claim grounds survive, but the diagnostic and operational systems lack a content measure. |
| Proxy discipline and beneficiary bar | Interested beneficiaries may certify descriptions of holders who cannot contest them. | The holder's good and valid performed exercises survive; stewardship loses its independence discipline. |
| Genuine-reason candidacy threshold | This candidacy threshold and conduct conclusions that depend on it fall unless another precautionary rule is supplied for uncertain sentience. | The sentience criterion, full standing of established someones, and ordinary claims and risk duties toward known parties survive. |
| Modal dischargeability of candidacy | The route ground needs another anti-ratchet exit rule; requiring practical discharge can make present opacity defeat candidacy rather than prolong it. | The differential floor, parity, expression ground, conditional route ground, and standing of established someones survive. |
| Priority rules across time | The theory tends toward biographical paternalism or toward treating directives as absolute in every respect. | Authorization, settlement, and the holder's good survive without a complete priority order. |
| Present implementation constraint | Present suffering either ceases to count or automatically repeals prior directives. | Valid exercises, scope interpretation, and the unresolved diachronic-weight question survive. |
| Adequacy conditions (a), (c), and (e) | Justifiability to a holder reverts to an unfilled placeholder. | Answerability and the demand for an account survive without a complete adequacy criterion. |
| Relevance-band silencing | Comparison loses its categorical exclusion of sufficiently lesser claims at every multiplier and requires another account of relevance. This refusal alone selects neither unrestricted aggregation nor any particular rival. | Claim identification, pairwise address, the defended same-order counting rule, and the open admission of unresolved comparison survive unless a replacement rule revises them. |
| Counting claims of the same order | Equal-order ties return to equal-chance lotteries or another rival rule. | Silencing, pairwise expression, and the open cell survive. |
| Duties in the open comparison cell | An unresolved comparison can be filled by pretense or unannounced discretion. | The admission that the comparison is unresolved survives. |
| Prospective risk claims | Ordinary risk imposition lacks a route to justification before harm materializes. | Materialized imposition, response, and repair claims survive. |
| Pairwise materialized priority | Materialized and probability-discounted claims can be treated as level in pairwise comparison. | Prospective claims, materialization, and the open many-claim comparison survive. |
| Possession marks, tests, jointness, and level rule | Classification returns to disputes over labels or to level-shopping. | The source diagnostic vocabulary and the underlying standing claims survive. |
| Possession's address argument | Possession's categorical ineligibility reverts to assertion or becomes a weighable burden. | The three-mark possession diagnosis survives. |
| Scale-invariant exclusion | The joint presence of many claims can force possession into the option set. | Each holder's separate standing, the possession diagnosis, and the single-claim means-bound case survive. |
| Catastrophe amendment | No canonical claim is lost; declining the amendment is the canonical position. | The means-bound and the unresolved pairwise-exhaustion dispute survive; scale-invariant exclusion follows only conditional on pairwise exhaustion. |
| Constraint of persons | The framework lacks a general account of constraint against non-culpable threats. | Possession, claim protection, and source claims about wrongdoers survive. |
| Forced sets, four statuses, and necessity-justified wronging | Forced sets return to silence or to a verdict that blurs required action with harmless action. | The underlying claims, wrongs, and comparison limits survive without a complete deontic classification. |
| Blame, excuse, and prior fault | Agent-level and act-level questions collapse back together. | The four act classifications and residue survive. |
| Exit categories and the forced-transition frontier | Gradual exit can become the default even where immediate cessation was available. | The possession verdict, necessity architecture, and residue claims survive without a transition rule. |
| Controlled-function participation bridge | Purchasing, investment, consumption, and other external support cannot be classified as participation without a separate argument, so no withdrawal duty follows for those cases from Exit alone. | Possession, the exit duty for established operators, maintainers, and administrators, and the necessity-governed frontier survive. |
| Differentiated residue and concentration conditions | Every burden tends to become compensable, or formal reciprocity defeats claims from those who bear concentrated loss. | G5 responsiveness and the open account survive without this taxonomy. |
| Claim-protection requirement for enforcement | Perfectionist enforcement reopens. | Adequacy, answerable-enforcer, and instrument requirements survive. |
| Differentiated bodily structures | Bodily cases are forced into one formula or reopened case by case. | The general enforcement gate and each independently accepted source-domain bodily rule survive. |
| Authority legs, finalities, and reopening discipline | Institutional authority remains under-grounded and closure tends toward unlimited reopening or moral closure. | The conceptual distinction between adjudication and settlement survives. |
| Institutional answerability rows | The recursion objection stands and the political half of the framework falls. | Directed claims against institutions and diagnostic wrongs survive without a viable answerability design. |
| Foreclosure-minimizing default for unresolved comparison | Delay and the status quo can escape audit unless a rival default replaces it. | The open cell and the requirement to state unresolved comparison survive. |
| Present, transition, and historical statuses | Historical classification becomes permanent or reform can occur by announcement. | The present three-mark diagnosis and historical residue survive. |
| Necessity-order conditions and role-obligation limits | Institutions may compel wrongs on their own certification, and role acceptance can become settlement against officials. | Necessity-justified wronging, the enforcement gate, officials' standing, and institutional answerability claims survive without an ordering rule; necessity does not become enforcement adequacy. |
| Completeness module | The framework does not claim all of morality and remains silent about impersonal wrongs. | Everything else in the framework survives unchanged. |

## Related pages
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Open-Questions.mdx

- Title: Open Questions
- Slug: Open-Questions
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Corpus orientation

````mdx
# Open Questions

## Summary

This page inventories the material questions left unresolved by [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics). It separates **missing theory**, **defended disputes**, **empirical and application dependencies**, and **principled indeterminacies**. The categories matter: a defended premise is not a blank, an empirical dependency cannot be supplied by philosophical stipulation, and a result deliberately barred by a source commitment is not missing theory.

[Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) supplies the layer, support, provenance, and dependency vocabulary used here. Local limits that concern only the design or evidence of one application remain on that application's page; inclusion here is reserved for questions that materially affect more than one module or expose a major dependency.

The relevance band's placement, the graver-versus-more-numerous open cell, and the cutoffs governing [practical availability and effective contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) are **missing theory**, not principled indeterminacies. The shared availability-and-contest structure and its proposed controlled-route evidential burden do not resolve either cutoff. The means-bound, origination anti-bootstrapping, and possession's address argument are **defended disputes**; the performance of institutional safeguards, sentience boundaries, and diffuse participation are **empirical or application dependencies**. External verdicts on another's life, closure of another's account, and a global legitimacy verdict are **principled indeterminacies** because identified commitments bar those results.

## Missing theory

### The standard-fixing regress

[Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) fixes conditions for justification to a holder, but the theory itself articulates those conditions. Corrigibility and contest through routes the proponent does not control are its posture toward the question "by what right?"; they do not derive the standard's authority.

**Required:** a non-circular fixing that survives the framework's critique of convention, contract, or ideal acceptance as external grantors, or an argument that corrigible articulation exhausts what authority over such a standard could mean.

### The relevance band and open cell

[Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) proposes a relevance band, defends counting distinct holders among claims of the same order, and leaves open cases in which one graver claim faces more numerous lesser but still relevant claims. No interpersonal metric places the band's boundary, and no exchange principle resolves the open cell.

**Required:** a theory of interpersonal gravity beyond ordinal foreclosure. Pre-committed public rules make a judgment reviewable; they do not supply the missing comparison.

### Practical availability and effective contest

[Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) consolidates the holder-relative structure used by holding, nullity, ongoing adequacy, and institutional answerability. It separates empirical findings about access, cost, retaliation, authority, collision history, and observed alteration from the evaluative judgments those findings inform. Its proposed controlled-route evidential burden determines who must support a route claim where the arrangement controls the route or record; it does not decide the claim.

What remains missing is when a cost forecloses enough of a holder's central interests for exit or refusal to cease being live, and what alteration, at what materiality and durability, makes contest effective. [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) structures both inquiries without computing them. A qualitative standard may be sufficient, but the framework has not yet stated one that distinguishes the cases without presenting judgment as measurement.

**Required:** a qualitative or otherwise defensible cutoff for when central-interest foreclosure defeats practical availability and when alteration is material and durable enough for effective contest. Any completion must preserve the tests' holder-relativity and make remaining judgment visible rather than promise a cardinal metric the framework may not need.

### Diachronic weight

[Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) distinguishes the substance of a prior exercise from the conditions of its present implementation. It does not establish how grave present experiential harm must be to defeat that implementation, nor does it supply a complete theory of capacity, coercion, or changing authority.

**Required:** an account of the authority of past exercises over present experience that preserves both valid prior exercises and the present holder's standing.

### Desert

[Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) and [Standing-Based Punishment Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics) permit protection, censure, restraint, repair, and violation-grade residue without deriving a fitting burden from culpability. The framework has no theory of desert.

**Required:** a fittingness theory connecting culpability to burden without allowing the punished party's standing to disappear inside the judgment.

### The exhaustiveness of claim grounds

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) reconstructs six grounds: imposition, initiation, holding, exercise, responsiveness, and need. They cover the cases tested so far, but no argument shows that a seventh relational type is impossible.

**Required:** a completeness argument over the ways directed obligations can arise, or an explicit decision to keep the roster permanently open.

## Defended disputes

### The means-bound and pairwise exhaustion

[Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) defends the claim that no directed claim contains another party's conversion. Its support states the framework's agent-centered and anti-possession commitment; it does not derive the restriction from the concept of a claim. Scale-invariant exclusion also requires the further premise that deliberative status is exhausted by what can be justified pairwise. The catastrophe opponent can deny that premise while retaining every endangered party's separate standing.

**What would strengthen the position:** an independent conceptual argument for the means-bound and an argument for pairwise exhaustion. The optional catastrophe amendment remains a coherent alternative at the cost of allowing sufficiently grave or numerous claims to require possessive means.

### Origination anti-bootstrapping

[Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) depends on the defended principle that goods internal to a condition created together with their holder do not, without a further independent person-directed ground, sufficiently justify originating that holder. The conditional inference is explicit; the bridge is not derived.

**The live alternative:** expected goods, legitimate reasons held by existing parties, responsible risk assessment, and permanent answerability can jointly provide a defeasible justification without claiming authorization, settlement, comparative benefit, or a verdict on the resulting person's life.

### Possession's address argument

[Possession](/wiki/Possession) argues that conduct bearing subordination, nullity, and extraction is categorically unavailable as justification to its target. A consequentialist can reject justification-as-address and treat possession as a grave but weighable burden. Even within the framework, the disposal and contest-channel tests remain defended interpretations, while jointness and the level rule are proposed.

**What would strengthen the position:** an argument for justification-as-address that does not rely on the diagnostic conclusion it is used to establish, together with evidence that the tests resist purpose-gerrymandering, manufactured exits, and controlled records.

### Precaution beyond established sentience

[Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) gives a defended threshold for precaution where sentience is not established. Whether expression and route exhaust the grounds, whether a reading remains live, and whether organizational readings remain live in artificial-mind cases are refusable judgments rather than resolved theory.

Its dischargeability rule is modal: a route must identify a parity-passing, candidate-specific finding about the organization or condition it invokes that would close it, but the finding need not be presently obtainable. This prevents practical opacity from defeating candidacy, including opacity an interested evidence-holder produced or preserved. The cost is that route-backed candidacy can remain unresolved indefinitely. A practical-discharge alternative would require a feasible path to the finding and thereby narrow candidacy, but can reward opacity by treating present inaccessibility as exclusionary. Neither rule makes precaution fixed or maximal.

**Cost of rejection:** rejecting the precautionary extension removes the threshold and conduct judgments that depend on it; the sentience criterion and standing of established someones remain. Rejecting only modal dischargeability leaves the extension in need of a different exit rule, with practical discharge available as the stated rival.

## Empirical and application dependencies

### Circulation's sufficiency

[Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) names normative requirements, structural safeguards, and failure conditions for institutional review. [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) leaves the evaluative cutoffs for accessible and outcome-changing review open. Once those cutoffs are fixed or made explicit in a case, whether safeguards satisfy them remains empirical. Collusion, diffusion, shared assumptions, inaccessible review, and powerless review can leave the formal design intact while defeating answerability.

**Required:** evidence that circulation works from burdened positions under an explicit practical-availability and effective-contest judgment. The political module depends on that performance rather than on the existence of a diagram or procedure.

### Sentience boundaries

[Someone](/wiki/Someone) identifies someones with sentient beings, but the onset of sentience in gradual biological development, its presence in unfamiliar animals or artificial systems, and the adequacy of proposed indicators remain empirical and conceptual questions. [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) and [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) therefore do not settle fetal status, while [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) remains conditional.

### Diffuse and collective participation

[Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) proposes a controlled-function bridge for distinguishing participation from remote benefit and ordinary causal contact. Direct operation, governance, commissioning, and earmarked finance usually expose the relevant route; [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) conditionally applies the bridge to repeated purchasing through an empirically established demand-and-replenishment mechanism. Neither step supplies a general attribution rule for one-off or de minimis acts, pooled or secondary-market investment, general taxation, bundled transactions, automated payments, or classes of contribution drawn so broadly that almost any economic activity could be included.

**Required:** empirical methods for tracing particular operating, revenue, and replenishment routes; a defensible account of when a collective mechanism may be attributed to a token or course of conduct; and a threshold for reasonably available knowledge where no independent monitoring duty exists. These questions affect classification and culpability. Alternatives and withdrawal burdens instead enter the exit and necessity analysis after participation has been classified.

### Proxy and stewardship independence

[Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) and the proxy discipline at [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) can disqualify interested certification; they cannot conjure a disinterested representative. Infants, some disabled parties, animals, future someones, and possible artificial someones expose the same dependence on institutions whose independence must be demonstrated rather than presumed.

### The dead and surviving relations

[Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) explains why a valid exercise performed while its holder lived need not lose force at death. Direct wrongs to the dead, duties of memory, and posthumous reputation remain unresolved where no performed exercise, promisee, or living claimant carries the relation.

### Relational obligation beyond settlement

[Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) and [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) distinguish gratitude, intrinsic grief, and legitimate attachment from repayment claims and punitive exit costs. They do not supply a general theory of fidelity, filial duty, trust, or obligations internal to love. Community-structured exit costs also leave responsibility difficult to place where an immediate relation preserves formal refusal but a surrounding institution makes departure devastating. Relational and Confucian accounts that ground filial obligation in lineage, ritual, or relation rather than in the [settlement](/wiki/Settlement) the framework denies remain an unperformed engagement.

## Principled indeterminacies

Three absences are consequences of identified commitments rather than debts awaiting completion.

- **Another's life-worth verdict** is barred by the reserved-verdict commitment at [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement). A critic can reject the commitment; the framework cannot supply the verdict while retaining it.
- **Closure of another's account** is barred by the settlement prohibition. Adjudication may close a question or an implementation, but not the holder's account.
- **A global legitimacy verdict for an arrangement as a whole** is displaced by claim-by-claim and function-by-function audit at [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability). A political theory requiring one status-level verdict asks this framework for work it deliberately declines.

## Rival framing and acknowledged costs

[The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) denies that beginnings belong to the vocabulary of warrant and account at all. The framework cannot refute that framing without presupposing the applicability in dispute. The same pressure appears in existential gratitude addressed to no benefactor: translating it as gladness without debt may preserve its practical boundary while losing part of what the speaker means. Whether the framing dispute can be adjudicated by shared reasons remains open.

The register and dependency system also carries a presentational cost. Accurate labels cannot prevent a defended or open claim from acquiring the cadence of a derivation, while modularity can either expose dependencies or insulate outer claims from pressure on the whole. [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) supplies disciplines for circulation, not a certification that the corpus has escaped those risks.

## Related pages

[Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) · [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) · [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) · [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Intellectual-Context.mdx

- Title: Intellectual Context
- Slug: Intellectual-Context
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Corpus orientation

````mdx
# Intellectual Context

## Summary

This page situates [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) among philosophical positions and traditions that help identify its commitments. It distinguishes acknowledged debts from structural comparison. A point of contact does not establish influence, equivalence, priority, or endorsement by the thinker named; [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) governs the framework's own claims, not the interpretation of external work.

The rebuilt theory is best located by its architecture: a second-personal conceptual core extended to every sentient party, a diagnostic theory of directed claim grounds and possession, and a proposed non-aggregative operational system. No single neighboring tradition supplies all three.

## Attribution boundary

Three kinds of relation appear below.

- **Acknowledged debt** reports a source or framework the corpus expressly credits.
- **Structural comparison** identifies a similarity or difference visible at the level of positions.
- **Rival or pressure** identifies a view that refuses a premise or exposes a cost.

Unless an entry is marked as an acknowledged debt, it makes no genealogical claim. This page is also not a substitute for a scholarly bibliography: its comparisons are orientation to the wiki's dependency structure, and claims about another writer's position should be checked against that writer's primary work.

## Acknowledged debts

**Force and conversion.** The source framework credits Simone Weil's analysis of force for the insight that a party can be converted into a thing through availability to another's purpose. [Possession](/wiki/Possession) reconstructs the diagnosis through subordination, nullity, and extraction; [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) extends attention to non-violent and procedural arrangements. Those reconstructions should not be attributed back to Weil.

**Opacity and legibility.** The administrative analysis borrows and narrows Édouard Glissant's right to opacity. Its specific claim is that standing cannot be made conditional on readability to an institution, not that every demand for information is defeated.

**Reproductive justice.** [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) expressly restates the reproductive-justice framework developed by Black feminist organizers and associated with Loretta Ross and the SisterSong collective: the rights to have children, not to have children, and to raise children in safe and dignified conditions. The Standing Framework's contribution is a reconstruction of why those claims form one jurisdictional structure; it does not claim the structure as its invention.

**Second-personal and contractualist tools.** The source framework names Stephen Darwall's second-personal ethics and T. M. Scanlon's contractualism as tools for thinking about answerability and justification to each. Borrowing those tools does not make the later standing extension, settlement prohibition, or operational system conclusions of either view.

## Conceptual neighbors

**Second-personal ethics.** Stephen Darwall's second-personal ethics supplies a clear comparison for claims addressed by and to parties. [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) extends such standing beyond beings capable of reciprocal address: a holder can be owed an account without being able to demand one linguistically or participate in reason-exchange.

**Contractualism.** The framework shares with T. M. Scanlon's contractualism a concern with justification to each affected party. Its distinct prohibition is [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement): availability of a justification is not acceptance, authorization, acquittal, or closure by the person to whom it is addressed. The wiki does not claim that contractualism proper commits the inference it blocks.

**Asymmetric responsibility and dependency.** Readers of Emmanuel Levinas may recognize obligation prior to reciprocity; readers of Hans Jonas, responsibility shaped by what agents bring into being; readers of Eva Kittay, the moral centrality of dependency that cannot be repaid in kind. The framework claims kinship of problem rather than lineage. Its distinctive work lies in claim grounds, demands and exercises, the means-bound, and the account that remains open.

**Wronging without comparative harm.** The beginnings line belongs near Seana Shiffrin's work on procreative responsibility and J. David Velleman's criticism of justifying creation by the created person's good. [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) does not require a worse-off comparison, while [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) adds a defended anti-bootstrapping premise. The page therefore shares a non-comparative problem space without reproducing either neighboring argument.

**Moral attention.** The framework presents, rather than derives, the foundation that a sentient being is a [someone](/wiki/Someone). That method is structurally near work associated with Cora Diamond and the moral attention enacted in J. M. Coetzee's *The Lives of Animals*: a proposed reorientation of what the reader sees before procedural inference begins. The comparison does not establish that those writers would accept the framework's foundation or method.

## Diagnostic and operational neighbors

**Republican contestability.** [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) is structurally near Philip Pettit's republican account of non-domination and contestability. The shared pressure is power that remains subject to effective challenge. The route differs: republican theory begins from freedom and domination, while this framework reconstructs authority from claim-protecting functions, holding relations, open accounts, and revisable adjudication.

**Non-aggregative rescue.** [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) occupies a contested region associated with Taurek-style objections to saving the greater number. Its defended counting rule rejects equal-chances lotteries among same-order claims, while its relevance band rejects unrestricted aggregation. The open cell records where that middle position lacks an exchange principle rather than treating either neighboring view as refuted.

**Truthfulness and rational agency.** [Deception and Captured Judgment](/wiki/Deception-and-Captured-Judgment) is near Kantian accounts, including Christine Korsgaard's work, that locate deception's wrong in the management of another's rational agency rather than in false assertion alone. The framework routes the wrong through captured judgment and possession, allowing the analysis to reach parties outside reciprocal rational practice.

**Abolitionist animal rights.** Gary Francione's abolitionist approach, developed in *Animals, Property, and the Law* and *Rain Without Thunder*, is a close structural neighbor to [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics). Both treat sentience rather than higher cognition as sufficient for moral inclusion and deny that improved welfare by itself answers the permissibility of institutional animal use. Their architectures diverge. Francione centers a basic right not to be property, treats veganism as a moral baseline, and rejects welfare-reform campaigns as a route to abolition. The Standing Framework treats legal property as evidence rather than criterion: possession requires subordination, nullity, and extraction at the same operative level; welfare remains owed without ratifying the structure; and individual withdrawal follows only through proposed participation and exit bridges together with empirical findings about conduct and alternatives. This is structural comparison, not acknowledged debt.

**Speaking for others.** [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) addresses the problem associated centrally with Linda Alcoff's work on speaking for others. It treats representation as a holding relation requiring evidential priority, corrigibility, conflict disclosure, and preserved routes, including where the represented party can never audit the speech.

## Rival and contrastive positions

**Natality and the gift view.** Hannah Arendt's concept of natality supplies the philosophical neighborhood for [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View), which treats birth as a new beginning rather than an event governed by prior warrant. The wiki's gift view is a constructed rival, not Arendt exegesis. Its strongest version denies that beginnings open an account at all.

**Harm-based antinatalism.** David Benatar's antinatalism is contrastive rather than a source for the framework's argument. The Standing Framework makes no claim that existence harms the person who exists, performs no existence/nonexistence comparison, and does not vary its conclusion with predicted life quality. Its disputed step concerns person-directed justification for origination.

**The procreative asymmetry.** The antinatalist application engages the asymmetry, associated with Jan Narveson's early formulation and later population-ethics discussion, according to which failing to create a happy life wrongs no one while creating a miserable life can wrong the person created. The framework grants that asymmetry but argues that it removes a person-directed reason to create rather than supplying a warrant.

**Welfarist animal ethics.** [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) treats welfare as relevant to claim content and implementation but insufficient to answer possession. A high-welfare arrangement can therefore remain wrong where all three possession marks are present; a sanctuary can fall outside the diagnosis even where dependence and legal ownership remain.

**Autonomy and disability critiques at the end of life.** [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics) converges with autonomy-centered accounts of decisional authority and with disability-rights criticism of external quality-of-life judgments. It joins the two through valid exercises, the reserved life-verdict, and bodily enforcement rules rather than by ranking the values against each other.

**Retributive punishment.** The framework can derive protection, constraint, censure, and repair without deriving desert. A retributive theory that treats culpability-proportional burden as indispensable does not merely fill a procedural detail; it supplies theory the framework currently lacks.

## Unperformed engagements

The most important acknowledged gap is engagement with relational and Confucian accounts of filial obligation. [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) defeats claims that a child owes repayment for being begun, but it does not answer obligations grounded in lineage, ritual, or relation rather than in the denied settlement. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) records the issue as missing engagement rather than a victory by default.

The comparison around [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) is also preliminary. Moral uncertainty, sentience indicators, the problem of other minds, and signal reliability are adjacent literatures; the wiki has not established that its expression-and-route threshold survives their strongest objections.

## Limits

- Structural proximity does not establish influence or convergence.
- The named comparisons locate modules, not the framework as a whole.
- This page does not supply a citation apparatus for claims about external traditions. Scholarly use requires primary-source verification beyond this orientation page.

## Related pages

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) · [Points of Entry](/wiki/Points-of-Entry) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Someone.mdx

- Title: Someone
- Slug: Someone
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: foundational
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: none

