````mdx
# Someone

## Summary

In [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics), a **someone** is any sentient being: any being for which there is something it is like to exist. Sentience is the sole entry condition. Intelligence, language, agency, usefulness, moral reciprocity, and the capacity to assert a claim may affect what a being is owed; none determines whether there is a party to be owed anything.

The foundational commitment is not only that experience matters. It is that every someone is a party, never a quantity: a being to whom obligations can be directed rather than a location in an impersonal total. [Standing](/wiki/Standing) names that position. [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) supplies the further relations required before one party holds a particular claim against another.

## Definition

A someone is a being with an experiential point of view: an inside from which its condition is undergone. The criterion asks whether experience is present, not what the being can do with it. Three substitutions are rejected:

- **Rationality.** Cognitive sophistication changes the possible dimensions and contents of claims, not entry into standing.
- **Reciprocity.** A being need not exchange reasons, accuse, release, or forgive in order to be owed anything.
- **Language.** Inability to report experience does not turn an experience into no one's experience.

The framework presents this identification rather than deriving it. A reader who finds no morally decisive party in the infant, the permanently non-verbal animal, or another sentient being has rejected the foundation, not missed a later inference.

## The anti-aggregation floor

Someones remain several. Experiences, benefits, burdens, and probabilities can be described and compared; adding those descriptions does not produce a further subject whose good is the total. There is no one for whom two beings' combined experience is a single experience.

This is the framework's **anti-aggregation floor**: an aggregate is not a claimant, and a favorable total is not by itself an answer to a party whose claim is left unsatisfied. The floor does not yet decide triage, rationing, or conflicts among claims. Those questions require claim identification and the later comparison discipline. What the foundation bars is replacing the parties with a quantity before those questions are asked.

## Why reciprocity is not the test

An infant can perform no exercise of standing, yet obligations toward it are complete. A permanently non-verbal animal may never call anyone to account, yet what is done to it still has a party. These cases separate the existence of an obligation from the holder's power to articulate or enforce it.

The general distinction is carried at [Standing](/wiki/Standing): demands can hold where exercises are unavailable. A someone's capacities determine what can be asked of it and which goods can form the content of its claims. They do not determine whether it is a someone.

## The uncertain edge

Sentience has no universally observable boundary. The framework therefore distinguishes two questions: whether a candidate is in fact a someone, and how agents should act under uncertainty about that fact. The foundational criterion answers only the first.

The conceptual core supplies no automatic caution rule. [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) gives a defended threshold for a precautionary extension, and [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) applies that extension to built systems. Those arguments must be accepted or refused on their own premises; uncertainty does not silently enlarge the foundation.

## Someone, standing, and claims

| Notion | Question | Dependency |
|---|---|---|
| Someone | Is there a sentient subject here? | foundational criterion |
| [Standing](/wiki/Standing) | What position follows from being a someone? | someone |
| [Claim ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) | Why does this party hold this claim against this addressee? | standing plus a relational ground |
| Claim content | What does fully answering that claim require? | holder's good, ground, and situation |

Equal standing does not imply identical claims. Every sentient being enters as a party; the experiential, agential, and relational shape of a life determines which goods and exercises are available within it.

## Limits

- The identification of someones with sentient beings is presented, not proved.
- The criterion presupposes that sentience is coherent enough to do this work; the framework does not answer skepticism about consciousness.
- The framework does not settle the [onset or presence of sentience](/wiki/Open-Questions) in gradual biological development or artificial systems.
- Direct obligations to beings who were once but are no longer sentient remain open at [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions); [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) gives the narrower account of exercises performed while a holder existed.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing.mdx

- Title: Standing
- Slug: Standing
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: foundational
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: Someone

````mdx
# Standing

## Summary

**Standing** is the position conferred by being a [someone](/wiki/Someone): the status of a party rather than a quantity. It is held equally by every sentient being, cannot be earned or forfeited, and does not vary with intelligence, usefulness, innocence, or the ability to assert it.

Standing states who can be owed. It does not by itself state who owes them, what is owed, or how competing claims should be decided. The relational formula *whatever affects a someone must answer to them* expresses the floor only when read with that limit; treated as a complete claim-generator, it would make everyone answerable to everyone. Directed claims require the individuating relations at [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds).

## Party rather than quantity

Standing requires that conduct be assessed with the affected someones still present as separate parties. An aggregate can describe outcomes but cannot receive an answer, because it has no point of view. The framework therefore refuses to let a total replace the parties whose goods produced it.

This is a floor, not a complete decision rule. Standing does not forbid every burden imposed for others, establish lexical priorities, or decide how several claims compare. It requires that any later justification remain directed to the actual holders and that no claimless total be treated as though it were itself owed something.

## Demands and exercises

Standing has two forms that ordinary moral language often merges.

**Demands** are what others can owe a holder independently of any act by that holder. A demand can bind where its holder cannot understand, state, or enforce it.

**Exercises** are acts only the holder can perform: consenting, refusing, promising, directing, waiving, releasing, and forgiving. A valid exercise requires an existing holder with the capacity and freedom to perform it. It cannot be supplied by another, presumed from silence, constructed counterfactually, or manufactured. [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) develops these validity conditions.

The load-bearing distinction is that **demands do not wait on exercises**. An infant's incapacity does not suspend claims held on the infant's behalf; an animal's inability to refuse does not become agreement. The absence of an exercise leaves the claim structure to be determined by the relevant grounds and [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good). It supplies no permission.

Performed exercises can change that structure. A valid consent, refusal, promise, release, or directive becomes a ground in its own right and can remain binding through later incapacity or death. The exercise ground and its limits are stated at [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds).

## Equal standing, unequal claims

Standing answers the threshold question: is there a party here? A claim answers a relational question: what is this holder owed, by this addressee, on this ground? Its content depends on [the holder's own good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good), the ground, and the situation.

A child and a cow can therefore have equal standing and profoundly different claims. The difference is not a rank between their lives. It follows from the dimensions each life has and the relations in which each stands. The same applies to any sentient artificial being: sentience would settle entry into standing while leaving most claim content to be established.

Two rules follow:

- Equal standing never entails identical treatment or interchangeable claims.
- Unequal claim content never reduces a holder's standing or turns the holder into a quantity.

## What standing does not establish

- It does not make mere causal effect a directed claim; [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) supplies the missing relation.
- It does not determine what counts as an [adequate justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) or resolve conflicts among claim holders.
- It yields no verdict on whether any life is worth living or continuing.
- It does not disqualify wrongdoers; [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) applies the same floor under conflict.

## Limits

- Standing inherits the unproved foundation at [Someone](/wiki/Someone).
- The demands/exercises distinction is source conceptual machinery. Particular conclusions drawn from it still require every additional premise to be stated.
- Direct claims of the dead remain unresolved. [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) explains why an exercise performed while its holder existed need not disappear with the holder.

## Related pages

[Someone](/wiki/Someone) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) · [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Answerability.mdx

- Title: Answerability
- Slug: Answerability
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: foundational
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: Standing

````mdx
# Answerability

## Summary

To be **answerable** to someone is to owe that party an [account](/wiki/Account) of conduct under a directed claim: to remain governed by what is owed to them, to preserve the conditions of assessment and response, and to leave their account unclosed. Answerability is distinct from [authorization](/wiki/Authorization). The first identifies a standard conduct must answer to; the second identifies a grantor whose performed permission changes what may be done.

Standing makes every someone eligible to hold claims. It does not make every agent answerable for every effect. [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) identifies the relation that directs a claim to an addressee; answerability describes the form the resulting obligation takes.

## A directed relation

Three forms of appraisal remain distinct:

1. **Impersonal appraisal** rates a state or act without identifying a party to whom anything is owed.
2. **Party-relative assessment** describes how a state or act bears on a particular someone.
3. **Answerability** identifies an obligation owed by an addressee to a holder on a ground.

Only the third is a directed relation. Mere affectedness can supply evidence for an imposition but cannot finish the claim roster: remote causal contribution, another party's free exercise, ordinary competition, and an arrangement's holding power differ in who owes what and why. The grounds discipline prevents the phrase *must answer to* from dissolving directedness.

Where answerability exists, it is keyed to [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) rather than the addressee's intentions. It begins in conduct before it becomes speech: care, truthfulness, preservation of options, records, response, and correction as the ground requires. Capacity to answer back changes the available performance, not the existence of the relation.

## Standard and grantor

Answerability and authorization do different work:

| Relation | The other party is | Constitutive question |
|---|---|---|
| Answerability | the holder of a claim and standard an account must meet | Is a person-directed justification available? |
| [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) | the grantor whose valid exercise changes the claim structure | Did the holder actually perform the grant? |

A standard can be applied to conduct whose addressee did not authorize it. A grant cannot exist before its grantor or be produced afterward by prediction. The unavailability of authorization therefore neither erases answerability nor proves the conduct unjustified. It removes one possible warrant and leaves the standard to be met by whatever claims and justifications actually govern.

The source criterion is **justifiability to each holder of an unsatisfied claim**. It requires availability, not prior permission or eventual acceptance. The conceptual core supplies that separation but not a complete test. [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) now proposes and defends the diagnostic conditions; its comparative condition remains incomplete until the operational comparison module is rebuilt.

## Three activities

Answerability can involve three activities with different preconditions:

1. **Answering in conduct:** acting under the holder's claim and preserving what the ground requires. This is possible toward a holder who cannot receive reasons.
2. **Giving and receiving reasons:** performing the explanatory part of an account where exchange is possible.
3. **Release or closure by the holder:** a valid exercise that changes what remains owed.

The third is not the prohibited act of [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement). A holder may release, waive, forgive, or settle a dispute within the scope of a valid exercise. Settlement in the framework's technical sense is closure entered by another in the holder's name, in advance or without the holder's exercise, and in the closer's favor.

## Judgment and jurisdiction

A **judgment** remains answerable to the one it judges: its reasons can be contested, its effects remain claims-bearing, and its maker must revise it if the account fails. A **jurisdiction** installs the judgment as a standard the target must answer to while the judging party is no longer answerable in return.

The distinction diagnoses informal as well as legal relations. Advice, criticism, classification, and moral advocacy become jurisdictional when challenge cannot move the party or arrangement imposing them. The distinction does not itself decide which standards may be enforced; that requires the later enforcement theory.

## Limits

- Answerability has normative force only because the framework accepts the standing floor and the relevant claim ground.
- This page does not establish that every affected party holds a claim against every causal contributor.
- Availability of justification is not self-certification by the actor and not a veto held by the addressee; [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) states its conditions and remaining gaps.
- The judgment/jurisdiction distinction identifies a structural risk but supplies no complete adjudication procedure.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Deception and Captured Judgment](/wiki/Deception-and-Captured-Judgment)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Authorization.mdx

- Title: Authorization
- Slug: Authorization
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: derived
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: Standing

````mdx
# Authorization

## Summary

To be **authorized** by someone is to hold permission produced by that holder's valid exercise. Authorization changes the claim structure because the holder has actually performed a grant; it is not a prediction that they would grant, a description of their good, or an approval supplied in their name by another.

Authorization is distinct from [answerability](/wiki/Answerability). A grantor must exist and perform before or during the authorized conduct. A standard of answerability can govern conduct never authorized by its holder. The difference is why missing consent cannot be repaired by hypothetical, tacit, retroactive, or manufactured agreement.

## Valid performed exercises

Authorization is one exercise of standing among consent, refusal, promise, directive, release, waiver, and forgiveness. A valid exercise requires:

- **Existence:** the holder exists when the exercise is performed.
- **Capacity:** the holder can understand and perform the exercise in question.
- **Freedom:** coercion or an engineered inability to refuse does not produce a grant.
- **Non-manufacture:** the addressee has not built or captured the standpoint whose declaration it invokes.

Validity is indexed to performance. Later incapacity or death prevents new exercises but does not unperform a valid earlier one. [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) governs the priority and scope of present and prior exercises; [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) develops the narrower posthumous result. The exercise ground at [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) explains how performed exercises reshape later claims.

Authorization is one possible warrant, not the exhaustive account of permission. Showing that no authorization exists leaves open whether another [justification is adequate](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) and whether the act is justified. It also leaves open the holder's later claim to an account.

## Counterfeit grants

Four recurring devices resemble authorization without containing a performed grant:

- **Tacit consent:** remaining counts as agreement even where exit was not live at reasonable cost.
- **Hypothetical consent:** a prediction that the holder would have agreed is treated as the agreement.
- **Retroactive consent:** later approval is made to authorize an earlier act rather than alter the relation from the time of approval.
- **Manufactured consent:** an arrangement invokes an endorsement it helped produce by shaping the holder's available standpoint or terms of judgment.

Participation, elections, flourishing, silence, and continued relationship can all be evidence relevant to other claims. None becomes authorization unless a capable and free holder actually performs the grant at issue.

## Stewardship is not authorization by proxy

Where a child, ward, unconscious patient, or other holder cannot exercise, another party may sometimes act for the holder's good. The framework classifies this as **stewardship**, not as the holder's authorization. No consent is imputed and no exercise is performed in the holder's name.

Stewardship operates under claims already directed to the guardian, clinician, or holder of power. [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) supplies the evidence, beneficiary, and contest disciplines for describing what those claims require; [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) gives priority to the holder's own valid exercises when they are available. Stewardship can justify intervention without manufacturing a grant, and it can fail without violating a refusal that was never performed.

This correction matters at beginnings. No proxy authorizes a beginning for the one begun. The positive duties of initiators arise from the [initiation ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds), not from consent given on behalf of a nonexistent grantor.

## Revocation and continuing performance

A valid exercise can create reliance and repair claims, but no exercise settles every later question in advance. Where carrying out an exercise requires the holder's continuing bodily performance, the exercise remains revocable as to specific performance while that condition continues. This result is derived at [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) given the bridge that compelled bodily continuation converts the holder into material; revocation's costs can sound in repair, never compulsion.

## Limits

- The validity conditions are conceptual constraints on an exercise, not a complete theory of capacity or coercion.
- Authorization does not establish the [adequacy](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) of conduct toward third parties whose claims the grantor cannot waive.
- Capacity, coercion, and the point at which the holder's own exercise displaces stewardship remain incomplete; [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) records that boundary.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) · [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Settlement.mdx

- Title: Settlement
- Slug: Settlement
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: foundational, derived
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: Standing, Authorization

````mdx
# Settlement

## Summary

**Settlement**, in the framework's technical sense, is closure entered in another's name: a reckoning fixed without that holder's valid exercise, in advance or beyond its scope, in the closer's favor, and later usable as credit, permission, moral acquittal, or moral finality. The settlement prohibition protects the difference between offering an answer and claiming the addressee's verdict.

The paradigm result is that no beginning can be settled in the name of the one begun. Before the beginning there is no holder who could release, waive, forgive, or authorize; afterward the person holds standing and any valid exercise is theirs. This establishes a limit on what initiators can claim, not a verdict that every beginning is wrongful.

## The prohibited closure

Four features jointly identify Settlement:

1. **Another's name:** the closer claims to dispose of a matter belonging to a different holder.
2. **No governing exercise:** the holder performed no valid release, waiver, forgiveness, or authorization covering the closure.
3. **The closer's favor:** the claimed finality protects the party who acted, benefited, governed, or imposed.
4. **Closure of the account:** later challenge is treated as already answered, ungrateful, disloyal, procedurally exhausted, or otherwise without standing.

Finality alone is not Settlement. Existing parties can resolve disputes; holders can perform releases; institutions can close questions of action for coordination while preserving review and the account. The later institutional theory distinguishes adjudication from Settlement. The wrong here is crossing from a decision about action into another party's moral closure.

## The argument at a beginning

1. A release, waiver, authorization, or verdict claimed on behalf of the person begun would have to be that person's exercise.
2. Under [Newness](/wiki/Newness), no such holder exists before the beginning.
3. Under [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization), an unavailable exercise cannot be supplied by prediction, proxy attribution, silence, or later approval.
4. Once the person exists, their exercises are theirs and the initiator is answerable under the [initiation ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds).
5. Therefore the initiator cannot enter a completed reckoning in the person's name or use the beginning itself as credit against later claims.

The argument does not depend on ignorance or on a negative welfare judgment. Perfect prediction of a good life would still not be the person's performed release or verdict. Nor does the conclusion make authorization a precondition of beginning; it denies only that missing authorization can be converted into a grant or a closed account.

## Credit, grievance, and gratitude

**Maker's credit.** The claim *your existence puts you in my debt* invokes a settlement that never occurred. Initiation creates claims running toward the person who must carry the condition; it creates no reciprocal claim founded on the initiation itself. Obligations can still arise later from promises, reliance, care, and shared relations on their own grounds.

**Created person's grievance.** No merely possible person held a prior claim against being created. Once someone exists, however, the initiation ground directs claims to those who knowingly began or deliberately assumed the condition. The grievance therefore need not be translated into a pre-existence right or a comparative harm in order to identify an account owed now.

**Gratitude.** Gratitude freely performed can alter a relationship but cannot be collected as repayment for the beginning. Treating approval, flourishing, or affection as retroactive permission converts a later response into a counterfeit grant and the gift into credit.

## Reserved verdict

No party's deliberation may contain, as premise or conclusion, that another's life is not worth living or continuing. The prohibition is broader than uncertainty: the life-verdict is reserved against external use. Claims about pain, agency, continuation, treatment, and implementation remain available without installing that verdict.

This reservation does not prevent a holder from exercising authority over matters within their own life, or prevent others from describing concrete claims and burdens. It prevents an external verdict about the life as a whole from doing justificatory work.

## Limits

- Settlement establishes what cannot be claimed in another's name; it does not decide whether the underlying act was justified.
- It does not erase genuine exercises, ordinary reciprocity, reconciliation, or obligations grounded in relations that developed after a beginning.
- Traditions that ground filial obligation in relation, lineage, ritual, or another source rather than the denied settlement are not answered by this argument.
- The distinction between legitimate institutional finality and Settlement requires the later authority and adjudication module.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) · [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) · [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Account.mdx

- Title: Account
- Slug: Account
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: derived
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: Answerability, Settlement

````mdx
# Account

## Summary

An **account** is the open performance of [answerability](/wiki/Answerability): conduct, reasons, records, acknowledgment, response, correction, and contest through which an addressee remains answerable to the holder of a directed claim. It is owed because a [claim ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) relates this holder to this addressee, not because every effect generates a universal duty to explain.

An account is neither [authorization](/wiki/Authorization) nor [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement). It does not supply prior permission, and the party who owes it cannot convert its availability or performance into the holder's release, acceptance, or acquittal. Performing an account can satisfy the duties of account, and reasons can justify conduct; neither fact by itself certifies the holder's verdict or erases the residue of a claim that remains unsatisfied.

## Form

Five features mark an account.

**Address.** It is owed to the claim holder, not merely produced about them or delivered to a supervisor, audience, court, or public.

**Conduct before speech.** Due care, truthfulness, preservation of options, response capacity, and protection of later assessment can be parts of the account before reasons are exchanged. What is required depends on the claim's ground and content.

**Record.** Where later review is possible or the affected holder cannot presently contest, preserving evidence can be part of what is owed. Concealment can defeat an account even where the actor could state reasons in the abstract.

**Contest.** An account remains exposed to challenge through a route capable of changing conduct, interpretation, or remedy. A statement made to an audience controlled by its author is not answerability merely because it is public.

**Non-closure.** The addressee cannot certify the holder's acceptance. Reasons may justify conduct without dissolving an unsatisfied claim or claiming that the matter is settled for its holder.

## Ground and content

The account is a form, not an independent ground of obligation. [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) determines why an account is owed and supplies its initial content. An initiator may owe care and truthful history; a holder of power may owe exit, contest, and welfare limits; the recipient of a performed exercise may owe compliance within its scope; a wrongdoer may owe repair.

Different grounds can address the same party at once. Their account duties accumulate unless one claim validly changes another. A generic explanation cannot substitute for this ground-specific structure: *we considered everyone* does not say which claim was recognized, what it required, or why it remained unsatisfied.

## What an account is not

- **Not a grant:** authorization requires the holder's performed exercise.
- **Not acceptance:** the holder need not endorse the reasons for them to be assessable.
- **Not acquittal:** [adequate reasons](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) do not erase [residue](/wiki/Residue) or prohibit later contest.
- **Not a procedure:** records and review can perform answerability, but compliance with a checklist cannot replace the holder.
- **Not a self-account:** a narrative of the actor's virtue, sacrifice, or purity answers nothing unless it remains directed to the claim at issue.

## Limits

- [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) distinguishes a justification's availability from the performance of the account duties defined here.
- The account duties attached to responsiveness and institutional holding extend the source concept through the reconstructed [claim grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds); those extensions retain the registers stated there.
- Direct accounts to the dead remain [unresolved](/wiki/Open-Questions) where no performed exercise or living claimant supplies the relation.

## Related pages

[Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Newness.mdx

- Title: Newness
- Slug: Newness
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Conceptual core
- Layer: conceptual-core
- Support: derived
- Provenance: source-framework
- Depends on: Someone, Authorization, Settlement

````mdx
# Newness

## Summary

**Newness** is the structural fact that, before an act brings a someone into existence, that someone does not exist. There is no prior holder whose permission could be sought, whose claim to creation could be satisfied, or in whose name the beginning could be closed. Once sentience is present, the being has full standing; nothing about the earlier absence weakens the later party.

Newness establishes a limit, not a positive claim ground. The positive undertaking arises under [initiation](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) if and when a someone exists. The distinction prevents two contrary errors: treating prior nonexistence as permission, and treating the absence of prior authorization as a violated exercise.

## The structural fact

A beginning cannot place its addressee on both sides of the act. No increase in foresight, communication, or benevolence can make the resulting holder exist earlier as a grantor or claimant. This is structural rather than practical.

Other acts can form a standpoint that later assesses them: education, governance, and construction of artificial minds all do so. Procreation is the limiting case because the standpoint does not pre-exist the act at all. [Mixed Intergenerational Cases](/wiki/Mixed-Intergenerational-Cases) treats acts that both shape future conditions and affect which holder will later exist.

## What newness rules out

**Prior authorization.** [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) requires an existing grantor who performs an exercise. A later person could not have authorized their beginning beforehand.

**Prior claims.** A merely possible someone holds no claim to be created, no claim against not being created, and no grievance or debt. The claim roster changes when a someone exists; it is not backdated to possibility.

**Advance settlement.** [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) cannot be entered in the initiator's favor on behalf of a holder who does not yet exist. Later approval cannot be converted into a performed earlier release.

These exclusions do not establish that authorization was required, that the beginning was wrongful, or that no justification could be adequate. They remove counterfeit grants and claims from the analysis.

## Benefit and comparison

Newness blocks a same-person comparative claim that creation improved an already existing individual from a prior condition. There was no earlier condition of that individual. It does not prove that existence contains no goods, settle every non-comparative theory of benefit, or determine whether expected goods can contribute to justification.

The narrower result is enough to block debt founded on comparative rescue from nonexistence. The act did not move a holder from a worse state into a better one and cannot be claimed against them as though it did. Other accounts of benefit require their own premises.

## Transition into claims

Conduct can occur before the holder exists and still ground claims once the holder does. Under the [initiation ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds), knowingly beginning a condition another later must carry creates a directed undertaking when the party exists. The claim is not held in advance by a possible person; it arises in the relation between an actual holder and those who initiated or deliberately assumed the condition.

[Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) develops this beginnings application. It does not add a second bedrock premise: its positive claim is derived given the initiation ground, while Newness supplies the inherited asymmetry that no prior holder stood on the other side.

## Merely possible someones

- A policy that prevents a possible life wrongs no merely possible person by depriving them of existence. Claims of existing parties can still govern the policy.
- A failed beginning before any someone exists opens no account to a new holder, while grief and other claims of existing parties remain fully real.
- The framework does not infer where sentience begins. That empirical and conceptual boundary remains open.

## Limits

- Newness supplies no verdict on whether beginnings should occur.
- It does not decide non-comparative benefit or impersonal value.
- It does not determine the onset of sentience in pregnancy and therefore does not settle reproductive jurisdiction.
- Claims concerning future someones who will exist regardless of a present option require separate institutional and risk analysis.

## Related pages

[Someone](/wiki/Someone) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Mixed Intergenerational Cases](/wiki/Mixed-Intergenerational-Cases) · [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/The-Holders-Good.mdx

- Title: The Holder's Good
- Slug: The-Holders-Good
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: foundational, proposed, empirical
- Provenance: source-framework, reconstruction, clarification, completion
- Depends on: Standing, Authorization, Settlement

````mdx
# The Holder's Good

## Summary

**The holder's good** is the working account by which [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) fixes the content and gravity of a particular [someone's](/wiki/Someone) claims. It is not a complete theory of flourishing and does not rank lives. The proposed account distinguishes experiential good in felt well-being, agential good in control and an uncaptured standpoint, and relational-biographical good in attachments, projects, truthful history, and an open future. These dimensions can diverge and apply only where the holder's life has the corresponding shape.

The account is deliberately holder-specific. A generic benefit, institutional purpose, or favorable total cannot replace the good of the party whose claim is being identified. Where the holder can exercise authority, that exercise governs what it addresses; where the holder cannot contest the description, proxy judgment is stewardship under evidential and institutional constraints. Neither the working account nor a proxy description may become an external verdict on whether the holder's life is worth living or continuing.

Those proxy constraints are necessary screens, not proof of independence or accuracy; both remain empirical questions about evidence, incentives, control, and outcome-changing review.

## Dimensions of good

The proposed working account recognizes three dimensions, present where the holder's life has the corresponding shape.

**Experiential good** concerns felt well-being and ill-being. It belongs to every someone because sentience is the framework's threshold for being a party.

**Agential good** concerns control over one's life and body and the preservation of an uncaptured evaluative standpoint. It applies where the holder has agency of the relevant kind; it is not inferred merely from species membership.

**Relational-biographical good** concerns attachments, projects, truthful history, and an open future. It applies wherever a life has that narrative and social shape. Whether and how it applies is empirical, and the category is not a human monopoly.

The dimensions can diverge. An intervention may relieve distress while closing an agential option, or preserve a prior project while burdening present experience. Naming the dimensions prevents one benefit from silently standing in for the whole of the holder's good.

## Centrality

The default measure of an interest's centrality is **foreclosure**: an interest is central to the degree that setting it back closes the holder's other interests and activities. Foreclosure is a measure of position within a life, not a license for another party to decide what that life is worth.

The holder's own valid exercises govern what they address. A performed refusal, consent, or directive is not merely evidence of the holder's good; within its content and scope, it changes the claim structure. Settled cares and the shape of a life become evidence where no valid exercise speaks. [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) states the priority rules.

Kind-typical evidence enters only where the holder's own authority and individual history are unavailable. It supplies a defeasible account of likely interests, not permission to reduce an individual to a type.

## Gravity

The gravity of leaving a claim unsatisfied depends on several considerations:

- **centrality:** how much of the holder's remaining good the setback forecloses;
- **irreversibility:** whether the setback forecloses later repair or answering;
- **duration:** how long the burden remains;
- **probability:** where the claim concerns risk rather than a materialized burden;
- **subordination-degree:** how closely the burden approaches [possession](/wiki/Possession);
- **cumulative position:** whether the same or allied arrangements have repeatedly routed grave unsatisfied claims to this holder.

The cumulative factor is a diagnostic commitment: repeated assignment of burdens to the same parties is evidence that they are being treated as supply. Gravity remains ordinal, coarse, and sometimes incomplete. These considerations do not produce a common unit or guarantee that every pair of claims can be ranked.

The same factors structure [practical-availability and effective-contest inquiries](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest), especially centrality, irreversibility, duration, and cumulative position. They do not fix the point at which an exit cost makes refusal practically inert or an institutional response becomes material enough to count as effective contest.

## The life-verdict firewall

[Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) supplies a fixed limit on this account. No deliberation may use, as premise or conclusion, that another party's life is not worth living or continuing. Claims within a life, including claims held by the same person at different times, remain comparable. A verdict on the worth of the life as a whole does not.

The firewall blocks a familiar misuse of proxy judgment. Evidence that a holder is suffering can identify an experiential claim and require response; it cannot authorize an outside party to convert that evidence into the verdict that the holder would be better off nonexistent or dead.

## Proxy discipline

Where a holder cannot contest descriptions of their good, description is stewardship rather than [authorization](/wiki/Authorization). It is governed by three conditions:

- **Evidence-constrained:** behavior, physiology, individual history, and kind-typical patterns may inform the description; institutional convenience and the proxy's preferred outcome may not.
- **Beneficiary-barred:** a party whose costs fall if the holder's good is described one way is disqualified from certifying that description. This bar is a proposed safeguard, not a derived result.
- **Independently contestable:** the description must remain open to review through a route the describing party does not control.

Where every available describer is interested, the description remains contested. The least-foreclosing course is the default, and independent review is required to the extent institutions can actually provide it. [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) applies this discipline to representation.

## Limits

- The three dimensions are a proposed diagnostic account, not a complete theory of value or a ranking of lives.
- Centrality and gravity do not yet supply the framework's comparison discipline. Incommensurable or closely balanced claims can remain unresolved.
- The beneficiary bar and least-foreclosing default are proposed safeguards. Their institutional independence and effectiveness are empirical questions.
- Capacity, coercion, and authority across changing conditions require the separate priority rules at [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time).

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Possession.mdx

- Title: Possession
- Slug: Possession
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: defended, proposed, open
- Provenance: source-framework, reconstruction, clarification
- Depends on: Standing, Answerability, Account, The-Holders-Good

````mdx
# Possession

## Summary

An act or arrangement **possesses** a [someone](/wiki/Someone) when, toward that party, it bears three marks together: the party's central interests are subordinated to a constitutive purpose, no effective channel can stop or alter the use for the party's sake, and benefits are secured through the party's subordinated condition. Possession is therefore a structure of disposal, nullity, and extraction rather than a synonym for ownership, force, dependence, harm, or administration.

The marks reconstruct the wrong tracked across the source framework's debtor, audience, supply, and captured-judgment forms. The disposal and contest-channel tests are defended interpretations; requiring all three marks and applying them at each operative level are proposed rules. One or two marks can still identify grave burdens without establishing possession.

Applying nullity is partly empirical and partly evaluative: evidence identifies exit costs and outcome-changing power, while the shared holder-relative analysis at [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) preserves the open cutoffs. Failure of nullity defeats the possession classification, not every other claim against the arrangement.

## The three marks

### Subordination: the disposal test

The party's central interests cannot, within the arrangement's own operation, defeat its constitutive purpose when the two collide. Welfare concessions do not by themselves defeat this mark. Comfort can limit *how* a use proceeds while the enterprise still prevents [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) from limiting *whether* it proceeds.

Purpose is read from operative decision rules and collision outcomes: what actually wins when central interests conflict with the enterprise's end across the standing pattern. Mission statements and local intentions cannot certify the structure, and one collision in either direction does not establish its standing rule.

### Nullity of standing: the contest-channel test

Nothing in the arrangement can stop or alter the use for the party's sake. Where the party can refuse, nullity appears when refusal is foreclosed or practically inert. Where the party cannot perform refusal because of infancy, incapacity, species, or form of life, nullity appears when no empowered substitute channel can halt the use and no review is keyed to the party's good rather than the use's efficiency.

The test is symmetric across articulacy. An arrangement does not escape the mark by selecting parties incapable of performing the refusal it would otherwise have to suppress.

Whether a route is live does not follow from its formal existence or from facts alone. Costs, access, timing, and collision history are empirical; [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) states the holder-relative inquiry and leaves open when those facts make refusal inert or a change too immaterial to count. Those questions concern the holder's practical relation to the route, not interpersonal comparison among claims.

### Extraction

Benefits are secured *through* the party's subordinated condition: body, labor, attention, esteem, attachment, or belief functions as a means rather than as a side effect of an independently achievable aim. Extraction identifies what the structure runs on.

## Level, time, and reform

Classification must name its level and assess the decision rules residing there. A system can possess while a local actor inside it does not; a local practice can possess inside a system whose wider rules do not. The proposed anti-gerrymander rule attaches the diagnosis at every level whose own operative rules bear the marks. An arrangement cannot escape by pointing upward or downward to a level where they are absent.

Possession is also a present-tense classification. The marks are assessed from operative rules now in force, evidenced by the recent pattern of real collisions. A history of possession does not make an arrangement possessive forever, and a declaration of reform does not change its status before new rules survive costly collisions.

Three statuses therefore remain distinct:

- **current structural status:** whether the marks operate now;
- **transition status:** whether [exit from a wrongful structure](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) remains incomplete;
- **historical wrong and residue:** what [remains owed](/wiki/Residue) because of earlier possession.

A reformed institution can cease possessing while still owing repair, correction, and transition. Duration affects residue and remedy, not whether the three marks are present.

## Four currencies

The source framework's earlier taxonomy identifies four recurrent currencies in which the same structure can operate. They remain useful diagnostics, but a case is classified as possession only where the three marks assemble.

**The debtor.** An unchosen benefit or beginning is held as credit, and the party's life or loyalty becomes payment. [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) and [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) identify the closure by which the claimant enters the account in their own favor.

**The audience.** The party's recognition, attachment, or story becomes support for another's self-account: the child as evidence of parental generosity, the beneficiary as testimony to the benefactor. Extraction operates through esteem and narrative rather than through a bill.

**The supply.** Body, labor, care, attention, or continued presence is arranged as material for an end that does not answer to the party. [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use) and [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) develop this currency.

**Captured judgment.** The party's evaluative standpoint is shaped so that it cannot freely assess the use being made of it. Concealment and manufacture supply nullity from inside the party's own vocabulary. [Deception and Captured Judgment](/wiki/Deception-and-Captured-Judgment) develops the form.

The currencies can compound. A built mind may be supply whose endorsement is manufactured; a child treated as debtor may also be made audience. The list organizes manifestations and does not replace the structural test.

## Neighboring burdens

- **Coercion** can produce episodic nullity without extraction or a standing disposal rule. It falls under [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) unless the other marks assemble.
- **Dependence** does not by itself establish subordination or nullity.
- **Hard use with live exit and empowered voice** may involve extraction without possession.
- **Harm as side effect** lacks extraction where the aim is achievable without the burdened party's subordinated condition.
- **Legal title** can evidence a disposal rule but is neither necessary nor sufficient. Its operative use matters.
- **Administration** can classify and coordinate without possession where standing remains effective within the arrangement.

These distinctions prevent the category from expanding until every burden, asymmetry, or institutional relation counts as possession.

## The address argument

[Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) makes justification directed: what is said to a claim holder must address that holder as a party. An act bearing all three marks denies that position in operation. The party's central interests cannot defeat the purpose, no channel can stop the use for their sake, and their condition is the instrument through which the benefit is secured.

On that defended interpretation of address, no person-directed justification for possession is available to its target. A purported justification is not an address that happens to be unpersuasive; it is an account *about* the party while the act denies the party the position of addressee. [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) therefore incorporates party-preservation as one of its conditions.

The argument does not by itself exclude possession from deliberation where others claim rescue or protection. That second step comes from the defended [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound): no claim includes another party's conversion. Rejecting the means-bound leaves possession categorically unjustifiable to its target while reopening whether the claims of others can nevertheless force it into the option set.

Catastrophe exposes the remaining dispute. The framework answers endangered parties pairwise: each claim remains bounded by the same prohibition on another's conversion. An opponent may accept separate claims and still argue that their joint presence changes the status of the means. Whether deliberative status is exhausted pairwise remains open.

## Constraint and reform

[Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) states the defended conditions under which restraint can remain danger-keyed, least-subordinating, terminating, welfare-bound, and answerable. Constraint becomes possession when the three marks assemble. Fault can change the ground and residue; it cannot remove standing or make possession self-justifying.

The corresponding positive discipline is [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession). Structural reform requires more than humane administration: the party's good must sometimes defeat the old purpose, effective contest must sometimes halt or alter the use, and the arrangement must cease securing its benefits through the subordinated condition.

## Limits

- The marks reconstruct source diagnostics; the disposal and contest-channel tests remain defended interpretations.
- Jointness, level classification, and the present-tense reform rule are proposed. Rejecting them returns the classification problem rather than preserving the same verdict by implication.
- The address argument depends on a defended conception of person-directed justification. A consequentialist who treats outcomes as sufficient justification rejects its major premise.
- The scale-invariance of the means-bound remains [disputed](/wiki/Open-Questions) where many claims jointly press for possessive means.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) · [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) · [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use) · [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Means-Bound.mdx

- Title: Means-Bound
- Slug: Means-Bound
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: defended, open
- Provenance: generalization, clarification
- Depends on: Standing, Possession

````mdx
# Means-Bound

## Summary

The **means-bound** is the defended principle that no claim, whatever its ground, contains another party's conversion. What a holder is owed is performance within party-preserving means. A parent's duty to a child, an institution's duty to those it governs, and a rescuer's duty to someone in peril can intensify what the addressee must do; none annexes a third party as material for satisfying it.

The principle operates at Stage 2 by fixing claim content. Whether a proposed means is party-preserving requires separate analysis, including the [possession](/wiki/Possession) test; the means-bound alone does not classify the option.

The means-bound is not derived from [Standing](/wiki/Standing) or from the existence of directed claims. It is the point at which the theory's agent-centered restriction enters. Its support is the framework's anti-possession character, which it generalizes rather than proves.

The means-bound alone does not make exclusion invariant under scale. That conclusion also requires **pairwise exhaustion**, the disputed premise that an option's deliberative status is exhausted by what can be justified to each party separately. The canonical theory declines a catastrophe amendment but leaves pairwise exhaustion open rather than treating joint claims as already unable to change the option set.

## Content

For claim holder P, addressee A, and third party T, the means-bound says that P's claim against A cannot include T's conversion into owned, owed, spent, subordinated, or otherwise available material. If A cannot satisfy P within party-preserving means, that failure can be a tragedy for P without making T's conversion something P was owed.

The bound applies across grounds. Rescue does not include harvesting another body; an undertaking to a child does not include consuming outsiders for the child's good; holding office does not authorize making officials or subjects into supply; a promise cannot confer authority over a party who did not perform it.

The principle limits claim content before comparison. It is not a late judgment that conversion is outweighed by other considerations. On the canonical position, the endangered holder's claim never contained that means.

## Why the framework defends it

The framework's central objection to possession is that a someone is treated as available for a purpose that does not answer to them. If another holder's need could make non-conversion a resource distributable by an addressee, the anti-possession floor would disappear exactly where the purpose was most urgent.

This supports the means-bound from within the framework but does not independently derive it from the concept of a claim. A reader can accept directed obligation while holding that some claims, especially special relational duties or sufficiently numerous rescue claims, alter the status of otherwise prohibited means. That is a coherent rival and not a misunderstanding.

## Special relations

Special relations can increase the cost, effort, risk, duration, and priority owed by the party inside them. They can also make failures culpable that would be supererogatory outside the relation. The means-bound denies only one route of intensification: expanding what is owed by converting someone who is not a party to that duty into its means.

An agent who breaches the bound under anguish or duress may have an excuse. Excuse concerns the agent; it does not turn the converted party's treatment into a justified answer to them.

## Scale and the open dispute

The means-bound alone does not establish that the status of a prohibited means is invariant under scale. That stronger conclusion also needs **pairwise exhaustion**: the premise that the deliberative status of an option is exhausted by what can be justified to each party separately. An opponent can preserve the several claims of many endangered someones while arguing that their joint presence changes the option set.

The canonical theory declines that amendment, but it has not proved pairwise exhaustion. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) therefore carries two distinct disputes: whether claim content can ever include another's conversion, and whether the joint presence of claims can alter deliberative status even when no single claim does.

## Limits

- The means-bound is defended, not derived. Arguments that depend on it must state the dependency.
- It does not determine which means are party-preserving; that requires the reconstructed possession tests.
- It does not deny that duties can be grave, costly, or tragic when party-preserving performance is impossible.
- Scale-invariance requires the further pairwise-exhaustion premise and remains [open](/wiki/Open-Questions).

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) · [Conflicts Among Standing Parties](/wiki/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Claim-Grounds.mdx

- Title: Claim Grounds
- Slug: Claim-Grounds
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: foundational, derived, defended, proposed, open
- Provenance: source-framework, reconstruction, generalization, clarification, completion
- Depends on: Standing, Answerability, Authorization, Account, Means-Bound, The-Holders-Good

````mdx
# Claim Grounds

## Summary

A **claim ground** is the relation that makes a particular [someone](/wiki/Someone) a claim holder against a particular addressee. [Standing](/wiki/Standing) establishes that every someone can be owed; a ground identifies who owes what to whom. Without this second step, the formula *whatever affects a someone must answer to them* would expand causal contact into universal liability and directedness would disappear.

The reconstructed roster has six grounds. **Imposition** concerns controlled or contributed impacts another cannot reasonably avoid and that do not consist solely in other parties' unowed exercises. **Initiation** concerns knowingly beginning, or deliberately assuming responsibility for, a condition another must carry. **Holding** concerns effective power exercised through a governing, custodial, employment, confinement, keeping, or classificatory relation, not mere situational ability to affect another. **Exercise** records how a holder's valid performance changes claims. **Responsiveness** identifies what an unsatisfied claim leaves owed afterward. **Need** concerns urgent rescue by a uniquely or saliently positioned addressee within a sacrifice cap.

One relation may instantiate several grounds; the claims are identified separately, and their contents accumulate unless a valid exercise or another rule changes them. The grounds have mixed support and are not proved exhaustive. Identifying a ground fixes directedness and initial claim content; it does not rank conflicting claims, establish adequate implementation, or authorize enforcement.

## Ground before content

Claim identification asks four questions in order: who is the holder, who is the addressee, what relation grounds the claim, and what that ground requires in this situation. A grave interest without an individuating relation may show that something bad is happening while leaving no directed claim against a particular agent. Conversely, a ground can create a claim even where no comparative harm occurred.

A claim's full content is fixed by [the holder's own good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good), its ground, and the situation before conflict with other claims is considered. Comparison may determine which claims can be satisfied together; it must not rewrite what any claim required at the identification stage.

## Imposition (G1)

An **imposition claim** arises where A's conduct sets back or endangers P's interests through a causal route A controls, contributes to, or creates the risk of, and P cannot avoid the impact at reasonable cost through ordinary exercises of standing. The impact must not consist solely in other parties' unowed exercises.

Its content includes due care before materialization and response and repair afterward, scaled by the endangered interest, A's control and knowledge, and the opportunities A had to avoid or reduce the imposition.

The last condition is the **protected-exercise filter**. A chosen rival, an honest criticism, or another holder's refusal can set back P without giving P an imposition claim against the person whose exercise produced the setback. Deception is not protected, because captured judgment is not a free exercise; a structural blockade is an imposition. The move from impact to this narrower ground is a generalization with proposed discipline, not a derivation from standing alone.

## Initiation (G2)

An **initiation claim** arises where A knowingly begins a condition another someone must carry, or deliberately assumes responsibility for a condition begun by someone else. Its content is the thick undertaking: care governed by the holder's own good, truthfulness about the condition and its origin, formation without capture where the relation helps form the holder's standpoint, and no claims against the holder founded on the initiation itself.

Procreation is the limiting case, not the whole ground. The source asymmetry remains bedrock: before a new someone exists, no holder has a claim to be created; once a someone exists, that party holds full claims against those who knowingly initiated or deliberately assumed the condition. [Newness](/wiki/Newness) supplies the limit and [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) develops the beginnings case. Generalizing that structure beyond procreation is a defended reconstruction.

## Holding (G3)

A **holding claim** arises where A governs, employs, confines, keeps, classifies, or otherwise holds effective power over P. The holder owes survivable exit or, where exit is impossible in principle, permanent callability; contestation capable of moving outcomes; P's welfare as a binding limit; no reliance on P's replaceability; and recognition not made conditional on administrative legibility.

The ground states those requirements without computing their practical thresholds. [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) separates evidence about access and alteration from the open holder-relative cutoffs and states the proposed evidential burden where A controls the route or its record.

Mere situational ability to aid, withhold aid, or cause a setback does not by itself establish holding. Such cases must satisfy either the need ground or the imposition ground on its own terms unless the agent has taken or occupies a role of effective control over the party.

The source framework establishes these requirements across institutional holdings. Treating them as one ground, and extending the ground to every relevant holding relation, is a generalization. The ground does not condemn power as such; it identifies the answerability power incurs.

## Exercise (G4)

A valid performed exercise changes the claim structure. Consent, refusal, release, promise, and directive bind within their content and scope, including through later incapacity or death. They cannot be supplied by others, presumed from silence, constructed counterfactually, or manufactured. [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) states the validity conditions.

Where performance requires the holder's continuing bodily condition, the exercise remains revocable as to specific performance while that condition continues. Reliance and loss can generate repair claims, but not bodily compulsion. This clause is derived given the bridge that compelled continuation converts the holder's body into material; a reader who rejects that bridge reopens specific performance.

## Responsiveness (G5)

An unsatisfied claim generates secondary claims appropriate to what occurred. A justified override, a necessity-wrong, and an unjustified wronging can all leave something owed afterward, though not the same thing.

The bridge is near-conceptual: if non-satisfaction left nothing behind, the theory could not distinguish after the fact between a claim it had [adequate reason](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) to override and one it violated. The existence of residue is derived given that distinction; [Residue](/wiki/Residue) proposes its differentiated recognitional, explanatory, compensatory, distributive, and violation-grade contents.

## Need (G6)

A **need claim** arises where P's central interest is in imminent peril, A is uniquely or saliently positioned to remedy it, no adequate institutional channel is available in time, and the remedy would impose neither a claim-violating means nor a cost grave relative to the stake. Directedness comes from A's situational position rather than from general beneficence.

This rescue ground is proposed. Its sacrifice cap is a defended placed line, not a computed result. Its prohibition on claim-violating rescue instantiates the general [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound): no claim contains another party's conversion.

## Multiple grounds

One relation can instantiate several grounds. An institution may both impose a risk and hold power over those exposed; a parent may initiate a condition, receive performed exercises, and later wrong the holder; a rescuer may become a holder by taking custody. The claims are identified separately and their contents accumulate unless a valid exercise or another rule changes them.

Grounds also identify different addressees. Genetic contribution alone does not fix the initiation claim; knowing agency and deliberate assumption do. Remote benefit alone does not fix an imposition claim; control and causal contribution matter. A public desire names no claim until holders, addressees, and grounds are supplied.

## Limits

- No argument proves the six grounds exhaustive. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) states what a completeness argument would require.
- The grounds identify claims and initial content. [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) supplies the diagnostic account of content and gravity; [comparison](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline), complete [adequacy](/wiki/Adequate-Justification), and [enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) remain downstream questions.
- The means-bound and sacrifice cap are defended commitments. They must not travel under the proposed need ground as though they were derived.
- Generalizations from source domains remain refusable without erasing the narrower source claims from which they began.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) · [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) · [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Provision-Claims.mdx

- Title: Provision Claims
- Slug: Provision-Claims
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: derived, proposed
- Provenance: reconstruction, clarification
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Authorization, Possession

````mdx
# Provision Claims

## Summary

A **provision claim** is a directed claim to a shared benefit or institutional function. It must identify its holders, its addressee, and the relation that makes the benefit owed. Its content must stay within the function displaced, collected for, relied on, promised, or required by existing claims; public desire, custom, growth, prestige, convenience, or an institution's preferred output cannot supply the missing ground.

The reconstruction recognizes six grounds. The **agency floor** covers basic agency and subsistence presupposed by an arrangement that forecloses alternatives. **Foreclosure-provision** requires an arrangement that occupies a means to supply the displaced function. **Participation-reciprocity** concerns functions collected through non-optional or foreclosing participation. **Legitimate reliance** protects reasonable, induced, life-structuring dependence, usually through transition rather than permanent continuation. **Enacted commitment** covers performed promises and entitlements. **Claim-infrastructure** covers systems needed to make existing claims answerable.

These grounds identify when provision is owed rather than merely wanted. Under the proposed claim-grounded adequacy condition, only such claims, not claimless totals or preferences, can justify burdening another party. The grounds do not create claims to another party's possession, and identifying a provision claim does not settle its priority, adequate implementation, or enforceability.

## Why provision needs grounds

Institutions routinely describe desired benefits as public needs. Without a ground test, the theory faces two failures. Treating every preference as a claim lets majorities burden anyone for whatever they want; treating no shared benefit as owed makes coordination, subsistence, review, and public infrastructure morally invisible.

Provision claims occupy the middle. Each must name the parties owed, the arrangement that owes them, the function owed, and the facts of jurisdiction, foreclosure, participation, reliance, commitment, or claim-service that direct the relation.

## The six provision grounds

**Agency floor.** An arrangement owes those under its effective jurisdiction the conditions of basic agency and subsistence that its operation presupposes and for which it forecloses alternatives. This reads the [holding ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds)'s welfare limit positively.

**Foreclosure-provision.** Where an arrangement occupies or closes the means by which parties would otherwise meet a need, it owes the displaced function to those it displaced. Monopolizing roads, currency, adjudication, emergency response, or another route creates a claim to the function, not merely an expectation of institutional generosity.

**Participation-reciprocity.** Non-optional or foreclosing participation can ground claims to benefits within the scheme's **function-set**: the functions it displaced or collected for. Taxation, regulation, and closed alternatives matter; custom alone does not. An amenity does not become owed because a prosperous arrangement usually supplies it.

**Legitimate reliance.** Induced, reasonable, life-structuring reliance on continued provision grounds claims against abrupt withdrawal. The claim is to transition and protection against concentrated foreclosure, not necessarily to permanent continuation of the original arrangement.

**Enacted commitment.** An arrangement's performed promises and enacted entitlements can bind it toward those who relied or were conscripted. Where the authority behind the commitment was defective, reasonable induced reliance can survive even if the stronger commitment claim fails.

**Claim-infrastructure.** Courts, records, registries, review routes, and other systems necessary to answer existing claims can themselves be owed because of the claims they make answerable.

## Function-set and anti-relabeling

A putative provision claim must survive an anti-relabeling check:

1. Which someones hold it?
2. Against which arrangement?
3. On which provision ground?
4. What function was displaced, collected for, relied on, promised, or made necessary by other claims?
5. Does the claimed content stay within that function?

Statements such as *the public wants it*, *growth requires it*, or *this is how the institution operates* answer none of these questions. A benefit can remain valuable while failing to be owed.

## No wrongful content

No commitment or provision ground can create a claim whose content is another party's possession. An enacted exclusionary benefit, for example, does not become claim-valid through reliance alone. What can survive its abolition is a transition claim for parties whose lives were reasonably structured around it, not a claim to continued subordination.

This rule is derived given [Possession](/wiki/Possession)'s reconstructed marks and defended address argument. Rejecting that analysis removes the no-wrongful-content rule rather than leaving it independently derived.

## Provision and prevention

[Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) concerns a particular priority within action: arrangements should answer the claims of existing parties before treating prevention of possible future parties as a substitute for meeting them. Provision claims are broader. They explain when the support, infrastructure, transition, and contest routes invoked by that priority are actually owed.

## Limits

- The provision grounds are a reconstruction with proposed checks; they are not claimed to exhaust every institutional source of provision.
- Whether an arrangement satisfies a ground is partly empirical, especially where foreclosure, function, reliance, and practical access are contested.
- The no-wrongful-content rule inherits possession's mixed registers: reconstructed marks, defended tests and address argument, and proposed jointness.
- Provision grounds identify claims; [comparison](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) and [enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) remain separate questions.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Authority-Across-Time.mdx

- Title: Authority Across Time
- Slug: Authority-Across-Time
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: defended, open
- Provenance: reconstruction, clarification
- Depends on: Authorization, The-Holders-Good, Settlement

````mdx
# Authority Across Time

## Summary

**Authority across time** governs how a holder's present exercises, prior exercises, settled cares, and current claims relate when they do not all point in the same direction. The rules protect a valid exercise from being replaced by biography, while preventing a prior exercise from becoming unlimited authority over every later circumstance or manner of implementation.

The order matters. A valid present exercise governs what it addresses. A valid prior exercise governs within its interpreted scope. Inferred ordering fills only the gaps. Present claims constrain implementation even where they do not repeal the substance of a prior exercise.

## Present exercise

An explicit, valid, present exercise governs what it addresses outright. A holder's biography cannot overrule it on the ground that the choice is uncharacteristic, imprudent, or inconsistent with the life others recognize. Biographical continuity is evidence for cases in which no exercise speaks, not a court over a present one.

Validity remains the gate. The holder must have the relevant capacity, and the exercise must be free and unmanufactured under [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization).
````
