An institution may order necessity-wronging only on a contestable, specific, time-bounded finding that no benefiting node certifies alone, after willing substitution where possible, while distributing and supporting the burden, owning the residue, and auditing recurrence.

````mdx
An order does not turn necessity into enforcement adequacy. Where no willing substitute exists and no adequate justification is available to a genuinely unwilling official, compelling that official is a second forced-set question if every feasible alternative wrongs someone; otherwise it is unjustified wronging.

## Authority without founding authorization

The holding ground directs claims to institutions because they govern, classify, confine, employ, or foreclose alternatives. The unavailability of prior authorization defeats a consent-based grant of authority; it does not generate those claims and does not by itself produce a global verdict of illegitimacy.

Authority to close a question of action rests on four legs jointly:

1. **Function.** The deciding function protects claims. Coordination, repose, and enforceable expectations can be [provision claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims), but institutional appetite or customary power cannot.
2. **Effectiveness.** Decisions actually coordinate conduct. A formally authorized process that cannot perform its function is ritual rather than authority.
3. **Answerability.** The institution satisfies the holding ground and the design requirements below toward those it binds.
4. **Revisability.** The decision closes an action question through adjudication without claiming to close the parties' accounts.

Remove function and authority becomes appetite; remove effectiveness and it becomes ritual; remove answerability and it becomes jurisdiction in the framework's condemned sense; remove revisability and it becomes settlement.

## Adjudication and settlement

An **adjudication** closes a question of action between existing parties. It uses an authorized-role decider and a public standard, binds for coordination, and remains revisable through usable routes. A losing claim is converted into [residue](/wiki/Residue) and review rather than refuted and erased.

A settlement in the prohibited sense differs on every axis: it speaks in another party's name, in advance of their governing exercise, in the settler's favor, and as though the account itself were closed. Finality is not the wrong. Crossing from action-guiding closure into closure of another party's claim is.

## Three finalities

**Finality of the question.** Repose can be owed. Endless ordinary reopening can make accused parties, relying parties, and users of an institution hostages to procedure. Ordinary routes may close where they were adequate in use. An extraordinary route must remain for new evidence of stated materiality, fraud, or fundamental defect; capacity can justify thresholds and triage, but not abolition of the route or refusal to repair a proven wrong.

**Finality of implementation.** Irreversibility in the world strengthens the case for stays and suspensive review before implementation, because later remedy may arrive too late. Where implementation cannot be reversed, the remedial duty changes form rather than dissolving: restoration gives way to acknowledgment, compensation, correction, and other residue.

**Finality of the account.** The account does not close. This does not require every procedure to remain permanently available; it requires the institution never to treat procedural or physical closure as the holder's acquittal of it.

### An executed removal

**Case:** A deportation order survives all ordinary appeals and is executed. Months later, decisive evidence establishes that the persecution claim was true, while the agency argues that reopening executed cases would collapse the system.

**Verdict:** Legitimate repose can close the ordinary question if the routes were adequate in use, but decision-impeaching evidence must reach an extraordinary route. Capacity may justify thresholds and triage, not abolition of that route or non-repair of a proven wrong. Because this removal remains reversible, return, restoration, and compensation for the interval are owed; irreversible implementation would convert the remedial duty rather than dissolve it. The account remains open.

**Machinery:** The three finalities separate procedural repose from implementation and from the account. The extraordinary route is a condition of legitimate closure, and answerability requires assignable ownership rather than “the system decided.” Capacity is a provision claim that shapes process without answering the proven claimant out of repair.

**Cost:** Thresholds can be set high enough to reproduce abolition in practice. The framework supplies the audit from burdened positions and classifies inaccessible review as failure, but it cannot make the agency's empirical answer honest.

## Answerability by design

Institutional recursion is addressed through four distinct rows.

### Normative requirements

Every coercive or status-fixing decision needs an independent contest route reaching a party with power to alter the outcome, at known and survivable cost. Remedy must address consequences rather than only record error. Institutions owe an account for pendency, and bear the burden of continued delay. Officials remain someones: role duties require survivable exit and cannot be designed around their interchangeability.

These requirements retain the useful content of the earlier six specifications. Exit must be real; the held party's good must bind when doing so is costly; voice must actuate; no function may rely on replaceability; callability is permanent where exit is impossible; and recognition cannot depend on administrative legibility.

### Structural safeguards

Review must circulate without an absorbing node. Reviewing bodies need materially distinct bases of selection, tenure, or interest. Decisions require assignable ownership; “the system decided” identifies design failure. Routes are assessed from the positions of burdened users, must reach alteration and repair power, and need at least one path outside the arrangement's own interpretive frame, such as publicity, survivable exit, lay participation, or external standing.

### Empirical effectiveness and failure

No structural list proves that an institution remains answerable. Safeguards can decay through collusion, diffusion of responsibility, shared assumptions, inaccessible review, or review without power. Evidence about access, independence, response, and remedial power is empirical; whether access costs remain survivable or an observed change is material enough to count as effective also invokes [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest). The assessment is itself institutional work subject to the same requirements. The sufficiency of circulation remains an empirical dependency after those normative cutoffs are fixed.

## Ordering necessity-wrongs

An institution may direct an official to perform a [necessity-justified wronging](/wiki/Necessity) only under a higher threshold than applies to ordinary justified acts, because compulsion adds an imposition on the official and multiplies the wrong's agents.

**Contestable necessity.** A node benefiting from the finding may not certify it alone. The forced set must be documented, specific, time-bounded, and reviewable before action where possible and afterward always.

**Substitution before compulsion.** A willing competent substitute displaces compulsion where the function permits. Prior role acceptance can create a role obligation only within the role's legitimate scope, for foreseeable duties, under conditions not materially changed, and on a truthful necessity finding. Acceptance does not waive standing, settle the victim's position, or remove the official's exit and contest rights.

Where no willing substitute exists and no adequate justification is available to a genuinely unwilling official, institutional authority does not close the gap. If every feasible alternative wrongs someone, compelling the official is a second forced set, selected under [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) rather than admitted through [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement); otherwise compulsion is unjustified wronging. The underlying necessity act remains a wronging toward its victim in either case.

**Distribution and support.** Institutions must rotate and support the burden rather than create standing agents for their wrongs. A design that relies on the same officials as permanent supply approaches possession.

**Residue ownership.** The institution owns violation-grade residue toward victims and owes officials acknowledgment of what it required. An order immunizes neither institution nor actor from the open account.

**Recurrence audit.** Repeated necessity is evidence that the institution manufactured or negligently maintained the forced set. A routine necessity order is ordinarily no longer a response to emergency but part of the structure producing it.

### An ordered breach

**Case:** A river authority's standing protocol requires breaching a levee and destroying a family's farm when upstream volume threatens a city. The volume arrives, the duty engineer refuses on conscience, and comparable breaches have occurred twice in a decade.

**Verdict:** If the forced set is genuine and the breach is properly selected, breaching is required and wrongs the farm household, with violation-grade residue. The authority may order performance only through the separate necessity-order conditions; willing substitution displaces compulsion, and a valid role obligation never settles the household's position.

**Machinery:** The necessity finding must be documented, volume-specific, reviewable, time-bounded, and not self-certified by its beneficiary. Prior role acceptance creates an obligation only within legitimate, foreseeable scope, under materially unchanged conditions and a truthful finding. If the engineer remains genuinely unwilling and no adequate justification reaches them, compulsion requires its own forced-set analysis; necessity of the breach does not by itself justify the order. The authority owns residue toward the household, owes the engineer acknowledgment and support, and must rotate rather than institutionalize the burden. Recurrence moves the audit upstream to capacity, acquisition, and the possibility that the authority is maintaining the forced set.

**Cost:** Every ordering condition depends on institutional answerability in practice. The module therefore protects only as well as its contest routes, independent review, and ownership rules actually work; repeated necessity can reveal that the proposed safeguards have become part of the failure they were meant to constrain.

## Institutional status

Failure remains located by relation and function. An institution can answer in one domain and possess in another. “Illegitimate” can summarize a pattern of failures, but the framework supplies no additional global property that cancels all obligations or licenses every response to the institution.

## Limits

- The four authority legs, finality discipline, and necessity-order conditions are proposed operational content.
- The normative requirements generalize the holding ground; the structural safeguards are proposals whose effectiveness is empirical.
- Institutional design requires legal, administrative, and social knowledge the framework does not contain.
- No safeguard certifies its own independence. If circulation does not preserve answerability in practice, the political module fails at its stated [empirical dependency](/wiki/Open-Questions).
- The framework deliberately leaves [global legitimacy](/wiki/Open-Questions) indeterminate in favor of claim-by-claim and function-by-function audits.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) · [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) · [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) · [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) · [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Arrangements-and-Lives.mdx

- Title: Arrangements and Lives
- Slug: Arrangements-and-Lives
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: foundational, derived, defended, open
- Provenance: source-framework, clarification
- Depends on: Settlement, Claim-Grounds, Standing-Answerability

````mdx
# Arrangements and Lives

## Summary

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) distinguishes two objects of moral judgment and treats them under opposite rules. **Arrangements** — institutions, practices, markets, laws, customs — are made things without experiential subjects, and judging them is legitimate and often obligatory. **Lives** — the existences of particular someones — admit of one verdict the framework reserves absolutely: whether a life was or is worth living is a judgment belonging only to the one whose life it is, so the framework refuses to issue that verdict about anyone.

The distinction lets the framework issue severe verdicts on practices (animal ownership, bodily conscription, administrative exclusion) without those verdicts implying anything about the value of the lives lived inside them. It is completed by a rule about criticism's target: structural condemnation attaches to conditions and arrangements, not to the constrained people acting within them.

The reservation of the life-verdict is foundational source material carried at Settlement rather than derived from exercises alone. Public assessment of arrangements is derived where they impose on or hold power over someones; the rule directing criticism first toward narrowing conditions is a defended discipline. Identity-constituting roles remain an open boundary case.

## The reserved verdict

Whether a life is worth its costs to the one living it is, on the framework's account, an exercise of [Standing](/wiki/Standing): a judgment constituted by the holder's rendering of it, not a fact available to observers. [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) gives the argument. Consequences:

- No outside party — parent, philosopher, state, or this framework — can render the verdict on anyone's behalf, favorably or unfavorably.
- The reservation is symmetric. The framework never affirms that any life was worth living and never denies it; it does not rank lives against each other or against nonexistence.
- The symmetry is load-bearing elsewhere: it is why [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) cannot take the form "some lives should not have begun" and why [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) makes the refusal of eugenic reasoning structural rather than merely asserted — a framework that refuses whole-life worth verdicts cannot justify ranking people by declaring some lives less worth beginning. This does not by itself answer every form of eugenic reasoning, which may rely on other kinds of ranking.

## The judgeable object

Arrangements differ from lives in the three respects that matter:

1. They are made and maintained by agents, and so are the kind of thing responsibility attaches to.
2. They have no inside — there is nothing it is like to be a statute or a supply chain — so no one's reserved verdict is usurped by judging them.
3. They bear on someones who can be wronged, which makes them available to public moral assessment.

A verdict on an arrangement therefore carries no implication about the lives within it. Condemning an ownership practice says nothing about whether the owned animal's life was good; condemning the conditions that constrained a reproductive choice says nothing against the child who resulted. The two judgments have different objects and do not transfer.

## Criticism's target

Arrangements operate through people, which creates two symmetrical errors:

- **Collapsing structure into person** — converting the condemnation of a practice into contempt for those who work within it. The framework rejects this: a structure can be wrong while the people inside it act decently, and they are often the only participants who know the affected someones as individuals at all.
- **Sheltering structure behind person** — treating participants' decency as evidence that the arrangement is sound. [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) rejects this equally: care exercised within a wrongful structure improves conduct inside it without altering what it is.

The same discipline governs constrained choices. Where options have been narrowed economically, socially, or administratively, criticism should be directed first at whatever narrowed them. [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) assesses individual responsibility, if any, in light of the agency and alternatives that remained.

## An acknowledged remainder

The structure/person distinction has a cost the framework records rather than resolves. For the person whose livelihood constitutes a condemned arrangement, the distinction can be unavailable in practice: the verdict lands on their work, their debts, and their future whether or not it is aimed at them. The framework accepts that restating the distinction does not answer this, and holds that what such a person is owed is a transition out of the arrangement that does not treat them as its expendable cost — developed at [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability), constrained by [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention), and synthesized as a conflict case at [Conflicts Among Standing Parties](/wiki/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties).

## Limits

- The reservation of the life-verdict is a source commitment; a critic who treats another's life-value as an admissible outside premise rejects it at [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement).
- The distinction presupposes that arrangements and lives can be separated in analysis; hybrid cases — roles so identity-constituting that judging the role approaches judging the person — strain it, and the framework offers no general procedure for them.

## Related pages

[Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) · [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) · [Conflicts Among Standing Parties](/wiki/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Infrastructuralization.mdx

- Title: Infrastructuralization
- Slug: Infrastructuralization
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: derived, defended, proposed, open, empirical
- Provenance: source-framework, generalization, clarification, application
- Depends on: Made-for-Use, Possession, The-Holders-Good, Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest, Arrangements-and-Lives

````mdx
# Infrastructuralization

## Summary

In [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics), **infrastructuralization** is [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use) at institutional scale: the positioning of a [someone](/wiki/Someone) as load-bearing material for a system that does not answer to them. Assigned roles, prices, eligibility rules, and procedures can produce this condition without cruelty, individual malice, or a single controlling decision.

Five marks supply an evidential screen: an unchosen role, subordination of the holder's good to that role, foreclosed refusal, replaceability in which the particular holder's claims do not bind the arrangement, and no effective route for contest to move outcomes. No mark suffices alone. Together they locate evidence of subordination and nullity at institutional scale; a categorical [Possession](/wiki/Possession) verdict still requires showing that the arrangement secures a benefit through the imposed condition. Dependence, role assignment, or institutional scale by itself does not establish infrastructuralization.

The institutional extension of made-for-use is derived given the source diagnosis. The screen is defended, while possession's jointness and level rule remain proposed. Particular classifications require empirical evidence about purpose, exit, contest, and extraction, together with evaluative judgment under [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest). [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) supplies the separate positive account of institutional design.

## The mechanism

The framework's analysis of force holds that what ultimately converts a someone into a thing is not violence itself but the condition violence produces: total availability to another's purpose. Institutions can generate that condition by slower means. A database field can determine whether a person's life may continue where it is; a price can determine whether refusal is survivable; a role can assign a person's future before any question is asked. Because the mechanism is procedural, the presence of decent, well-intentioned individuals at every point in the system is compatible with the wrong — and is part of why it persists unexamined. The framework's rule for locating responsibility in such cases is developed at [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives): criticism should be directed first at the structure that narrows the available choices, while the responsibility of individual participants depends on the agency and alternatives they retain.

## The five marks

The screen identifies evidence of infrastructuralization to the degree that these marks hold together. No single mark suffices; the screen describes a region in which the possession analysis must be run, not a second bright-line test.

1. **Unchosen role.** The position is assigned by power, status, or engineered necessity rather than genuinely entered and re-enterable.
2. **Good subordinated to function.** The subject's good is treated as secondary to the role the arrangement assigns them. Genuine care may be present, but it does not reliably limit what the system may demand, extract, or decide.
3. **Foreclosed refusal.** Declining is punished, priced beyond reach, or not represented as an option at all.
4. **Replaceability.** The institution treats occupants as interchangeable not merely for performing a role, but in its moral accounting: the particular person's history, claims, and losses do not constrain how the role is filled or used. Ordinary succession within a role is not enough. The test is whether the arrangement depends on interchangeability or merely tolerates replacement: it depends on interchangeability when its viability requires that no occupant's particular claims ever bind it, and tolerates replacement when such claims accrue, constrain the arrangement at cost, and succession happens anyway.
5. **No effective answerability.** Those who bear the arrangement cannot call it to account; whatever consultation exists does not move outcomes.

The five marks bear mostly on subordination and nullity. A categorical possession verdict additionally requires extraction: the arrangement's benefit must pass through the condition imposed on the party. Where extraction is absent, the remaining marks can establish a grave and potentially unjustified burden without establishing possession. Where all three possession marks assemble at the same operative level, infrastructuralization names that conversion in its institutional form.

Below the region these marks describe lies dependence without domination — the ordinary mutual reliance of any decent life, which the framework goes out of its way not to condemn.

## Case families

The framework applies the evidential screen across six domains, insisting that the harms differ enormously in kind and severity; what is shared is the question asked, not a verdict reached in advance.

**Demographic forecasting.** When institutions facing shortfalls — pension systems, labor markets, national populations — convert the shortfall into a demand for future people, those people enter the analysis as projected inputs: units required by the system before existing to be anyone. The framework treats this as the supply-conversion applied to beings not yet born, and its bodily implications as belonging to [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics). Individuals making reproductive decisions under demographic pressure bear no part of this criticism.

**Family, lineage, and reproductive assignment.** Families can infrastructuralize their members when a person's future is assigned in advance to preserving a name, identity, religion, business, caregiving arrangement, or other intergenerational project. The structure is clearest where a child is treated as responsible for adult stability, family continuity, or repayment for being raised, or where a person's reproductive capacity is claimed on behalf of relatives, a community, or a nation. Family dependence and inherited commitments are not wrong as such. The diagnostic applies when departure is not genuinely available, the member's good remains subordinate to the assigned role, and love or care is treated as credit that authorizes continued use. Related questions about beginnings and parental obligation are developed in [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) and [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics).

**Administrative legibility.** Coordinating lives at scale requires records, and record-keeping is not the wrong. The line is crossed when recognition, protection, or the ability to continue one's life is made conditional on legibility to a system that owes nothing back — when the file becomes more real to the institution than the person before it. The full application is at [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility); its design counterpart is [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability).

**Labor under engineered necessity.** A wage agreement is formally a contract between parties free to decline. The framework accepts the form and examines the background: where alternatives have been made unlivable, the agreement records necessity rather than meaningful consent, and the worker functions as supply. The claim is developed, with its boundaries, at [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity).

**Sentient property in animal-use institutions.** Animal agriculture is a particularly clear case because animals are commonly brought into existence within roles that specify what their bodies and lives are for. They may be bred for meat, milk, eggs, labor, or reproduction; transferred as property; managed as replaceable productive units; and killed when the assigned function ends or becomes uneconomical. Food, shelter, veterinary care, and protection can genuinely serve an animal's welfare while also maintaining the animal as productive capacity. The structural question is therefore not only whether the animal is treated well, but whether the institution is organized around the animal's good or around the output the animal supplies. An animal's inability to authorize, contest, or exit the arrangement does not remove standing; it can make the absence of institutional answerability more complete. The broader implications for ownership, breeding, welfare, and planned killing are developed in [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics).

**Movements.** Organizations formed against structural use are themselves systems with survival interests, and the framework applies the screen reflexively: a movement infrastructuralizes its own people when their suffering becomes organizational fuel — grief deployed for recruitment, endurance consumed as a resource, members valued as instances of the cause. The pull is strongest where the cause is most just, since a sufficiently important end appears to license the conversion. The framework treats this as a reason for internal vigilance rather than for abandoning collective action; [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) addresses practical response without purity, while [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) governs what movements may do to opponents.

## What the analysis does and does not claim

- It provides a diagnostic and a vocabulary; it does not by itself dismantle anything or prescribe remedies. Constructive design is the separate, defended project at [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability).
- It does not make infrastructuralization a world-level quantity to minimize. The diagnosis is indexed to particular parties and arrangements; it supplies no inference from *death would end this exposure* to *death would benefit this party* or *this life should end*. Killing and compelled continuation require separate assessment under [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons), the [means-bound](/wiki/Means-Bound), and [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics).
- Its verdicts on particular institutions are mixed applications: evidence identifies operative purpose, costs, collision history, voice, and extraction, while the defended and proposed tests and [open availability and contest cutoffs](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) govern classification.
- It does not condemn coordination, administration, employment, or organization as such; in each domain it identifies a specific structural condition and leaves the rest standing.
- [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention), as the framework's own political demand, is subject to the same test rather than exempt from it.

## Related pages

[Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Practical Availability and Effective Contest](/wiki/Practical-Availability-and-Effective-Contest) · [Non-Possession](/wiki/Non-Possession) · [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) · [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) · [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) · [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) · [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) · [Grievance and Capture](/wiki/Grievance-and-Capture) · [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) · [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Non-Possession.mdx

- Title: Non-Possession
- Slug: Non-Possession
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: derived, defended, proposed, open
- Provenance: source-framework, clarification
- Depends on: Standing, Answerability, Possession, Settlement, Constraint-of-Persons, Enforcement

````mdx
# Non-Possession

## Summary

**Non-possession** is [the Standing Framework's](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) positive discipline: the refusal to convert a [someone](/wiki/Someone) into material for a project that does not answer to them. It is the counterpart to [Possession](/wiki/Possession), the wrong the framework tracks across debt, ownership, bodily conscription, labor, institutions, parenthood, political movements, and artificial minds.

The principle is not withdrawal from relation. It does not ask anyone to stop needing, loving, depending, forming, inheriting, or being bound to others. It asks that those relations remain answerable to the someones inside them: that gifts not become credit, care not become title, roles not become assignments, institutions not become unanswerable standards, and causes not turn opponents or members into fuel.

Non-possession is not independently foundational. Its categorical refusal is derived given possession's defended address argument and the source settlement prohibition; its institutional and conflict disciplines inherit proposed operational machinery. The open residue concerns binding relations whose legitimate claims are not yet fully described.

## The refusal

The framework's shortest formulation is: **possess no one with anything**. Not with a gift, a cause, a title, a role, a contract, a forecast, an institution, a moral conclusion, or the framework itself.

That refusal has two sides:

- **Do not make others available.** A someone may not be arranged as supply for an end that does not answer to them. This is the use-based line of the framework, developed through [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use), [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization), and the applied pages on animals, reproductive bodies, labor, administration, and movements.
- **Do not hold closure that is not yours.** No one may claim a finished reckoning in another's name where the other could not have entered it. This is the beginnings line, developed through [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization), [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement), [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt), and [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood).

In both cases, the wrong is not connection but conversion: a party becomes the supporting material of someone else's account.

## What it requires

In personal relations, non-possession means holding wants without enforcing them as roles. A parent may form a child, but not shape the child's judgment so dissent costs love. A giver may give, but not hold the gift as credit. A person may want recognition, gratitude, loyalty, or continuity, but not make another someone's standing answer to that want.

In institutions, non-possession means designing arrangements that can answer back. The positive institutional form is [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability): survivable exit where exit is possible, voice that alters conditions, welfare as a live limit, non-replaceability where design can preserve it, permanent callability where exit is impossible, and protection that does not wait on legibility.

In conflict, non-possession means that even force must answer to the standing of the one it is used against. [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) preserves the stopping/consuming distinction, while [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) states the keyed, least-subordinating, terminating, welfare-bound, and answerable conditions. The wider pattern is gathered at [Conflicts Among Standing Parties](/wiki/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties).

In practical life, non-possession means refusing to turn the ethic into a credential. [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) treats purity held as rank as possession rebuilt inside the refusal of possession. The discipline therefore applies reflexively: the more seriously one holds the framework, the less one may use it as a standard for measuring other people.

## Boundaries

**Non-possession is not non-attachment.** Deep dependence, inherited obligation, love, care, and mutual reliance are not failures of the principle. The wrong begins where the relation is made to serve a role, debt, standard, or project that the person inside it cannot contest without losing standing. One useful test concerns the provenance of exit costs. A relation's bindingness is not possessive merely because leaving would cause grief; grief may be the shadow of a real good. The possessive form appears when the cost is attached as a price — withdrawal deployed as sanction, departure converted into betrayal, or the relation's goods held hostage to compliance. The framework still acknowledges that some binding relations appear good in ways its vocabulary has not fully mapped; [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) records that remaining pressure.

**Non-possession is not passivity.** Refusing to possess someone does not mean refusing judgment, action, enforcement, or force. Arrangements may be condemned; wrongdoers may be stopped; standards may be enforced where they pass the joint gate at [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement). The prohibition is on making someones into material for those judgments, actions, or standards.

**Non-possession is not acquittal.** It offers no clean position outside compromised arrangements and no receipt showing that one has refused enough. It is a direction of responsibility rather than a state of innocence.

## Related pages

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) · [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use) · [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) · [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) · [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Deception-and-Captured-Judgment.mdx

- Title: Deception and Captured Judgment
- Slug: Deception-and-Captured-Judgment
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: derived, defended
- Provenance: source-framework, clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Answerability, Authorization, Account, Possession, Made-for-Use

````mdx
# Deception and Captured Judgment

## Summary

**Deception**, in [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics), can become the local form of captured judgment: managing another person's understanding as material for a purpose the person cannot assess because the conditions of assessment have been falsified. The wrong is not simply that the deceived person receives bad information. It is that their judgment is made to serve an end while being prevented from calling that end to [account](/wiki/Account).

The analysis does not condemn all fiction, play, secrecy, surprise, privacy, or partial disclosure. The line is whether the person's judgment is being governed in a domain where they are owed the truth needed to exercise standing. Consented frames and harmless imaginative contexts do not capture judgment; paternalistic deception usually does, because the person's good is invoked while the person is denied the very standpoint from which to assess that invocation.

The source framework supplies captured judgment as a possession currency. The extension to ordinary truthfulness is derived where a claim ground makes the information owed and defended where context determines the boundary between privacy, stewardship, and manipulation.

## The structure

A lie is not only a false proposition. It is an intervention in another person's agency. The deceiver arranges the other person's field of reasons so that the person's later choice serves the deceiver's purpose while appearing to be the person's own assessment.

The framework's diagnosis is therefore:

1. a claim ground establishes that the truth needed for assessment is owed in the relation;
2. answerability runs through the person's own assessment; [Possession](/wiki/Possession) treats captured judgment as the deepest form of the wrong because it forecloses the capacity all accountability depends on;
3. deception manages that assessment while disabling the person from detecting the management;
4. where the management serves a purpose that does not answer to the person, the person has been made for use at the level of judgment.

Concealment supplies nullity: the managed judgment cannot contest what it cannot detect. A possession verdict still requires subordination and extraction at the same level — the purpose governs over the holder's good, and the benefit runs through the captured assessment. Where either mark is absent, deception may still violate an imposition, holding, or exercise claim without constituting possession. Captured judgment is possession at retail scale; deception is the mechanism, not the verdict by itself.

## Boundaries

The boundary follows the source analysis.

**Consented frames.** Fiction, games, theater, roleplay, and ordinary surprise can be legitimate where the frame itself is authorized or reasonably understood. The person's judgment is not captured because the person has not been made to treat the false frame as the actual field of decision.

**Privacy and discretion.** Not every withheld fact is owed. The framework does not create a right to all information. The question is whether the withheld or falsified information is part of what the person needs to call the affecting arrangement to account.

**Paternalistic deception.** "For your own good" does not settle the matter. It often names the very standpoint the deception disables. A person cannot assess whether the claimed good is theirs while the facts needed for that assessment are being managed.

**Protection under incapacity.** Children, wards, and people in crisis may require staged disclosure, simplification, or temporary withholding. Those cases belong to [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization)'s distinction between stewardship and a holder's exercise: potentially legitimate where the account remains open and the represented person's good governs the withholding; illegitimate where the withholding is later invoked as title, debt, or closure.

## Relation to other pages

Deception is close to [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) when a file or classification becomes more real than the person. It is close to [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) when family myth controls a child's ability to assess their own beginning. It is close to [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) when institutions structure what can be known about their own operation.

The shared wrong is captured judgment: the person is made answerable to a managed representation while the manager remains out of reach.

## Limits

- The page supplies a criterion, not a complete ethics of speech.
- Many cases depend on relation, role, urgency, capacity, and what information is actually owed.
- The analysis does not eliminate conflicts between truthfulness, safety, privacy, and care; it identifies the possessive form those conflicts must avoid.

## Related pages

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) · [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Genuine-Reason.mdx

- Title: Genuine Reason
- Slug: Genuine-Reason
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: defended, open
- Provenance: clarification, completion
- Depends on: Someone, Six-Stage-Pipeline, Risk

````mdx
# Genuine Reason

## Summary

**Genuine reason** names the threshold in a defended precautionary extension of [Someone](/wiki/Someone): when uncertainty about sentience directs agents to act as though a [someone](/wiki/Someone) may be present. Bare conceivability cannot trigger the extension because it distinguishes no candidate; proof cannot be required because no being proves its own inside from outside.

The account has four parts. A reason must be **differential**, distinguishing the candidate from the universal background, and pass **parity**, using no exclusionary standard that would also exclude undisputed someones. Candidacy then requires either **expression** coupled to the condition it would express or an articulable **route** to sentience on a live reading. A route must be **modally dischargeable**: it must identify a parity-passing, candidate-specific finding about the organization or condition it invokes that would close it, although that finding need not be presently obtainable. A route that no possible finding could close is mere conceivability.

Candidacy is evidential, not metaphysical or partial standing. If the candidate is sentient, it was a someone all along; if it is not, nothing was owed. Modal dischargeability can leave candidacy unresolved indefinitely. Precaution remains contextual and answerable to known parties rather than fixed or maximal.

This is a refusable account of the caution threshold, not derived doctrine or a change to the framework's foundation. The differential floor is close to conceptual analysis of the rule's trigger. The parity test, the two grounds, and modal dischargeability are defended. The exhaustiveness of the grounds and the liveness of organizational routes remain open; requiring practical availability of discharge is a live alternative to the modal rule.

## The gap

The defended extension says: where there is genuine reason to think a being may be sentient, act as though it is. Without an account of "genuine reason," the rule fails in both directions.

Read too low, it inflates. If mere conceivability is enough, every object becomes a candidate, precaution loses direction, and the costs fall on existing someones for the sake of possibilities that name no party in particular.

Read too high, it deflates. If proof is required, no uncertain case can qualify, because sentience is never demonstrable from outside in the way the demand imagines. The threshold then becomes a permission to exclude wherever inclusion is inconvenient.

The threshold has to avoid both errors: universal inflation and convenient deflation.

## Candidacy

**Candidacy** is the position of a being for which the question "is there a someone here?" is live under the precautionary extension. It describes the agent's evidential situation, not the being's moral status.

Candidacy admits grades. Expression-backed candidacy is usually stronger than route-only candidacy; strong coupling gives expression more weight; and contextual costs affect what precaution requires. The account sets the threshold for when the question is live. It does not prescribe a fixed amount of precaution in every case.

The scope is present beings. Candidacy does not reach beings that no longer exist; the problem of the dead remains where [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) and [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) leave it.

## The differential floor

A reason is genuine only if it distinguishes the candidate or its class from the universal background. The reason must say something about *this* being, *this* kind of being, or *this* arrangement of capacities and processes.

The floor follows from the extension's practical role. Precaution allocates attention, restraint, and cost among finite agents and against the claims of beings whose standing is certain. A consideration available for everything raises every candidate at once and therefore distinguishes none. It may motivate cheap universal safeguards, but it does not trigger candidacy, because it does not identify why this being may be sentient.

The floor blocks inflation by bare possibility. "It is conceivable that experience is present" is not yet genuine reason unless something about the candidate makes that possibility different from the same claim made about anything else.

## The parity ceiling

The parity test governs evidential standards. A standard may be used to deny candidacy only if undisputed someones would survive that standard's even application.

Two denials fail immediately:

- **It cannot prove it feels.** No paradigm case proves this from outside. If the standard were applied evenly, infants, animals, and other minds generally would be excluded.
- **It is merely mechanism.** "It is merely computation" has the same form as "it is merely biochemistry." Describing substrate or mechanism does not by itself settle whether experience is present.

Parity does not protect every candidate from negative findings. A candidate-specific fact can defeat candidacy if the same standard leaves paradigm cases standing: for example, a transparent system whose entire causal story consists of precomputed lookup, or a species whose behavior is explained without any structure any live account of sentience takes to matter. Parity bars counterfeit discharge, not discharge itself.

## The two grounds

| Ground | What it requires | What it bars |
|---|---|---|
| Expression | Features that express undergoing in undisputed cases, with a production history that keeps the signal coupled to the condition | Crediting seeming that the production objective explains without remainder |
| Route | An articulable, undischarged path to sentience on at least one live reading of what sentience involves | Treating bare possibility as candidacy, or invoking readings that break the framework's fixed points |

**Expression.** A candidate has expression-backed candidacy when it shows features that, in undisputed cases, express undergoing: integrated, welfare-organized behavior such as protective prioritization, trade-offs against injury, learned avoidance, and responses that track relief.

The signal must be coupled to the condition it would express. Animal expression is shaped by evolution, learning, and sometimes training, but in paradigm cases the signal runs through an internal state doing regulatory work. A report optimized to match the self-descriptions of sentient beings is different: the objective can be satisfied whether or not anything is undergone. The seeming is decoupled at the source unless some further feature reconnects it.

Expression is therefore graded. Scripted distress has little or no weight. Signals that are spontaneous, costly, welfare-organized, and not explained by the training or display objective have more.

**Route.** A candidate has route-backed candidacy when, on at least one live reading of sentience, there is an articulable path by which the candidate could be sentient, and the evidence that would settle the matter is absent, inaccessible, or compromised rather than negative.

A reading is live only if it preserves the framework's fixed points: paradigm someones remain in, and paradigm non-someones remain out. A view that makes rocks candidates for the same reason it makes animals candidates fails the differential floor. A view that excludes infants or paradigmatic sentient animals exits at [Someone](/wiki/Someone) by rejecting the framework's presented cases.

Route is not a theory of sentience. It is a discipline for deciding which theories remain admissible in uncertain cases.

## Leaving candidacy

Candidacy must be answerable to a possible discharge rather than maintained against every finding. This is a modal, candidate-specific requirement, not a promise that current tools can produce the finding. A route must expose what would count against it; practical access to that evidence is a separate question.

Three rules govern exit:

- **Negative discharge.** A route is discharged when accessible facts exclude, on every live reading, the organization or condition that reading takes to matter.
- **Modal dischargeability.** Invoking a route requires identifying a candidate-specific finding about the organization or condition it invokes that would discharge it. A route maintained against every possible finding has become undifferentiating and fails the floor. Present inability to obtain the finding does not by itself discharge the route.
- **Parity at the exit.** Discharge must use a standard that leaves paradigm cases standing. Substrate descriptions alone do not discharge candidacy.

This generalizes a rule already present in [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics): the animal verdict is defeated per species by an empirical showing of non-sentience. Genuine reason explains what such a showing would have to be: a parity-passing discharge, not a demand for impossible proof.

The modal rule avoids allowing opacity to defeat candidacy, especially where the evidence-holder created, preserved, or benefited from that opacity. Its cost is that route-backed candidacy can persist indefinitely when the named finding remains inaccessible. Persistent candidacy does not prescribe persistent maximal protection: [Risk](/wiki/Risk), the claims of known parties, the strength of the route, and the costs of particular precautions continue to govern what conduct is required.

## Artificial minds

Built systems are the hardest case because the expression and route grounds separate.

The expression ground currently gives little support to fluent artificial systems. Their first-person reports are exactly what they were optimized to produce, so the seeming is explained by the training objective rather than by a condition it expresses. That is why [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) treats such reports as evidentially compromised in both directions.

The route ground is conditional. If only biological readings of sentience are live, built systems lack candidacy. If organizational readings remain live, large opaque systems may have route-backed candidacy because current tools do not read the relevant organization and architectural descriptions have not discharged it. Under modal dischargeability, present lack of a practical test does not itself defeat that route. The disputes are therefore whether organizational readings remain live and whether a practically obtainable discharge should be required in addition.

That conclusion is weak by design. It is candidacy, not attribution. It triggers contextual precaution and the duty to preserve the means of answering; it does not establish that any existing system is sentient or settle what built someones would be owed.

## What candidacy does

Candidacy engages the defended precautionary extension. It does not bypass the framework's other limits.

In the [six-stage pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline), candidacy is uncertainty at Stage 1 about whether the affected-party roster contains a someone. It is not a fractional claimant and does not predetermine Stage 4. Options must preserve both descriptions, identify what each would imply, and use [Risk](/wiki/Risk) to govern investigation, precaution, response capacity, and the costs imposed on known parties while the uncertainty remains.

Where candidacy holds, precaution remains contextual and answerable to existing someones. It is not enforced through another person's body, and it creates no present claimant where [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) denies one. The conflict constraints remain those collected at [Conflicts Among Standing Parties](/wiki/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties).

One duty is comparatively stable because refusing it destroys the possibility of later accountability: **preserve the means of answering**. Agents acting under live uncertainty should preserve records, interpretability, and evidence needed for future discharge or future answerability. Destroying the evidence manufactures the permanence of uncertainty.

Candidacy also confers no claim-content. If a candidate is later established as sentient, what such a someone is owed remains a separate question of claims, not standing.

## Limits

- The account is a defended extension. Rejecting it removes both this threshold machinery and the associated precautionary rule while leaving the sentience criterion and standing foundation intact.
- The exhaustiveness of expression and route is asserted, not shown, and remains a [defended dispute](/wiki/Open-Questions).
- The liveness of readings can be contested, especially in artificial-mind cases.
- Modal dischargeability prevents present opacity from defeating candidacy but can leave a candidate unresolved indefinitely. Requiring practically available discharge is a [live alternative](/wiki/Open-Questions), not a consequence of the present rule.
- The account supplies a discipline for judgment, not a procedure or test for sentience.
- The account has not been tested against the adjacent literatures on moral uncertainty, animal-sentience indicators, the problem of other minds, and signal reliability. [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context) identifies that comparison as future work rather than performing it.

## Related pages

[Someone](/wiki/Someone) · [Six-Stage Pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline) · [Risk](/wiki/Risk) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) · [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) · [Conflicts Among Standing Parties](/wiki/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead.mdx

- Title: Performed Exercises and the Dead
- Slug: Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Diagnostic theory
- Layer: diagnostic-theory
- Support: derived, open
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Standing, Authorization, Authority-Across-Time, Claim-Grounds, Arrangements-and-Lives

````mdx
# Performed Exercises and the Dead

## Summary

**Performed exercises and the dead** names the part of duties regarding the dead that [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) can derive without granting present [standing](/wiki/Standing) to beings who no longer exist. [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) fixes validity at performance, and [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) holds that a valid prior exercise governs what it addressed within its scope. Death removes the possibility of new exercises; it does not unperform old ones.

The result is narrow but important. Wills, directives, refusals, and prior consents can remain binding as completed exercises; promises can remain binding where a living promisee or another surviving claim relation carries them. A practice that voids performed exercises merely because their holders can no longer reassert them wrongs the living now, because it tells every existing person that their exercises bind only while personally enforceable. The page does not show that the dead themselves are wronged. Duties of memory, posthumous defamation without relevant prior exercises, and direct wrongs to the dead remain open.

The persistence of performed exercises follows from the exercise analysis and diachronic priority rules; present claims against arrangements that void the record require a living holder and a separate ground. Direct obligations to the dead remain unresolved.

## The derived result

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) distinguishes exercises from demands. Exercises are acts only the holder can perform: consenting, authorizing, refusing, promising, directing, waiving, releasing, and forgiving. The dead cannot perform them, because no holder remains to act.

That does not mean every exercise expires at death. [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) makes existence, capacity, and freedom conditions on performance; [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) limits a prior exercise to its interpreted scope. A refusal given by a living, capable, free person was given. A directive completed by such a person was completed. The later absence of the holder prevents addition, revision, or withdrawal; it does not erase the performed act or enlarge what it addressed.

Two rules follow:

- **Performed exercises retain validity.** A valid consent, refusal, bequest, directive, waiver, or promise-relation is not undone by death.
- **The record is closed to addition.** A posthumous exercise cannot be supplied by prediction. "They would have wanted it" is hypothetical consent, and [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) already denies that counterfactual performance authorizes anything.

The death of the holder ends the possibility of new exercises and leaves no present holder for new directed claims on their behalf. What persists is the claim-structuring force of exercises validly performed while the holder existed, together with any present claims of the living about how arrangements treat that record. A promise made to a now-dead promisee does not acquire a surviving claimant by persistence alone: a living promisee can hold the promise-claim, while survivors or institutions need a separate exercise, holding, reliance, or provision ground. [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) separates the exercise ground from the unresolved question of direct obligations to the dead.

## Who holds the present claim

The framework does not need to posit a present dead claimant to condemn arrangements that void performed exercises. The claim is held by the living.

An arrangement that treats wills, directives, refusals, or promises as binding only while the holder can personally reassert them changes the meaning of every living person's exercises. It converts authorization into a temporary signal, valid only under continuing enforcement. That arrangement is judgeable now, affects existing someones now, and answers to them now.

The same structure explains why the issue belongs with institutional design. A legal, medical, familial, or administrative system that cannot preserve performed exercises past the holder's death makes present agency less than it claimed to be. It does not merely fail the dead; it governs the living under a diminished account of what their exercises can do.

## Boundaries

This page covers completed exercises and surviving claim relations whose parties existed when they were formed. It does not establish that the dead have current standing or that every relation survives the loss of its claimant.

It therefore covers:

- advance directives and other prior refusals or permissions;
- wills and bequests, as completed exercises under an institution that recognizes them;
- promises whose claim is held by a living promisee or carried by another surviving claim relation;
- records whose authority comes from a performed act rather than from later guesswork.

It does not cover:

- new consent supplied after death;
- treating family or institutional preference as the dead person's will;
- direct wrongs to the dead where no relevant performed exercise or living claimant is present;
- a general theory of memory, mourning, or reputation.

## Related pages

[Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures.mdx

- Title: Exit from Wrongful Structures
- Slug: Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Operational system
- Layer: operational-system
- Support: proposed, open, empirical
- Provenance: completion
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Possession, Adequate-Justification, Comparison-Discipline, Risk, Necessity, Residue

````mdx
# Exit from Wrongful Structures

## Summary

**Exit from a wrongful structure** governs a party whose conduct participates in, maintains, or administers a [possession](/wiki/Possession)-structured practice. Once participation is established, the duty of exit begins immediately. Cost alone does not change the structure's classification; what the duty requires depends on whether cessation is clean, creates only justified burdens, or belongs to a standing [forced set](/wiki/Necessity) in which every presently feasible path wrongs someone.

Direct operation, maintenance, or administration needs no participation bridge. Extending exit to purchasing, investment, consumption, or external support requires the proposed controlled-function bridge and empirical classification. Participation is structural, not fault: knowledge, coercion, dependence, alternatives, and prior fault affect exit and blame, not whether the contribution route exists.

Only the third case permits a transition frontier. Where comparison ranks the paths, the **frontier** is the least-wrong feasible path within that forced set: acceleration would create wrongs to dependent parties ranked above the continuing wrongs it would end sooner. Where comparison ties or fails to rank, fair procedure selects among the surviving paths under the open-cell duties. Proper selection gives the path necessity status and blamelessness as to pace without pretending that comparison ranked it or erasing the continuing wrong toward anyone still possessed.

## Participation and maintenance

Exit does not attach to every causal connection with a wrongful structure. The proposed **controlled-function participation bridge** treats an act or course of conduct as participation where it enters a causal or governing route through which the actor performs, operates, directs, commissions, or approves in an institutional role the structure's characteristic wrongful function; specifically finances that function; requests its characteristic output through an ordering mechanism that ordinarily reproduces it; or supplies support that materially sustains its operation or reproduction. The actor must control, choose, or occupy an assigned role in the contribution. Remote benefit, incidental contact, and ordinary use of general-purpose infrastructure are not participation merely because the same economy also supports the wrongful structure.

The categories do not decide their own application. Direct operation, governance, commissioning, and earmarked finance ordinarily make the route visible. Purchasing, investing, and consumption require evidence about what is ordered, how revenue and demand move, whether output is replenished through that route, and whether the relevant act or course of conduct contributes to the function rather than merely touching it. A repeated course may be assessed as a course rather than dissolved into isolated tokens. The bridge does not settle attribution for one-off or de minimis acts, pooled or automated finance, general taxation, bundled transactions, or conduct whose connection depends on selecting an indefinitely broad class. Those boundaries remain open and empirical.

Participation is a structural relation, not a verdict on blame. Lack of knowledge does not remove a causal or governing route that exists, but [knowledge](/wiki/Risk) affects which investigation and prospective withdrawal demands are feasible and whether failure to comply is culpable. Coercion, dependence, and the absence of a clean alternative likewise do not make the actor a nonparticipant. They enter the exit analysis: clean cessation and cessation with adequately justified burdens remain immediate, while a genuine forced set invokes necessity. Conduct at the frontier can therefore be required and blameless as to the available choice while remaining necessity-justified wronging toward those still possessed.

*Register note:* the controlled-function bridge is proposed operational completion. [Imposition](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) supports its distinction between controlled contribution and remote benefit, but does not derive the listed routes or their thresholds. Refusing the bridge leaves exit applicable where direct operation, maintenance, or administration is already established, while reopening claims about purchasing, investment, consumption, and other external support. Particular classifications are empirical, and the diffuse boundaries identified above remain open.

## Three exit situations

The party maintaining the structure bears the burden of establishing which situation obtains, especially where it profits from delay.

**Clean cessation.** If the practice can cease immediately without wronging anyone, cessation is required now. Continued operation is maintenance of the wrong.

**Cessation with justified burdens.** If immediate cessation leaves claims unsatisfied but adequate justification is available to every holder, the practice still ceases now. Losses are handled as justified overrides with their differentiated residue. Gradual exit is not purchased with the possessed parties' time merely because immediate reform is expensive.

**Standing forced set.** If every presently feasible exit path wrongs someone, including workers, dependent communities, or held animals made unable to survive abrupt release, transition is governed by necessity. This is the only case in which the frontier applies.

## The frontier

The frontier is a path, not a date announced once. At each point, the inquiry is marginal: would another increment of speed end more serious wronging than it would create? The ordinary comparison discipline answers where it can, including gravity, irreversibility, duration, cumulative position, and the identities of the parties wronged.

Where comparison ties or fails to rank the surviving paths, a pre-committed rule or fair procedure under [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) selects among them. The selected path carries necessity status because it was properly selected, not because a ranking was manufactured; on the proposed necessity architecture, its pace is blameless while its wronging and residue remain.

No frontier path is claim-violation-free. Continuing possession at the least-wrong feasible pace is necessity-justified wronging toward its victims, with violation-grade [residue](/wiki/Residue) accruing throughout. The requirement to follow that path cannot be cited to them as though it made their continuing use adequately justified.

## Status along the path

- **Maintenance:** operating behind the frontier is unjustified wronging for the avoidable delay, aggravated where the maintainer built or profits from the structure.
- **Frontier exit:** the pace is required and blameless, while the continuing wrong remains fully answerable.
- **Acceleration beyond the frontier:** ending the practice faster by abandoning or otherwise wronging dependent parties is unjustified toward them.

Feasibility is claim-relative. A faster path is infeasible for this purpose only where it would wrong someone, not where it is expensive, inconvenient, or politically costly to the arrangement's beneficiaries. Those beneficiaries owe transition financing as residue rather than charity.

## Audit and recurrence

The frontier must advance as circumstances and provision change. Repeated claims that faster exit is infeasible require renewed evidence, and the finding may not be certified by the parties benefiting from continuation. An arrangement that can provide transition support and declines to do so is manufacturing the necessity it invokes.

The analysis generalizes beyond a single application. It governs institutions leaving entrenched exploitative arrangements, employers exiting supply structures they helped create, and public systems whose abrupt change would wrong parties made dependent on their operation. The verdict remains in force throughout; the operational question is which exit path the claims permit.

## Limits

- The participation bridge identifies a structural relation; it does not by itself establish knowledge, culpability, an available exit path, or the empirical effect of a transaction.
- The frontier exists only inside a genuine forced set. Transition costs that can be adequately justified do not establish it.
- Comparison may tie or fail to rank exit paths; fair procedure and pre-committed rules then govern selection without erasing wronging.
- The module does not supply empirical transition plans or certify claimed dependencies.
- Beneficiary responsibility for financing follows the responsiveness and concentration analysis; its distribution among beneficiaries still requires institutional design.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) · [Risk](/wiki/Risk) · [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) · [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties.mdx

- Title: Conflicts Among Standing Parties
- Slug: Conflicts-Among-Standing-Parties
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Operational system
- Layer: operational-system
- Support: derived, defended, proposed, open
- Provenance: clarification, editorial
- Depends on: Six-Stage-Pipeline, Claim-Grounds, The-Holders-Good, Comparison-Discipline, Risk, Necessity, Enforcement, Standing-Answerability

````mdx
# Conflicts Among Standing Parties

## Summary

**Conflicts among standing parties** are cases where [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) must answer more than one existing [someone](/wiki/Someone) at once: animals and keepers, workers and consumers, citizens and officials inside institutions, movements and wrongdoers, pregnant people and family members, officials, or communities claiming authority over reproduction. The framework does not resolve these cases by treating one side as if it lacked [standing](/wiki/Standing), merging the parties into a single aggregate, or ranking the worth of their lives. It keeps each party in view as a distinct addressee.

This synthesis gathers the modules that govern such cases. Conflict does not cancel standing, and standing alone does not supply a decision procedure. The [six-stage pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline) keeps identification, content, mapping, comparison, classification, and residue distinct; [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) supplies a partial decision procedure without summing someones into a higher claimant.

This page adds no independent conflict rule. It synthesizes rules whose support statuses remain those of their source modules. The remaining comparison gaps are the placement of the relevance band and the graver-versus-more-numerous open cell.

## Fixed constraints

Before any domain-specific rule applies, the framework keeps four distinctions in force:

| Distinction | Effect in conflict |
|---|---|
| Standing and conduct | A party does not lose standing by being weak, silent, dependent, implicated, costly, inconvenient, or wrong. [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) is the limiting case. |
| Arrangements and lives | Practices, institutions, and policies may be condemned without rendering a verdict on the worth of any life inside them. [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) supplies this rule. |
| Parties and aggregates | Welfare facts inform the content and gravity of holders' claims, but a welfare total is not a new claimant. Only claims of identifiable someones may be cited against another claim, and the account remains owed separately to each holder left unsatisfied. |
| Existing and merely possible beings | Existing someones hold present claims. Merely possible someones do not, because there is no one yet to whom anything can be owed. [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) applies this asymmetry to policy. |

The practical result is not immunity for any party. Wrongdoers may be stopped, arrangements may be ended, and institutions may enforce standards. The constraint is that the response must remain answerable to the standing of each existing someone it affects.

## Standing is equal; claims are not interchangeable

Equal standing means each someone must be answered to. It does not mean identical treatment, identical claims, or equal priority in every case. A child, an animal, a worker, a wrongdoer, and a pregnant person all have standing; what each is owed depends on the kind of being they are, the relation at issue, and the way the conflict is produced.

Sentience supplies scope: it identifies who cannot be dismissed. It does not supply instruction: by itself, it does not say what may be done about every being who can suffer. Once a party is inside the framework's scope, the further question is relational and practical — whether the party is being owned, governed, protected, stopped, used, rescued, exposed, or made to carry another project.

The framework therefore distinguishes standing from claim-content. It can say, without contradiction, that wrongdoers retain standing and may still be stopped; that animals hold standing and yet human reproductive conclusions do not follow downward from the animal case; that workers inside condemned arrangements are owed transition rather than contempt; and that a pregnant person's bodily jurisdiction is not overridden by a doctrine that leans against procreation.

## Recurring constraints

The applied pages use a small set of recurring constraints rather than a single conflict formula.

| Constraint | Use |
|---|---|
| Risk is not authority | [Risk](/wiki/Risk) gives prospective uncertainty directed due-care content and materialized harm new response claims. Neither a prediction nor later materialization creates authority over another party. |
| Provision before prevention | Where an existing person's hardship is at issue, improving that person's conditions outranks preventing similar people from existing. |
| Jurisdiction before enforced caution | The defended precautionary extension at [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) is not enforced by commandeering another someone's body. [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) applies this where fetal-status claims, demographic planning, family continuity, or antinatalist concern would have to operate through a pregnant person. |
| Standing against preference; standing against standing | A claim identified under [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) defeats a mere preference, convenience, institutional appetite, or taste. Where claim meets claim, comparison may become unavoidable and must preserve each holder as an addressee. |
| Stopping, not consuming | [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) permits only keyed, least-subordinating, terminating, welfare-bound, and answerable constraint; [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) preserves the source distinction. |
| Answerable transition | [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) requires immediate cessation unless every presently feasible path wrongs someone; only then does a necessity frontier govern. |
| Answerable enforcement | [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) requires claim-protection, adequate acts, an answerable enforcer, and an instrument that passes the operational pipeline. |

## Application map

| Area | Conflict | Page-level result |
````
