````mdx
|---|---|---|
| Beginnings and parenthood | A beginning creates no prior claim holder, but once a child exists the initiation claim is thick and answerability is distributed across initiators and those who assume care. | [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) adds defended premises to the beginnings machinery; [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) derives formation, truthfulness, and no-debt duties independently of that conclusion. |
| Animal use | Ownership-based use can subordinate animals, nullify contest, and extract benefit; keepers and dependent communities are existing someones affected by an exit path. | [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) derives its verdict where sentience and all three possession marks are established. Implementation is constrained by transition duties. |
| Reproduction | The framework defends antinatalism while denying authority to administer, appropriate, or compel continuation through an existing reproductive body. | [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) applies the competent-refusal rule and means-bound against antinatalist, pronatalist, population-control, eugenic, and fetal-status projects; indirect restrictions remain separately auditable. |
| End of life | A person's own continuation verdict can conflict with family, state, institutional, clinical, or public-cost judgments, while vulnerable people also need protection from external better-off-dead verdicts. | [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics) reserves the life-verdict to its holder, treats performed directives as binding exercises, and requires provision before facilitation where engineered necessity may manufacture surrender. |
| Provision policy | Existing people have claims to repair; merely possible people are not present claimants. | [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) ranks provision over person-prevention without ranking all provision claims against each other. |
| Labor and administration | Institutions coordinate real needs through arrangements people did not authorize and often cannot leave. | [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity) and [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) diagnose unanswerable control; [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) supplies the constructive standard. |
| Movements and wrongdoers | A cause may need to stop a wrong without converting opponents, members, grief, or purity into fuel. | [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) draws the stopping/consuming line; [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) applies the same refusal to purity and practical life. |
| Punishment | Institutions may need to protect existing people and answer wrongs without making the punished person material for a claimless total, spectacle, or institutional supply. | [Standing-Based Punishment Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics) admits prospective protection claims through adequacy and constraint, excludes claimless aggregate justification and possession, and leaves desert open. |
| Artificial minds | Candidate systems create uncertainty about the party roster while development also affects known workers, users, and publics. | [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) places candidacy at Stage 1; [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) requires answer-sensitive development without attributing sentience or treating candidacy as a veto over known claims. |

## Comparison without an aggregate claimant

The framework cannot avoid comparison across existing someones. Transitions, rationing, provision, and institutional design leave different claims unsatisfied under different options. [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) makes those comparisons claim-by-claim after possession and prior-rule filters have removed ineligible options.

The discipline proposes silencing claims below a relevance band against a graver claim and defends counting distinct holders where the claims left unsatisfied are of the same order. Counting does not assert cross-person compensation, and the answer to each losing party must remain pairwise. The equal-chances rival can reject counting while preserving separate standing.

Two gaps remain. No interpersonal metric fixes the relevance band's boundary. Where one graver claim faces more numerous lesser claims that remain relevant, no exchange principle determines when the number should prevail. Recurrent cases require public and contestable pre-committed rules, but adoption in advance does not prove those rules adequate.

Where comparison remains unresolved and time forces action, the framework uses fair procedure or a pre-committed rule and keeps pendency in the burden map. [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) still requires a separate keyed, party-preserving, claim-grounded, comparatively vindicated, and open address to every holder whose claim remains unsatisfied. Procedure selects conduct; it does not manufacture that address or erase [residue](/wiki/Residue).

## What this page is not

This page does not provide an adjudication algorithm for real disputes. It does not place the relevance band, solve the open cell, rank all provision claims, or determine whether force has crossed from stopping into consuming. Those limits remain where the linked pages place them.

The page also does not moderate the framework's condemnations. [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) can require an act while preserving that it wrongs its victim, and [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) classifies continued possession as necessity-justified or unjustified wronging rather than as clean conduct. A wrongdoer who retains standing may still be stopped. A jurisdictional firewall around reproductive bodies does not erase the framework's antinatalist position.

## Related pages

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) · [Six-Stage Pipeline](/wiki/Six-Stage-Pipeline) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) · [Risk](/wiki/Risk) · [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) · [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Exposure.mdx

- Title: Exposure
- Slug: Exposure
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Newness, The-Holders-Good

````mdx
# Exposure

## Summary

**Exposure** names the beginnings case of the [initiation ground](/wiki/Claim-Grounds): once a new someone exists, they carry a condition knowingly initiated by others and lived from a standpoint that cannot be delegated. The condition includes a body, dependence, a social and material world already underway, ongoing needs, and mortality. It is unchosen without being a missing exercise of consent.

Exposure is not an additional claim ground and not a second foundation. The initiation ground directs the claim to those who knowingly began the condition or deliberately assumed it; [Newness](/wiki/Newness) explains why no prior holder authorized or held a claim to the beginning. Together they identify an asymmetrical undertaking without deciding whether the beginning was justified.

## The condition

Exposure has three features relevant to the initiation ground:

- **Origination:** another's conduct knowingly began the condition, or another party deliberately assumed responsibility for it.
- **Comprehensiveness:** the condition is not one event within an established life but the setting in which that life first becomes possible.
- **Non-transferability:** the resulting someone must undergo the condition from their own standpoint; no initiator can carry it for them.

These features do not assert that the life is bad or that creation made its holder worse off. They identify the relation between the holder and the parties answerable for the undertaking.

## The claim

The argument is conditional and short:

1. [Newness](/wiki/Newness) establishes that no merely possible holder had a prior claim to be created and no prior exercise authorized the beginning.
2. Once a sentient being exists, that being is a [someone](/wiki/Someone) with [standing](/wiki/Standing).
3. Under the initiation ground, whoever knowingly initiates a condition another must carry, or deliberately assumes one begun, owes the claims of that undertaking.
4. Therefore the exposed holder has claims against those initiators and assumers once the holder exists.

The conclusion is derived given the initiation ground. Because that ground is a defended generalization of source material rather than a conclusion of standing alone, rejecting it removes the exposure claim without denying the holder's standing or the newness limit.

## Content of the undertaking

Exposure gives the initiation claim its beginnings-specific content:

- care governed by the holder's own good rather than the initiator's project;
- truthfulness about the condition, its origins, and the agents who shaped it;
- formation without capturing the standpoint that will later assess the relation;
- no debt, credit, or reciprocal claim founded on having initiated the holder's existence;
- an [account](/wiki/Account) that remains open to later exercises, contest, and revision.

This is answerability, not culpability. An initiator can owe the undertaking without the act of initiation having been shown wrongful. Nor does the ground guarantee that every later demand by the holder belongs to the claim; its content remains bounded by the relation, [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good), and the situation.

## Non-identity

The exposure claim is non-comparative. It does not say that the beginning made this holder worse off than the same holder would otherwise have been. It says that this holder now carries a condition knowingly initiated by another, and the initiation ground directs claims accordingly.

The non-identity problem therefore defeats one formulation the page does not use: comparative harm to a prior holder. A critic can still reject exposure by denying the initiation ground or insisting that obligations arising from beginnings must reduce to comparative harm. That dispute concerns the ground, not the internal validity of the conditional argument.

## Addressees and scope

Initiation follows knowing agency and deliberate assumption, not genetic relation alone.

- **Intending initiators** undertake the full beginnings relation where their conduct knowingly aims at bringing about the condition.
- **Knowing contributors** can incur claims proportionate to control, knowledge, and role, including truthfulness and access to origins without necessarily assuming parenthood.
- **Deliberate assumers** such as adoptive or step-parents can undertake the holding and formation relation without having initiated the life.

Exposure does not make initiators the authors of mortality, illness, history, or every later event. It prevents them from treating those universal features as though the particular undertaking created no relation at all. Separate impositions, holdings, exercises, and wrongs generate claims on their own grounds.

## Limits

- Exposure is derived only given the initiation ground; it is not a direct entailment of standing.
- The page does not determine when sentience begins in gradual development; that [sentience boundary remains open](/wiki/Open-Questions).
- It supplies no verdict on whether procreation is justified. [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) requires an additional defended principle.
- Nothing in the exposure claim generates authority over an existing pregnancy or another holder's body.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) · [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework.mdx

- Title: Antinatalism in the Standing Framework
- Slug: Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework
- Aliases: /wiki/Numean-Antinatalism
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended
- Provenance: source-framework, clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Exposure, Newness, Settlement, Means-Bound, Adequate-Justification, Enforcement

````mdx
# Antinatalism in the Standing Framework

## Summary

**Antinatalism** is the most contested position within [the Standing Framework](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics): the claim that **optional procreation requires a justification that is not available** — that no one may optionally initiate an unchosen, maximally consequential [exposure](/wiki/Exposure) that cannot be [settled](/wiki/Settlement) in advance in the name of the one exposed. Nume holds and argues this as a **defended position with an explicit conditional argument**. The framework's machinery establishes that beginnings cannot be authorized or settled in advance, that an [account](/wiki/Account) will be owed, and that no later flourishing, welcome, gratitude, or care can close that account on behalf of the one begun. The argument also requires a defended bridge premise, **origination anti-bootstrapping**, which denies that goods created together with their holder can by themselves justify originating that holder.

Three features distinguish it from better-known antinatalisms. It makes no claim that existence is a harm; it applies to fortunate and unfortunate prospective lives identically, and so cannot rank lives; and it binds only in the first person — it licenses no interference with anyone's reproduction and generates no claim over any pregnancy.

Derived constraints determine what cannot count as authorization, settlement, or a claim held before a new someone exists. The antinatalist conclusion remains defended: the inference is valid only given origination anti-bootstrapping, which the framework defends but does not derive. [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) supplies a separate upstream refusal of the framework's application to beginnings.

## The position

The claim: *no one may optionally initiate an unchosen, maximally consequential exposure that cannot be settled in advance in the name of the one exposed.* Its three operative terms:

**Optional.** Construed narrowly: an act genuinely open to the agent — neither forced nor foreclosed by circumstance. Reproductive lives are shaped by economic pressure, family and religious expectation, restricted access to contraception, and social sanction; beginnings that were avoidable in principle but not genuinely open to the person are outside the claim's scope. The claim concerns acts, never persons: where options were narrowed, criticism attaches to the [narrowing conditions](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives).

**Maximally consequential.** Not because a life can contain suffering, ends in death, or cannot be undone — each is true in lesser degree of decisions routinely and permissibly made for others. The distinctive feature is structural: procreation creates both the party and the entire condition in which anything can subsequently count as a good or cost for that party. [Newness](/wiki/Newness) also resists overstating this: many acts partially form the standpoint that later evaluates them, and procreation is the limiting case of that familiar structure rather than a metaphysical exception.

**Cannot be settled.** Imported from [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement): no reckoning can be entered in advance, in the initiator's favor, on behalf of the one begun. Settlement is not the whole issue. The sharper problem is whether the act can be keyed to the good of the one to whom the account will be owed, rather than to no one, to the initiator, or to other existing people.

## The argument from absent warrants

Unsettleability alone prohibits nothing — people permissibly open unclosable accounts in promising, teaching, and governing. The position's supporting argument is therefore not an argument from unclosability by itself. Its sharper claim concerns **un-keyability**: in ordinary unclosable accounts, the account can still be addressed to an already existing party's good; in procreation, the act creates the very standpoint to which the reason would have to be keyed.

More precisely, a warrant for the beginning cannot be received in advance by the one begun. No exercise of standing can receive it, because no holder yet exists to authorize or settle it; and no prior good of that individual exists for the demands-side of standing to serve. Timing, provision, care, truthfulness, and welcome can be keyed to the child once someone exists, and conditions can be shaped for whoever will exist under them. The origination of the carrier is the act whose warrant cannot be received in that way.

The argument asks where, if not from the one exposed, a warrant for this particular act could come from, and contends that the three candidates fail. The recurring premise doing the work is the framework's foundational commitment: considerations that answer to no one cannot warrant overriding the position of a someone.

**1. Impersonal value** — *a good life makes the world better.* The framework engages the strongest version, which invokes a widely defended asymmetry: the absence of a never-created happy life wrongs no one, while a miserable life harms the one who lives it. The framework grants the asymmetry and argues it undermines rather than supplies the warrant: the asymmetry itself says there is no standing reason to create happy lives for the sake of their happiness. Impersonal goodness, on the framework's terms, never converts into permission to impose an irreversible condition on the being created to carry it.

**2. Permissible risk imposition** — *we impose unconsented risks on future people constantly.* Granted; but the permissible cases alter conditions for people who will exist independently of the act, and can be accounted for afterward between existing parties. Procreation originates the affected standpoint, and for the origination itself no after-the-fact accounting between prior parties is possible. Mitigating the imposed condition lowers its costs; it does not address the missing warrant.

**3. Agent-relative value** — *the importance, to the agent, of having a child.* Personal projects legitimately receive extra weight in one's own deliberation — but not, on the framework's commitment, by making a non-consenting someone the irreversible instrument of them. The framework adds a dilemma: love for *this* child cannot justify the act, since it exists only after the act; what exists before is the desire for *a* child, a role awaiting an occupant — the structure examined at [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use), where the framework is equally explicit that role-formation alone wrongs no one. The dilemma shows the warrant is missing, not that the wanting is corrupt.

**What the argument establishes.** The three candidates are not meant as a loose inventory. They sort attempted warrants by their addressee, and within the framework that sorting is exhaustive: a reason answers to no one, to the one begun, or to the agent and other existing parties. Merely possible people hold nothing, so appeals to future people as such collapse, for present warrant, into reasons keyed to no one. A proposed fourth ground must still say whose reason it is.

On that sorting, the first route cannot answer a directed claim, the second is structurally unavailable before the beginning, and the third would require another party's claim or project to include originating the new someone as its means. The defended [means-bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) excludes that content from any claim; mere projects and preferences do not supply claims at all. Optional procreation therefore proceeds without a warrant receivable in advance by the one begun.

That yields a derived constraint stronger than unsettleability alone: no one may treat a beginning as already warranted *in the name of the one begun*. Expected happiness, later gratitude, loving care, welcome, and permanent answerability may be reasons the initiator gives, evidence within an account, and obligations the initiator assumes; none can function as prior authorization or as the child's-side verdict that the beginning was acceptable. Claimed in either form, the warrant counterfeits an unavailable exercise of standing.

A good-life threshold does not reopen the route. If expected flourishing functions as a benefit conferred by being begun, [Newness](/wiki/Newness) blocks it; if it functions as evidence that later care will be good, it bears on the keyable obligations after a child exists. Later endorsement may bear on whether an expectation was reasonable, but cannot supply antecedent authorization or independently establish permission, since the act helped produce both the endorsing standpoint and the goods cited. A permission rule that varies with predicted life quality would also violate the page's non-eugenic boundary.

## Origination anti-bootstrapping

The remaining step is stated as a defended bridge rather than hidden inside the warrant analysis:

> **Origination anti-bootstrapping:** In an optional act that creates both a someone and the entire condition in which anything can subsequently count as a good or cost for them, goods internal to that created condition do not, without a further independent person-directed ground, constitute sufficient justification to that someone for originating the condition.

A ground is **independent** where its person-directed force does not depend on the act's having created its holder and the goods or costs to which the ground appeals. The qualification matters. The principle does not assert that created goods are unreal, that expected conditions never matter, or that an act is impermissible merely because it produces the goods cited in its defense. Its target is narrower: using goods whose entire person-directed force arises within the originating act as sufficient warrant for originating their own holder.

The principle is defended, not derived. Its support comes from [Newness](/wiki/Newness)'s holder-dependent account, [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure)'s totality analysis, and [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement)'s refusal to let an arrangement manufacture the permission it needs. The breeding and built-mind applications exhibit the same anti-manufacture pattern, but those analogies do not derive the principle for human beginnings. Its live opponent holds that expected goods, legitimate agent-relative reasons, responsible risk assessment, and permanent answerability can jointly provide a defeasible, non-settling justification. That position accepts the derived constraints and denies this bridge.

The principle carries the argument's disputed normative weight. Stating the inference conditionally exposes that dependence; it supplies no independent support for the principle, and a reader who denies it loses the antinatalist conclusion without surrendering the derived beginnings machinery.

Conditional on the principle, the argument closes. Exposure places the initiation itself within answerability once its holder exists. [Adequate justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) excludes claimless value; the means-bound prevents claims of existing parties from containing the new party's origination as their means; and anti-bootstrapping prevents goods internal to the created condition from supplying the missing independent ground by themselves. An open account cannot fill the position, because justified and wrongful conduct can both open accounts. No initiation-specific justification remains, so optional origination is impermissible.

## Boundaries of the position

- **No harm claim.** The position nowhere asserts that coming to exist is bad for anyone or that nonexistence would have been better — judgments [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) says the framework cannot form. It applies to a life of unbroken flourishing exactly as to any other. [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context) separates it categorically from harm-based antinatalism.
- **First-person binding only.** [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) confines the position to conviction and criticism: the standard protects no claim held by the merely possible person whose prevention it would enforce, and bodily enforcement fails independently. [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) therefore supports no coercion, demographic management, or claim over existing pregnancies.
- **Structurally non-eugenic.** Because the claim concerns all beginnings equally and gains no strength from unfavorable forecasts, it cannot generate the judgment that particular kinds of lives should not begin; the moment a version of it varies with predicted life quality, it has become a different (and, on the framework's analysis, eugenic) claim.
- **Not contempt.** The position implies no criticism of parents as persons, no denial of the goods of family life, and no discount on anyone's [gratitude for their own existence](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt).
- **Not a binary.** [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) treats assuming responsibility for an already existing child as a standing alternative, not as an obligation: it realizes the desire for parenthood without initiating any exposure.

## Deliberative limit

The framework notes a structural limit on all deliberation about the position: those deliberating exist, and the party with the most at stake in any particular beginning cannot, in principle, be consulted. This is offered not as an argument but as a reason the question resists closure from either side.

## Objections

- **The gift objection** (strongest): beginnings do not belong to the vocabulary of warrant and justification at all. For a reader who accepts [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure), this is an upstream refusal of Exposure's claim that beginnings open answerability, not merely a downstream objection to antinatalism. Presented in full, without rebuttal, at [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View).
- **The anti-bootstrapping objection:** expected goods within the life, legitimate reasons held by existing parties, responsible risk assessment, and unconditional answerability may jointly justify an optional beginning without authorizing or settling it in the resulting person's name. This objection denies the defended bridge while preserving the framework's derived constraints.

The framework's reply to the second objection is origination anti-bootstrapping: none of the proposed components supplies the further independent person-directed ground the principle requires, and combining them does not change their source. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) records the premise and the remaining dispute.

Accordingly, the page does not classify antinatalism as derived doctrine. It classifies the inferential structure as valid conditional on all its premises and the final position as defended, because origination anti-bootstrapping remains refusable. A reader may reject that premise while retaining [Newness](/wiki/Newness), [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization), [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement), [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure), [Account](/wiki/Account), and every derived constraint they generate.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) · [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) · [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics.mdx

- Title: Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics
- Slug: Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics
- Aliases: /wiki/Numean-Reproductive-Ethics
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended
- Provenance: source-framework, reconstruction, application
- Depends on: Someone, Authority-Across-Time, Means-Bound, Possession, Constraint-of-Persons, Enforcement, Newness, Arrangements-and-Lives

````mdx
# Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics

## Summary

**Reproductive ethics** in [the Standing Framework](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) is a claim about **jurisdiction**: no project — demographic, familial, religious, economic, or philosophical — acquires authority over a person's reproductive body. Population shortfalls, family continuity, and labor forecasts may all be real concerns; on this account, none of them converts into a claim on anyone's fertility, because a person's body is not an instrument for ends that person did not set and cannot contest.

The position's distinguishing feature is that it applies in every direction. It treats pronatalist and population-control policy as versions of the same jurisdictional claim with opposite aims; it rejects eugenic selection without ranking lives; and it protects the pregnant person's decision from outside control, including control justified by [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework).

This is Nume's application of [the Standing Framework](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) to reproduction, including a restatement of the reproductive justice framework; [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context) credits that framework in its own right.

The conclusion is derived given the competent-refusal rule and the framework's defended means-bound. Direct administration, appropriation, or compelled continuation through a person's reproductive body is barred; indirect restrictions require separate analysis and are not possession merely because they burden choice. The argument does not require resolving fetal sentience because no claim, on the framework's defended account, includes another party's bodily conversion.

## The jurisdiction argument

1. A pregnant or potentially pregnant person is a [someone](/wiki/Someone) with full standing and present authority over their own exercises.
2. Against a competent present refusal, [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) bars administering something into, taking substance from within, or compelling continued appropriation of the holder's body.
3. No claim includes another party's conversion under the defended [means-bound](/wiki/Means-Bound). A demographic, familial, or fetal claim therefore cannot contain authority to use the reproductive body as its means.
4. Direct reproductive compulsion is consequently unavailable in either direction. Positioning, eligibility, advice, and other indirect measures remain subject to the ordinary tests for constraint, holding, adequate alternatives, and possession; they do not inherit permission merely by avoiding physical force.

The bodily rule is stringent but scoped. It does not claim that every pressure, condition, or social judgment is bodily invasion. It claims that competing goods cannot become authority to administer, appropriate, or compel continuation through the one body by which they would have to be pursued. A critic who rejects the means-bound or confines the refusal rule to narrower source cases reopens the conclusion at that exact dependency.

## Reproductive conscription

The framework analyzes demands on reproduction as a single structure appearing at different scales:

- **State scale.** A polity facing population decline that adopts natalist policy has converted a fiscal and institutional problem into an assignment against particular bodies: someone's fertility entered into public projections as the variable that balances them. The unstated remainder of "we need more births" is a claim about who will be expected to produce them.
- **Intimate scale.** Family expectation, appeals to a future self who will allegedly need children to have existed, the framing of children as old-age security, and cultural judgments of childlessness as selfishness exert the same structure without policy instruments. The framework emphasizes that these usually proceed from real love and carry no cruelty — which is why they merit analysis: the wrong arrives at the moment a hope hardens into a claim on another person's body, and it typically arrives unnoticed.

Two descriptive points accompany the analysis. First, the conscripted body is, overwhelmingly and as a matter of documented history, a woman's — the projections, judgments, incentives, and coercions have been built around women's fertility. Trans men and nonbinary people who can carry pregnancies meet the same structure, often intensified. The framework treats naming this asymmetry as part of describing the phenomenon accurately. Second, [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) directs the analysis at the conditions, not at individuals making reproductive choices under those pressures.

**Symmetry of the two policy signs.** Pronatalist regimes (banning abortion and contraception, incentivizing births) and population-control regimes (birth limits, coerced sterilization) are conventionally treated as opposites. On the jurisdictional analysis they share their operative premise — that reproduction is a collective lever, adjustable toward whatever total the collective requires — and dispute only its direction. Historically, both have been applied to the same populations, with the same constant: the body in question was treated as public material under both signs. Where the arrangement also subordinates central interests, nullifies effective contest, and extracts its benefit through that condition, the framework classifies it as [Possession](/wiki/Possession).

**Reproductive justice.** The framework explicitly restates, and credits rather than claims, the reproductive justice framework developed by Black feminist organizers: the right to have children, the right not to, and the right to raise children in conditions of dignity, held as one indivisible right. Its own addition is limited to the observation that the three unify because each refuses the same jurisdictional structure. The framework also acknowledges standing grounds for suspicion toward it: positions that lean against procreation have historically been enforced selectively against particular communities. Its answer is structural and appears in the next two sections — the position cannot rank lives and cannot be applied to anyone's body.

## The eugenic boundary

Selective judgments — that certain kinds of lives should not begin — are the jurisdictional claim in its quality-directed form. The framework's rejection of them is structural: [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) applies to all beginnings identically and gains no force from unfavorable forecasts; a position that strengthened with predicted hardship would thereby have become a ranking of lives, which [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) says the framework has no machinery to formulate. Its response to disability is accordingly [provision rather than prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention).

One scope line is drawn in bold: this boundary condemns public standards, policies, and social verdicts about kinds of lives. It does not audit the private decision of a particular person facing a particular pregnancy under medical uncertainty. That decision is protected by the jurisdictional rule below, and condemning eugenic policy confers no license to scrutinize it.

## Reproductive jurisdiction

On abortion, the framework separates two questions usually fused:

- **The metaphysical question** — when a someone begins — it declines, on record, as unresolved: a hard question on which conscientious positions differ, and one nothing in the framework requires answering. [Newness](/wiki/Newness) deliberately leaves the timing of the transition open.
- **The jurisdictional question** — who decides — it answers: the pregnant person, without remainder. Whatever moral weight anyone assigns the embryo or fetus, that weight cannot be converted into a third party's authority over the one body indisputably present and indisputably a someone's. Compelling a pregnancy to continue is the direct governance of a person's body by a project external to her.

This jurisdictional rule applies to [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) as well as to pronatalist or population-control projects. A moral view that defended bodily authority only when the person chose its preferred outcome would merely replace one external controller with another. [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) therefore denies that its own conclusions about procreation give it authority over any person's pregnancy or reproductive decision.

[Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) gives this result its operational form. Antinatalist, pronatalist, and eugenic coercion fail claim-protection where they enforce a doctrine rather than an existing holder's claim. Direct bodily administration or appropriation fails independently against competent refusal; a policy implemented through exclusion or conditioning must instead be tested for genuine alternatives, holding claims, proportionality, and engineered necessity. The route matters.

Two boundaries remain visible:

- **Caution and bodily jurisdiction.** [Someone](/wiki/Someone)'s rule of erring toward uncertain candidates for sentience is not applied by compelling another person to continue a pregnancy, because doing so would use that person's body to manage uncertainty about a different being. Jurisdiction precedes caution where caution would have to be enforced through another someone's body.
- **Conviction and jurisdiction.** The framework can hold an antinatalist conviction while defending every person's authority over their own reproductive decisions because the [enforcement gate](/wiki/Enforcement) assigns the two conclusions different practical roles. The antinatalist argument can guide first-person choice and moral criticism; it supplies no claim held by a merely possible being whose protection could authorize coercion. The coexistence remains a practical pressure, but not an unresolved comparison between two present claim holders.

## Judgment without jurisdiction

The jurisdictional refusal does not silence moral conversation about reproduction. The framework's line is the judgment/jurisdiction distinction from [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability): advice offered within a relation of mutual accountability — contestable, retractable, answerable to the person it concerns — is judgment, and legitimate. The same content installed as a standard the person must answer to, by an institution, community, or informal tribunal of opinion that answers nothing in return, is jurisdiction, and is what this page condemns. No legal apparatus is needed to cross the line; sustained social pricing of reproductive choices crosses it informally.

## Limits

- The position is conditional on the competent-refusal rule and the defended means-bound; critics who treat bodies as defeasible instruments for other parties' claims reject the framework at that point.
- The jurisdictional rule addresses authority, not metaphysics; readers seeking an account of embryonic or fetal moral status will not find one here.
- The precedence of jurisdiction over caution applies where caution would require commandeering a body; the page does not supply a general hierarchy for every conflict between caution and other claims.

## Related pages

[Someone](/wiki/Someone) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Gratitude-Without-Debt.mdx

- Title: Gratitude Without Debt
- Slug: Gratitude-Without-Debt
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, open
- Provenance: source-framework, application
- Depends on: Standing, Authorization, Settlement, Possession

````mdx
# Gratitude Without Debt

## Summary

**Gratitude without debt** names the framework's narrow result about gifts, beginnings, and return. [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) denies that existence can be collected as a debt, that gratitude can prove a beginning was settled, or that a gift may later be invoked as credit against its recipient. It does not deny gratitude. Freely given thanks, love's ordinary returns, and obligations grown within a shared relation all survive.

The distinction matters because one of the common misunderstandings of the framework is that it confiscates gratitude in order to protect its argument. The framework's claim is more limited and more severe: gratitude ceases to be gratitude when it is demanded as payment.

The denial of existence-debt is derived from the settlement prohibition. The treatment of existential gratitude that has no clear benefactor remains an acknowledged pressure on the framework and is linked to [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) and [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions).

## What settlement denies

The settlement argument denies one act: entering a closed reckoning, in advance, in one's own favor, in the name of a person who could not close it. That denial blocks claims such as:

- your existence puts you in my debt;
- my sacrifice for your beginning entitles me to your loyalty;
- your gratitude proves the beginning was justified;
- a gift I gave you may now be used as credit against you.

Each claim performs a prohibited settlement by treating the recipient as debtor, witness, or supporting evidence in the giver's account of themselves. It becomes [Possession](/wiki/Possession) only where collection subordinates the recipient's central interests, no effective channel can stop it for the recipient's sake, and the giver extracts loyalty, esteem, or support through the indebted condition.

## Gratitude freely given

Nothing in the argument prevents a person from being grateful for their life, for care, for rescue, for patience, for a home, or for the continued presence of those who raised them. Gratitude freely given is an act of the person whose gratitude it is. It belongs to the giver of thanks, not to the person who wants to receive it.

For that reason it cannot be demanded without changing kind. A thank-you can be welcomed; it cannot be invoiced. A return of love can be received; it cannot be treated as arrears. The framework's phrase "no debt" therefore protects gratitude rather than abolishing it: only what is not collected can remain a gift.

The same point preserves ordinary reciprocity. If someone keeps faith with another across a shared life, obligations may grow from that relation. They are not grounded in the bare fact that one party caused the other to exist.

## Gift, credit, and audience

The framework separates three things that are often confused.

**Gift:** something given without a claim against the recipient.

**Credit:** a claimed moral balance in the giver's favor.

**Audience:** the recipient repositioned as evidence of the giver's goodness.

A gift can become credit after the fact if it is invoked to close an account. It can become an audience relation if the recipient is pressured to testify to the giver's generosity. These are not defects in all giving. They are ways a good can be converted into possession after it has been given.

This is why the framework's dispute with [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) is precise. It does not deny that a person may experience life as gift. It denies that "gift" answers the question of whether the giver may claim anything from the recipient, or whether a beginning is exempt from answerability.

## The sentence the grammar strains to hold

The framework records one pressure it has not resolved: expressions of gratitude for existence that do not seem reducible to happiness, advantage, or thanks to a benefactor. A person may say, in effect, "thank you that I am," without meaning "I owe my makers" and without clearly addressing anyone.

The framework's vocabulary can translate part of this: the person is glad, the world is received as gift, no debt follows. The framework admits that the translation may lose something. That loss is listed at [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions), not treated as a refuted objection.

## Limits

- The page does not provide a general theory of gratitude, filial duty, or religious thanksgiving.
- It leaves [open](/wiki/Open-Questions) whether traditions that ground filial obligation in relation, lineage, or ritual rather than settlement are touched by the framework's argument.
- It does not settle the gift-view fork: whether beginnings belong to the vocabulary of answerability at all.

## Related pages

[Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) · [Adoption and Relinquishment](/wiki/Adoption-and-Relinquishment) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood.mdx

- Title: Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood
- Slug: Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood
- Aliases: /wiki/Numean-Ethics-of-Parenthood
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended, open
- Provenance: source-framework, clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Exposure, The-Holders-Good, Authority-Across-Time, Account, Settlement, Possession, Deception-and-Captured-Judgment, Made-for-Use, Gratitude-Without-Debt

````mdx
# Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood

## Summary

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) grounds parental obligation in [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure), not in the impossibility of [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement): whoever knowingly initiates a life, or deliberately assumes responsibility for one already begun, owes an ongoing [account](/wiki/Account) to the person who lives it. The account's deepest requirement follows from a structural fact about the relation — parents substantially form the very standpoint from which their child will one day evaluate them, their beginning, and everything else. The core obligation is therefore twofold: to form the child, as all parenting must, **without bending the child's judgment**; and to claim nothing from the child on the basis of the beginning itself.

The account distributes obligation across initiators, contributors, and those who deliberately assume the parental role. It is not a procedure, an ideal of detachment, or a rejection of family reciprocity.

The obligations are derived given the initiation ground and its application at Exposure. Because generalizing that ground beyond the source beginnings case is defended, the page does not present a complete theory of parenthood as derived from standing alone. Its open questions concern reciprocal obligations and the boundary between costly inheritance and captured formation. The obligations remain independent of the framework's antinatalism and apply to those who have or raise children whatever one concludes about whether to have children.

## The central obligation: forming without bending

All parenting forms a person: a child acquires language, habits, concepts, and evaluative capacities from those who raise them, long before being able to assess any of it. The framework does not treat this as a wrong — it is the condition of there being a person at all. The wrong it identifies is specific: shaping the child's evaluative standpoint *so that it cannot freely assess the parent*. [Deception and Captured Judgment](/wiki/Deception-and-Captured-Judgment) identifies the direct failure. The relation becomes [Possession](/wiki/Possession) only where a parental purpose subordinates the child's central interests, no effective channel can alter the use for the child's sake, and the parent secures a benefit through the captured condition.

Because formation as such is unavoidable, the obligation needs a three-way distinction:

- **Formation** — unavoidable and often enabling. A first language, schooling, moral basics: closures that are preconditions of the child's later freedom, not violations of it.
- **Inheritance** — legitimate depth. A faith, a craft, a culture may be transmitted in full seriousness, and refusing a deep inheritance may cost the child real grief. Costly refusal is not the mark of wrongdoing; things worth inheriting are hard to leave.
- **Capture** — the wrong. Transmission arranged so that refusal costs the child the relationship itself: dissent priced as disloyalty, departure as betrayal, the child's love held conditional on adopting the parent's commitments. The test is not whether leaving hurts but whether the parent has attached abandonment to it.

Two corollaries complete the obligation:

- **Truthfulness about the beginning.** The child is owed an accurate account of how they came to exist, including unflattering parts. A beginning curated into myth for the parent's benefit deprives the child of the actual history their self-assessment needs.
- **No claims from the beginning.** [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) means the beginning generates no debt; gratitude may be received but never collected, and the child's eventual judgment of the whole matter — including of the parent — belongs to the child.

## Distribution of obligation

Parental answerability tracks the knowing shaping of an exposure — agency and knowledge — not genetic contribution:

- **Deliberate initiators** bear the fullest obligation.
- **Knowing contributors** (donors, clinicians, surrogates) bear obligations proportional to their role and knowledge. A gamete donor, for example, may owe truthfulness and reachability regarding origins without owing a parental relation.
- **Those who assume the role** undertake the complete relational obligation by choice, having initiated nothing. Their position, including adoptive and step-parental cases, is developed at [Adoption and Relinquishment](/wiki/Adoption-and-Relinquishment).
- **Those who relinquish.** The framework distinguishes relinquishment from abandonment, and reserves its sharpest condemnation for arrangements that manufacture relinquishment by depriving parents of the means to keep their children. The distinction is developed at [Adoption and Relinquishment](/wiki/Adoption-and-Relinquishment), with the political constraint at [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention).

The gradation is one-directional: which addressees owe what varies with agency, knowledge, and deliberate assumption; the child's standing and the basic content of the initiation claim do not vary with whether the beginning was accidental or long planned.

Proxy decisions within the relation — medical authorization, schooling choices — are governed by [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) and [authority across time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time). The proxy must preserve the child's position as the party whose good governs and who will later be owed an account; a decision becomes illegitimate when it serves the proxy's project, manufactures the child's endorsement, or is invoked later as debt.

## What the account does not demand

- **Not a procedure.** The obligation describes a relational orientation, not an auditable protocol. The framework explicitly warns against converting it into continuous self-monitoring, which re-centers the parent's moral standing — the ledger reappearing as a ledger about openness. Most of what children are owed is care, honesty, and presence, none of which takes the form of account-keeping.
- **Not detachment.** Parents may want deeply — a child at all, a shared craft, recognition, resemblance. The framework locates the wrong not in wanting but in enforcement: converting hopes into standards the child must meet, or engineering the child so the hopes are guaranteed satisfaction, the structure named at [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use). Hoping, and grieving unmet hopes, remain fully legitimate.
- **Not a denial of the parent's burden.** The framework acknowledges that early parenthood can be experienced as an overwhelming claim on the parent's body, time, and identity. The initiation itself generates no counterclaim against the child; any claim running toward the parent or caregiver requires its own holder, addressee, and ground.
- **Not a demolition of reciprocity.** What the settlement result removes is exactly one thing: debt grounded in the beginning. [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) preserves gratitude freely given, obligations grown from the shared relationship, and love's ordinary returns; [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) preserves the framework's scope note about filial-obligation traditions grounded otherwise.

## What flows back

The denial of existence-debt creates no standing deficit in parents. A parent who kept faith remains a someone, and everything the framework forbids doing to someones is forbidden toward them, including by their children. A grown child may demand an account of the beginning on the child's terms; the child may not keep the parent as permanent defendant, grievance-fuel, or material for the child's self-account.

This is only a floor. It preserves gratitude freely given, obligations grown within the kept relation, and the parent's standing against use. It does not produce a general theory of legitimate credit, nor does it settle filial traditions grounded in relation, lineage, ritual, or other sources not reducible to the denied settlement.

## Hard cases the account structures

- **The child's challenge.** A grown child may demand an account of their beginning. The framework's requirement is structural: the parent owes truth and owes the child an intact standpoint from which to judge the answer — which rules out treating the question itself as ingratitude, and rules out managing the exchange so that the child ends by apologizing for asking. It does not require that the parent produce an answer the child accepts.
- **The request to stop.** A child may also decline the accounting — may ask the parent to stop justifying the beginning. Answerability includes this: the account is owed *to the child*, on the child's terms, and continuing to explain over the child's refusal converts accountability into self-exculpation performed at the child's expense.

## Limits

- The obligations are conditional on the initiation ground's defended generalization as applied at [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure).
- The formation/inheritance/capture distinction is a criterion, not a decision procedure; particular cases — especially deep religious and cultural transmission — will be contestable, and the framework supplies the question to ask rather than an algorithm.
- Community-structured exit costs remain difficult: a parent can preserve a child's formal permission to refuse while transmitting a way of life whose surrounding community makes refusal socially devastating. The placement of responsibility between parent, community, and institution remains open at [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions).
- The account gives only the floor of what flows back. A broader theory of legitimate credit and relational obligation remains undeveloped at [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions).

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Adoption and Relinquishment](/wiki/Adoption-and-Relinquishment) · [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) · [Deception and Captured Judgment](/wiki/Deception-and-Captured-Judgment) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Provision-Before-Prevention.mdx

- Title: Provision Before Prevention
- Slug: Provision-Before-Prevention
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, proposed
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Provision-Claims, Newness, Adequate-Justification, Arrangements-and-Lives, Comparison-Discipline, Necessity, Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures, Residue, Enforcement, Standing-Answerability, Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics, Infrastructuralization

````mdx
# Provision Before Prevention

## Summary

**Provision before prevention** is a political priority within [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics): where existing someones hold [provision claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims), an arrangement cannot answer those claims by substituting policies that prevent possible people from coming to exist. Its basis is an asymmetry of addressees. Existing hardship becomes a directed claim only through an imposition, holding, need, or provision ground; under [Newness](/wiki/Newness), merely possible beings hold no current claims, and preventing a person from coming into existence cannot benefit that person.

In disability policy, the priority directs institutions toward repairing withheld conditions rather than treating the prevention of possible disabled people as relief for those people. In transitions out of wrongful structures, it requires existing provision claims to enter the map, but [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures), not this priority alone, determines whether they create a forced set. Provision at scale is itself imposed through taxation, codes, and inspection, so its standards and instruments must separately pass [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) and remain institutionally answerable.

The priority is derived given an existing provision claim, Newness's account of merely possible someones, and the proposed claim-grounded condition of adequate justification. Standing alone does not generate the provision claim, rank claims among existing holders, or establish a transition or enforcement verdict.

## The asymmetry of addressees

Every claim to moral repair needs a party, an addressee, and a ground. Where an existing person's deprivation engages those conditions, remedy is owed *to them*; there is someone for whom the repair is an improvement. A policy of preventing future people has no corresponding holder among the people prevented: if it succeeds, no such person exists to be protected, and a life that never begins is a loss to no one.

Two clarifications fix the target:

- **"Prevention" means prevention of persons, not of harms.** Preventing harm to existing or expected people is itself provision. What cannot benefit the prevented person is specifically the subtraction of future people offered as the remedy for present or anticipated hardship.
- **The principle addresses policy, not private choice.** It constrains states, institutions, and planners. Individuals' decisions about their own reproduction are outside its scope entirely, protected by the jurisdictional arguments at [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics).

The priority is not neutral arithmetic. It depends on [Standing](/wiki/Standing)'s anti-aggregation floor and on the diagnostic rule that claims, rather than claimless totals, supply person-directed justification. A welfare-aggregating critic can hold that preventing lives likely to contain suffering reduces future aggregate suffering even without a beneficiary; on the framework's map, that rejects the directed restriction rather than exposing a beneficiary the policy serves.

## Disability: provision and prevention as opposites

Confronted with lives made harder by bodily difference, two contrasting policy orientations can be distinguished. These are ideal types rather than an exhaustive classification. One locates the difficulty in the person and responds by preventing people with that condition from coming to exist. The other locates the difficulty in withheld conditions — inaccessible environments, unfunded support, inflexible institutions — and responds by repairing them.

The Standing Framework treats these orientations as opposed at the level of justification, even though actual policies may combine elements of both: they assign the source of the problem and the object of repair differently. The first, generalized into public policy, is a ranking of lives, which [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) says the framework has no machinery even to formulate and which [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) analyzes as the core eugenic structure. The second is provision. Claims that certain lives are too costly are, on this view, invoices presented to the wrong party: the costs are real and are chargeable to the conditions and the arrangements that withheld repair.

The scope line drawn on the reproductive page applies here with full force: this analysis condemns public standards and policy postures. It does not audit private reproductive decisions made under medical uncertainty, which remain entirely the deciding person's.

## Transitions: provision inside exit

The framework condemns practices — animal ownership centrally — whose cessation can fall heavily on existing someones: those whose livelihoods were built into the practice and those for whom it is currently the only accessible means of subsistence. Their claims are not implementation costs. The arrangement and its beneficiaries can owe transition support under [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) and [Residue](/wiki/Residue).

If immediate cessation wrongs no one, it is required; if it creates only adequately justified burdens, cessation remains required and those burdens carry residue. Only where every presently feasible exit path wrongs someone does a standing [forced set](/wiki/Necessity) exist. [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) then requires the least-wrong feasible frontier while classifying continuing possession as necessity-justified wronging toward its victims.

Provision thus affects the claim roster and the feasibility of exit; it does not itself compare “destruction” and “relief” as totals. [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) governs the distinct claims, including its unresolved relevance band and open cell, and [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) governs institutions administering the transition.

## Demographic policy without conscription

The principle also answers the policy fear that most often motivates claims on reproduction: population aging, with fewer workers supporting more dependents. The framework treats the fear as legitimate and the reflexive remedy — increasing births as a matter of policy — as bodily conscription in the sense analyzed at [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics).

Its alternative is provision-shaped: redistribute the load rather than requisition bodies. Compensating care work as work, restructuring the institutions of aging, and admitting willing migrants are all available — with [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization)'s caution that migration policy which models people purely as labor inputs reproduces the supply-conversion at the border. These remedies are expensive and politically difficult; the framework's claim is not that they are easy but that they are contestable by the people who bear their costs, which requisitioning reproduction never is.

## The self-directed difficulty: provision is enforcement

The framework declines to present its own demand as innocent. Provision at scale is built by codes, funded by taxation, and enforced by inspection — imposed on people who never agreed to the standard and may reject the conviction behind it. A framework whose central target is the unaccountable standard must therefore either abandon its one political demand or distinguish accountable enforcement from the structure it condemns.

It chooses the second. [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) requires claim-protection, adequate instruments, an answerable enforcer, and a full pipeline analysis; [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) specifies the authority, review, and institutional design on which that answerability depends. Whether the safeguards work remains an empirical question rather than a conclusion licensed by the provision priority.

## Limits

- The priority depends on the anti-aggregation foundation; welfare-aggregating readers can consistently reject it by rejecting the framework's floor.
- Transition claims enter the ordinary comparison discipline. Its relevance-band boundary and graver-versus-more-numerous open cell remain unresolved.
- The principle ranks provision above person-prevention; it does not rank provision claims against each other, and supplies no general theory of distributive priority among existing someones.

## Related pages

[Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Comparison Discipline](/wiki/Comparison-Discipline) · [Necessity](/wiki/Necessity) · [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) · [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) · [The Gift View](/wiki/The-Gift-View)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Adoption-and-Relinquishment.mdx

- Title: Adoption and Relinquishment
- Slug: Adoption-and-Relinquishment
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended, open, empirical
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood, The-Holders-Good, Account, Provision-Claims, Provision-Before-Prevention, Possession

````mdx
# Adoption and Relinquishment

## Summary

**Adoption and relinquishment** clarify how [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) distributes parental answerability when the person who raises a child did not begin them, or when the person who began or bore responsibility for a child cannot keep the whole relation. The framework ties obligation to the knowing shaping of an exposure and to the deliberate assumption of care, not to biology alone.

An adoptive parent, step-parent, or other person who assumes the parental role may have initiated nothing and still owe the whole relation. A parent who relinquishes a child may, in some cases, be answering to the child rather than abandoning them. What the framework condemns without qualification is a social arrangement that manufactures relinquishment by depriving parents of the means to keep children they could otherwise care for.

The distribution of answerability is derived given the initiation and holding grounds. Applying it to particular placements remains empirical, and the legal allocation of authority is outside the theory. The claim that answerable relinquishment can transfer the parental undertaking without erasing every initiation-based obligation is a defended clarification.

## The one who began nothing

The framework's account of parenthood is not genetic title. Parental answerability tracks agency, knowledge, and the assumption of a role that forms the child's world. A person who adopts, joins a household as a parent, or otherwise undertakes the role enters the complete obligation because they now shape the child's exposure from inside the relation.

Their position is structurally distinct from that of initiators. They cannot say "I gave you life" because they did not. That absence is not a weakness in the relation; it removes one of parenthood's most dangerous temptations. What they owe is not repayment for a beginning but fidelity to a trust they chose to hold.

The obligation is renewed in practice rather than settled once by entry. To assume the role is to become answerable for how one keeps it: truthfulness, presence, formation without capture, and refusal to turn the child's dependence into credit.

## Relinquishment versus abandonment

The framework distinguishes relinquishment from abandonment. Abandonment is the refusal of answerability: leaving the child exposed because the child's claim has been treated as disposable.

Relinquishment can be different. If a person cannot keep the whole relation without failing the child, transferring care to someone able to sustain it may be the most answerable act available. In that case the parent does not erase responsibility by leaving; they exercise responsibility by refusing to hold as title what they cannot keep as trust.

This distinction does not sentimentalize relinquishment. It can involve grief, loss, error, and permanent consequences. The framework's point is narrower: the moral category depends on whether the act answers to the child or treats the child as a burden to be discarded.

## Manufactured relinquishment

The hardest criticism falls on arrangements that make relinquishment necessary by withholding provision: poverty, medical cost, housing precarity, legal exposure, family violence, disability discrimination, lack of child care, or other conditions that separate children from parents who could have kept them had support been present.

In those cases, the framework charges the arrangement rather than the parent first. A society that refuses the conditions of keeping and then treats relinquishment as private failure has presented the invoice to the wrong party. The relevant political principle is [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention): repair the conditions under which existing someones live before treating family separation as the solution.

This can also become a possession relation. A parent's attachment and a child's dependence may be made load-bearing for systems that save money, protect reputation, or manage risk by making the vulnerable absorb the cost. Whether all three marks are present depends on whether those purposes subordinate the parties' central interests, no effective channel can alter the arrangement for their sake, and the system secures its benefit through their condition.

## Answerability after transfer

Relinquishment and adoption alter roles; they do not make answerability disappear. The resulting division follows the grounds each party continues to instantiate:

- **The current parent or caregiver** holds the ongoing undertaking: care governed by the child's good, formation without capture, truthful stewardship of history, and answerability for present decisions.
- **The initiator** retains obligations tied to origin and earlier conduct that were not transferred: truthful records, appropriate reachability, an account of the beginning, and any support obligation that the transfer did not validly discharge. Initiation creates no title to contact or to the parental role.
- **The relinquishing parent** cannot cite the transfer as release from prior wrongs, but neither does the initiation ground by itself require continued relational performance after an answerable transfer. Contact is governed by the child's valid exercises and good, not by an adult's claim to recover the role.
- **The placing or supervising institution** incurs its own holding and imposition claims. It is answerable for coercive conditions, record loss, classification, separation, and the terms under which the transfer was made.

The framework denies debt grounded in the beginning. It does not deny gratitude, attachment, loyalty, or obligations grown within a shared life. In adoptive and non-biological parenting, what flows back, if anything does, cannot be collected as repayment for existence. It can arise only from the relation actually kept. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) retains the broader problem of trust, gratitude, and legitimate credit.

## Limits

- The page does not adjudicate custody, adoption screening, termination of rights, support allocation, or the legal structure of family placement. Its division of answerability is moral rather than a family-law rule.
- It does not assume that every biological parent can or should keep the parental role.
- It does not assume that every adoption is answerable; adoption itself can become a market, a rescue narrative, or a possession relation if the child is treated as material for adult purposes.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Parenthood](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Parenthood) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) · [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Mixed-Intergenerational-Cases.mdx

- Title: Mixed Intergenerational Cases
- Slug: Mixed-Intergenerational-Cases
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, open
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Newness, Exposure, Account, Risk, Standing-Answerability

````mdx
# Mixed Intergenerational Cases

## Summary

**Mixed intergenerational cases**, in [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics), are acts that both shape future conditions and help determine which people will exist under them. Climate policy, state formation, institutional design, reproductive policy, and large infrastructure can have this structure. A different act may not merely have given the same future people better or worse conditions; it may have resulted in different people altogether.

The framework's answer is that the same-person comparison is not the source of the claim. [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure) grounds answerability non-comparatively: the claim is not "you made me worse off than I otherwise would have been," but "you knowingly helped shape the condition I carry." Where a future someone comes to exist under conditions knowingly shaped by an earlier act, the relevant agents or arrangements are answerable to that someone once they exist. [Newness](/wiki/Newness)'s limit and Exposure's source can attach to the same act without sorting the act into only one category.

The identity-open answerability structure is derived given the initiation and holding grounds. The concrete content of institutional obligations before future holders exist remains open; the page specifies present disciplines on existing actors without treating merely possible people as current claimants.

## The problem

[Newness](/wiki/Newness) separates two relations:

- forming a context that future people will inhabit;
- creating the subject who will later inhabit and evaluate that context.

Mixed cases strain that separation because one act can do both. A policy can shape the world future people receive while also changing which people come to exist. A harm-based account may struggle because the affected person cannot be compared with a condition in which the same person existed without the act.

The Standing Framework does not need that comparison. Its answerability claim does not require that the same individual would otherwise have existed.

## The answerability structure

Three existing commitments carry the result.

1. **Exposure is non-comparative.** The claim concerns an unchosen condition knowingly shaped by another, not a loss relative to an alternative life for the same individual.
2. **The undertaking is identity-open.** The initiation ground requires knowing agency, not prior identification of a particular future holder. If a someone results, the agent becomes answerable to that someone for the condition knowingly helped into being.
3. **Arrangements can hold claims from people they form.** [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) applies the holding ground to states and institutions whose power reaches people they substantially form and who could not have authorized them in advance.

The conclusion is limited: an agent or institution that knowingly acts so that future someones will exist under conditions it helped shape owes those someones an [account](/wiki/Account) once they exist, in proportion to agency and knowledge. The identity-dependence that defeats some harm comparisons does not defeat answerability, because answerability is owed to the person who exists under the condition.

## Present force

The claimants arrive later, but the undertaking has present force. [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) is prospective: having reasons does not discharge the account. An agent who knows an account will be owed cannot treat the future addressee as irrelevant until they appear; the anticipated account must discipline present reasons, records, [risk](/wiki/Risk), and design.

This present force is not yet a decision rule. It does not say that every act whose later addressee cannot authorize it is prohibited, or that every unsettled account is forbidden. Applied verdicts require further premises about what would count as an adequate answer to the later party. [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) supplies such a premise for optional procreation as a defended position; this page supplies only the intergenerational answerability structure.

This does not make merely possible people present claimants. [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) still holds: merely possible someones hold no current claims. The present constraint falls on existing agents and arrangements because of what they knowingly undertake.

Consider a city choosing a flood-defense design that will shape settlement patterns for generations. Existing residents hold present imposition and provision claims; merely possible future residents do not. The city nevertheless knows that its design may help determine both who later lives there and the conditions those people must carry. Present answerability therefore requires a truthful risk map, preserved reasons and records, reversible design where feasible, and an institution capable of answering later holders once they exist.
````
