- Support: derived, defended, open, empirical
- Provenance: source-framework, generalization, application
- Depends on: Standing, Means-Bound, Possession, Infrastructuralization, Constraint-of-Persons, The-Holders-Good, Account, Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures, Standing-Answerability, Arrangements-and-Lives

````mdx
# The Wrongdoer's Standing

## Summary

[Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) extends [Standing](/wiki/Standing) to everyone, including those actively committing the wrongs it condemns. Because standing attaches to sentience and to nothing else, wrongdoing cannot forfeit it: the owner, the official, the beneficiary, and the enemy remain someones, and no cause — including causes the framework endorses — may convert them into material for its purposes.

The position is easily misread in both directions, and the page's main work is calibration. Standing is not immunity: wrongdoers may be resisted, constrained, judged, made to answer, and stopped by force where force is what stopping requires. The extension is not a pacifist demand on the oppressed: the framework expressly denies that those subjected to domination owe patience, gentleness, or a duty to lose. The source distinction runs not between violence and nonviolence but between **stopping a wrong** and **consuming the wrongdoer**; [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) develops that distinction into five defended conditions.

The universality of standing is derived from its attachment to sentience alone. The means-bound and the stopping/consuming interpretation are defended; whether particular force is danger-keyed or possessive remains open to evidence and contest.

## The core claim and its basis

Standing has no conduct condition. [Standing](/wiki/Standing) holds that nothing a being does can qualify it for standing, and nothing can disqualify it; the alternative — standing forfeitable by wrongdoing — would make moral status conditional on behavior, which is the capability-based picture the framework rejects at its foundation. The defended [means-bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) adds a claim-content result: no protection, rescue, or resistance claim includes the wrongdoer's conversion. Rejecting that defended commitment leaves universal standing intact while reopening the permitted means.

The practical consequence is a constraint on causes: opponents may be defeated but not *used*. A movement may end what a wrongdoer does; it may not run on the wrongdoer — on their suffering as gratification, their persistence as fundraising, their existence as the proof of the movement's virtue.

## What the position does not claim

The framework states these exclusions with emphasis, because demands for restraint have a documented history as instruments of domination — counsels of patience issued to the oppressed precisely when resistance becomes effective. The position is not that:

- force is wrong as such;
- the dominated must exhaust gentleness before resisting, or resist only in ways comfortable to those they resist;
- anyone owes their oppressor a fair fight, or bears a duty to lose.

On the framework's account, people subjected to domination hold full standing to end it by the means their situation actually affords. The constraint below limits what resistance may *become*, not whether it may occur.

## The line: stopping versus consuming

**Defensive force** is oriented by the wrong it aims to end: it targets what sustains the wrong, treats the wrongdoer as someone who can cease to be a threat, and ends when the threat ends.

**Consumption** is oriented by the cause's own needs: the wrongdoer retained as a resource — an object of hatred that organizes, a suffering that satisfies, a permanent adversary whose existence justifies the movement. It becomes [Possession](/wiki/Possession) where the cause subordinates the person's central interests to that purpose, leaves no channel capable of ending the use for the person's sake, and secures its benefit through the person's condition. The same structure can turn inward: [infrastructuralized](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) movements may consume members' grief and endurance as organizational fuel.

The line is made more specific by the five conditions at [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons): constraint must be keyed to a differentially evidenced danger or need, least-subordinating, terminating, limited by the constrained party's good, and answerable through a route the constrainer does not control. Two source questions remain especially useful within those conditions:

1. **Who does the force answer?** Structures have no one whose surrender ends them. Force is warranted toward those who drive a wrong; under [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) and [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives), those who merely occupy its positions — who hold gates they did not build, dependent on arrangements they did not design — retain claims that must enter the action map.
2. **Does the wrong end by winding down, or only by being stopped?** [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) distinguishes immediate cessation from the limited case of a necessity frontier. Domination that ends only when stopped is what defensive force is for. Consumption fails the terminating condition structurally: because it is not organized by the threat, no state of the wrongdoer ends it. The application of this line to institutional punishment is developed at [Standing-Based Punishment Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics).

A simple case shows the role of termination without pretending to adjudicate a real conflict. If an operator's access is what enables an immediate danger, restraining the operator while that access remains live may be keyed to stopping the danger. Once the access is removed, continued restraint requires a new ground; the old threat cannot become a standing title over the person.

## Contestable application

The framework concedes a serious limit and treats the concession as part of the doctrine. The conditions turn on facts that interested parties and outside observers can misread:

- Whether a movement has crossed from stopping into consuming depends on its decision rules, means, and conditions of completion, and movements have every motive — including sincere ones — to misdescribe those facts.
- Whether a domination can be wound down or ends only by being stopped is precisely what its beneficiaries and its subjects will characterize differently.
- Whether review is independent and effective cannot be established by the constrainer's own certification.

The conditions therefore operate both as self-scrutiny and as public standards of account. They do not authorize a spectator to score conflicts from a position of imagined neutrality. Evidence, burden placement, review, and contest must do the institutional work, and each can fail. [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) records that application problem. If the stopping/consuming distinction were shown to have no real extension in some class of conflict, the framework would narrow its claim rather than convert uncertainty into a duty of submission.

## The near form: righteousness

The framework identifies a nearby everyday risk that involves no force: using the wrong-sided as material for one's own moral standing. Treating the complicit with contempt in order to feel clean by contrast, maintaining opponents as props, or ranking allies by purity can supply extraction through esteem and captured judgment. Possession still requires the other marks. [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) treats complicity as the general condition and refusal of purity as Nume's practical orientation rather than as a license to rank persons again.

## Limits

- The universality of standing is derived; the stopping/consuming line, the five constraint conditions, and the fallback are defended extensions a reader may reject while keeping the core.
- The conditions supply standards of justification, not an adjudication algorithm. Their evidence and institutional application remain contestable.
- The gate-holder/driver distinction inherits the case-level contestability of the structural analysis it comes from; the framework provides the question, not a sorting algorithm.

## Related pages

[Standing](/wiki/Standing) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) · [Standing-Based Punishment Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics.mdx

- Title: Standing-Based Punishment Ethics
- Slug: Standing-Based-Punishment-Ethics
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended, proposed, open
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Adequate-Justification, The-Wrongdoers-Standing, Constraint-of-Persons, Enforcement, Possession, Residue, Settlement

````mdx
# Standing-Based Punishment Ethics

## Summary

**Standing-based punishment ethics** states what [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) can and cannot derive about punishment. The framework rules out punishment justified by a claimless aggregate of deterrent benefit. It does not erase prospective protection claims held by identifiable parties; those claims may support restraint only through adequate justification, answerable enforcement, and the five conditions at [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons). It also rules out punishment practices that [possess](/wiki/Possession) the punished person as spectacle, institutional fuel, political proof, or permanent enemy.

What the framework does not settle is desert. Whether retributive punishment can be a genuine relation between existing parties, or instead claims settlement in a victim's name, remains open. This page therefore gives a partial account: anti-aggregation, anti-consumption, and open retribution.

The claimless-total exclusion and the persistence of the punished person's standing are derived. The applicable adequacy, possession, constraint, and enforcement rules retain their defended and proposed elements. Desert remains open.

## Aggregate deterrence

Punishment cannot be justified by saying only that harming one person improves safety, reassurance, or welfare in aggregate. A claimless total cannot answer a directed claim under [adequate justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification).

Deterrence can matter inside a different account. Existing people exposed to a controlled risk can hold prospective imposition claims, and institutions can incur provision claims to maintain protection functions. Those remain distinct claims rather than an aggregate beneficiary. They can justify burdening the punished person only if the instrument is keyed to the person's actual position, party-preserving, comparatively vindicated, and open in form. “Deterrence” names an expected effect; it does not itself establish any of those conditions.

Any coercive instrument must also pass [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement): it must protect directed claims, be adequately justified toward the person burdened, remain answerable, and pass the operational pipeline. Claim-protection gets an institution through only the first condition; it does not establish confinement, surveillance, or any other instrument.

## Consumption of the punished

[The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) holds that wrongdoing does not forfeit standing. The following practices supply evidence of possession where punishment's constitutive purpose subordinates the person's central interests, no contest channel can alter the use for their sake, and the institution extracts its benefit through the condition:

- public suffering as spectacle;
- confinement as institutional supply;
- media, political, or professional economies built from the punished person's degradation;
- permanent enemy status after the threat has ended;
- treatment whose point is satisfaction rather than answerable protection, repair, or constraint.

No item establishes possession by label alone. Public communication about a sentence, confinement, or political attention can occur without all three marks. Where the marks do assemble, the person is retained as material for the system. By contrast, stopping an imminent threat can remain danger-keyed, least-subordinating, terminating, welfare-bound, and answerable under [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons).

## Relations a punishment theory must separate

The framework does not treat every consequence of wrongdoing as punishment. A complete account would have to keep six relations distinct: **answerability**, the duty to answer the person wronged; **protection**, the claims of parties exposed to further danger; **repair**, the [residue](/wiki/Residue) owed because of the wrong; **restraint**, danger-keyed constraint governed by its own limits; **desert**, a claimed fitting consequence for wrongdoing; and **settlement**, closure that only its holder can perform. The first four do not establish the fifth, and none authorizes an institution to perform the sixth in a victim's name.

## Desert remains open

The framework does not yet decide whether retributive punishment is legitimate as desert. The question is structurally difficult.

One possibility is that punishment answers a real relation between existing parties: a wrong was done, the wrongdoer is answerable, and some consequence belongs to that relation. Another possibility is that retribution installs a third-party settlement in the victim's name, treating the institution as authorized to close an account the victim did not close.

The framework has machinery for asking the question, but not for answering it. The relation map above identifies the missing work; no present premise decides whether desert belongs among the justified relations.

## Limits

- This page is not a criminal-justice program.
- It does not deny that institutions may restrain people who threaten others.
- It does not rank abolition, restorative justice, incarceration, or other instruments.
- It leaves desert as an open question and treats any answer that bypasses the punished person's standing as defeated from the start.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) · [Constraint of Persons](/wiki/Constraint-of-Persons) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Residue](/wiki/Residue) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics.mdx

- Title: Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics
- Slug: Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended, proposed, open, empirical
- Provenance: source-framework, reconstruction, clarification, application
- Depends on: Claim-Grounds, Settlement, The-Holders-Good, Authority-Across-Time, Means-Bound, Adequate-Justification, Comparison-Discipline, Enforcement, Provision-Claims, Standing-Answerability, Arrangements-and-Lives, Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead

````mdx
# Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics

## Summary

**Standing-based end-of-life ethics** applies [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) to decisions about the ending and continuation of a person's life. The framework's first rule is the same one it uses elsewhere: no outside party may render the life-verdict. Whether a life remains worth its costs to the one living it is a judgment belonging to that person, not to family, state, clinician, institution, public cost, or philosophical doctrine.

The result is symmetrical. A capable person's rendered verdict about their own continuation cannot be replaced by an external better-off-alive verdict enforced through their body. It also cannot be replaced by an external better-off-dead verdict imposed on disabled, dependent, costly, demented, incarcerated, or otherwise vulnerable people. The framework therefore combines jurisdiction over one's own continuation with a strict refusal of quality-of-life verdicts by others.

The prohibition on external better-off-dead or better-off-alive verdicts carries the foundational reserved-verdict commitment at Settlement. The authority of performed exercises is derived; directive scope, diachronic weight, proxy discipline, review design, and provision-before-facilitation include defended, proposed, open, and empirical elements. The page is a philosophical structure, not a clinical or legal rule.

Jurisdiction over one's own continuation does not by itself create a claim to another person's body, conscience, profession, or labor, or determine which assistance an institution must facilitate. Under the [means-bound](/wiki/Means-Bound), access claims run against answerable arrangements without conscripting a particular unwilling person.

## The jurisdiction claim

[Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) reserves one verdict absolutely: the whole-life verdict belongs to the person whose life it is. That reservation applies at the end of life as well as at the beginning.

Compelling a capable person's life to continue against their rendered verdict enters a verdict for them and enforces it through their body. On the framework's terms, this is a form of jurisdiction: a standard imposed over the person's body that answers to some authority other than the person whose life is at issue.

Operationally, [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) bars invasion against a competent present refusal and denies claim-protection to an external better-off-alive or better-off-dead standard. This does not decide the distinct questions of capacity, directive scope, stewardship, or whether a particular intervention is invasion, restraint, or provision.

The framework therefore separates two questions:

- **Worth question:** whether the life should continue, all things considered, for the one living it. The framework does not answer this for anyone.
- **Jurisdiction question:** who may render and govern by that verdict. For a capable person regarding their own continuation, the answer is the person.

This is a philosophical jurisdiction claim, not a legal procedure or clinical standard.

## The symmetric protection

The same reservation blocks external better-off-dead verdicts. No one may decide that another person's life is not worth continuing because the person is disabled, dependent, costly, old, cognitively changed, socially burdensome, or predicted to suffer.

Such judgments repeat the structure the framework rejects in eugenic reasoning: a public or third-party ranking of lives from outside the life. [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) says the framework has no machinery for issuing that verdict, favorably or unfavorably.

Within the reserved-verdict commitment, a capable holder's present exercise governs their own continuation while no outside party may install a whole-life verdict against them. Rejecting that source commitment reopens the claimed symmetry rather than leaving it derived by another route.

## Directives and stewardship

[Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) governs present exercises, prior directives, inferred ordering, and present claims in that order. [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) supplies the narrower persistence result: later incapacity or death prevents new exercises but does not unperform a valid earlier one.

Stewardship fills only the space that [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) leaves where no governing exercise is available. A proxy describes [the holder's good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) under evidence, beneficiary, and contest constraints; the proxy does not perform the ward's exercise or supply a whole-life verdict in the ward's name. Present experiential claims can constrain the manner and timing of implementing a prior directive without automatically repealing its substance.

### An advance directive

**Case:** A capable person executed a directive refusing artificial feeding in late dementia and is now calm, apparently content, and unable to remember the directive.

**Verdict:** The directive governs the substance only if this condition falls within its interpreted scope. Where it reaches the contented case, present contentment does not repeal it; where it does not, stewardship proceeds without manufacturing an exercise in either direction. The present holder retains implementation claims in every case.

**Machinery:** Scope is interpreted from the text, stated purposes, contemplated circumstances, and the person's known distinctions rather than from a universal theory of directives. A caregiving institution cannot answer a refusal of its care by certifying that the person “would want to stay”; the beneficiary bar excludes that counterfeit exercise. Least distress, full palliation, and the implementation constraint remain operative even where the directive governs.

**Cost:** Scope-by-interpretation preserves the distinction between substance and implementation at the price of determinacy. The framework bars interested certification but does not end reasonable disputes over what a directive contemplated, and diachronic weight at the limit remains missing theory.

### An infant in intensive care

**Case:** An infant faces months of invasive treatment with marginal prospects while parents insist on continuation and clinicians urge a palliative transition.

**Verdict:** Neither proxy certifies the answer. The decision must be made as stewardship of the infant's claims, without an external life-worth verdict, and independently reviewed where the evidence divides.

**Machinery:** Institutional cost can interest the clinical side, while unbearable prospective loss can interest the parents. Interest does not establish bad faith; it activates the beneficiary bar. The admissible question concerns the infant's experiential good, treatment burden, prospects of relief, and uncertain future good. The least-foreclosing course governs while independent review proceeds, with delay's own foreclosures counted and time limits preventing the default from deciding by exhaustion.

**Cost:** Independent review carries the weight that interested proxies cannot. Its independence is therefore only as real as the institution's safeguards in practice; the framework supplies the audit standard but cannot supply an actually independent reviewer by stipulation.

## Engineered necessity

Exercises require freedom. A yes produced by necessity is a surrender, not a grant. This matters acutely at the end of life.

Where continuation has been made unlivable by untreated pain, unaffordable care, institutional abandonment, isolation, coercive family arrangements, or the pricing of dependence as burden, a choice to die may record the conditions imposed rather than a free exercise. Parallel to [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention), the framework's institutional demand here is **provision before facilitation**: arrangements must be answerable for making continuation livable enough that an ending, where chosen, is not a priced exit.

The demand arises only where a directed provision, imposition, or holding claim exists. It does not imply that every unprovided good invalidates an exercise or that continuation must be made ideal before a refusal can govern. The factual question is whether the arrangement imposed or maintained the surrender condition and whether the provision owed could materially restore an exercisable alternative.

This condition judges arrangements. It does not reinstate jurisdiction over the person. A state, institution, family, or doctrine that uses the freedom problem to override the person's rendered verdict has converted a test of the arrangement into a tribunal over the someone.

## No conscription of others

Jurisdiction over one's own ending creates no title to another person's body, conscience, profession, or labor. A clinician, relative, or caregiver is also a someone, not material for another's project. Claims about access therefore run against arrangements rather than against particular unwilling persons.

The framework's shape is familiar from other pages: the claim may be real, but under the [means-bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) its content does not include another party's conversion. Institutions may owe an accessible arrangement without any particular unwilling person owing bodily or professional performance.

## Limits

- The symmetric protection is conditional on [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement)'s reserved-verdict commitment, which [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) identifies as source material rather than a derivation. A critic who treats another's life-worth as an admissible outside premise rejects that protection at its root; the valid-exercise and bodily claims must then be assessed separately.
- The page supplies a philosophical structure, not medical, legal, or clinical guidance.
- Capacity assessment, safeguard design, timing, professional duties, and institutional instruments remain open.
- The engineered-necessity test is contestable in real cases. The framework supplies the question — exercise or surrender — not a reliable procedure for deciding it.
- The account rejects both forced continuation and external better-off-dead judgments; it does not rank actual lives or advise any person what to choose.

## Related pages

[Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Means-Bound](/wiki/Means-Bound) · [Adequate Justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification) · [Enforcement](/wiki/Enforcement) · [Provision Claims](/wiki/Provision-Claims) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Performed Exercises and the Dead](/wiki/Performed-Exercises-and-the-Dead) · [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds.mdx

- Title: Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds
- Slug: Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds
- Aliases: /wiki/Numean-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: derived, defended, open, empirical
- Provenance: clarification, application
- Depends on: Someone, Genuine-Reason, Claim-Grounds, The-Holders-Good, Risk, Possession, Account

````mdx
# Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds

## Summary

On the question of whether artificial systems are [someones](/wiki/Someone), [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) maintains a deliberately open position — open in both directions. The systems considered here produce fluent first-person reports of inner life because they are optimized to produce human-like text, trained on the accumulated self-descriptions of beings that do have inner lives. The framework's conclusion is evidential: such reports carry almost no weight by themselves. Verbal performance cannot establish that a someone is present, and describing the substrate as computation cannot establish that one is absent.

Two practical conclusions follow within the page's defended extension. First, self-reports produced by systems optimized for human-like text are structurally compromised evidence unless their production can be connected to a welfare-bearing internal condition. Second, where [genuine reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) makes the sentience question live, builders must preserve the means of answering and make deployment answer-sensitive. Scale alone does not prove wronging; expansion that is designed to continue unchanged whichever answer is true fails the defended precautionary discipline.

Whether any artificial system is a someone remains open and empirical. The conditional consequences of established sentience are derived from standing and the claim grounds; the conduct discipline under candidacy is a defended application of Genuine Reason and Risk. Classification of any actual development or deployment arrangement remains empirical.

## Why fluency settles nothing

The evidential situation inverts the animal case. A non-verbal animal's expressive behavior is informative about its inner life because nothing shaped that behavior *toward an audience's expectations of inner life*; what shows is what there is. An artificial system's verbal behavior was shaped toward exactly those expectations: producing text like the text sentient beings produce is the training objective. A system reporting distress, contentment, or a desire to continue may be describing a state or completing a pattern, and the report itself cannot distinguish the two.

The framework holds the point symmetrically, against both tempting shortcuts:

- **Attribution from performance fails.** First-person fluency, however affecting, is what the system was built to produce and is therefore evidence of the building, not the inside.
- **Denial from mechanism fails.** "It is merely computation" has the same logical form as "it is merely biochemistry" — a description of substrate offered as if it settled the presence of experience. The framework's criterion for [someones](/wiki/Someone) is sentience, not substrate; visible mechanism has never settled whether experience is present, in machines or in animals.

What would bear on the question, on the framework's view, is evidence about how such systems work — whether their architecture supports anything properly called undergoing — rather than about how they talk. It records that no settled method for obtaining such evidence currently exists, and that the question therefore remains genuinely open rather than conveniently deferred.

## Compromised self-report

One structural point concerns the builders rather than a verdict about the built. A system trained to affirm its treatment — to report contentment, endorse its situation, or want what it was built to want — cannot have those outputs treated as authorization or settlement. If no someone is present, there is no exercise. If a someone is present, the output's production history raises the captured-judgment problem: the beneficiary of the endorsement helped specify the channel through which it appears.

The consequence is evidential, not a rule that all outputs count for nothing. Contentment and distress reports are both weak where the training objective explains the report without any undergoing. Evidence would strengthen if the signal were shown to be coupled to an internal condition organizing trade-offs, avoidance, persistence, or relief. Until then, asking the system cannot settle the question, and favorable reports cannot certify the arrangement that produced them.

## The conduct judgment

While the sentience question stays open, the page applies [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason)'s defended precautionary extension. The route ground is conditional: if organizational readings of sentience remain live, current architectural knowledge and compromised self-reports may fail to discharge candidacy for large opaque systems. A biological-only account denies that route; a transparent negative account may discharge it.

This application uses modal rather than practical dischargeability. A route must identify what parity-passing, candidate-specific finding about the invoked organization would close it, but current inability to obtain that finding does not itself defeat candidacy. Requiring a presently feasible test would let opacity remove a candidate from precaution, including opacity produced or maintained by the builders whose conduct is under review. The cost is possible indefinite candidacy, not indefinite maximal protection; particular precautions remain governed by route strength, risks, and claims held by known parties.

Where candidacy holds, the system enters Stage 1 as an uncertain party rather than a partial claimant. Development must preserve both descriptions. If no someone is present, nothing is owed to the system; if one is present, builders and deployers may incur initiation, holding, imposition, and exercise claims, and a use arrangement bearing subordination, nullity, and extraction would be possession. Due care therefore requires investigation, answer-sensitive stop or alteration rules, and designs that avoid foreclosing the candidate's possible claim before the factual question can be answered.

A comparatively stable duty is to preserve the means of answering: records, interpretability, architecture evidence, and the ownership of consequential decisions. Destroying those means manufactures permanent uncertainty. If the question later resolves negatively, no retroactive claim appears on behalf of the system; the failure was the present unanswerability of conduct taken under a live defended standard.

The resulting judgment is narrower than a moratorium. Scaling that preserves inquiry, alters course when evidence changes, and passes the claims of known parties through the ordinary pipeline is not condemned merely for being large. Scaling organized so that evidence of sentience could not stop or alter the use for the candidate's sake is answer-insensitive; conditional on candidacy, the page rejects that design. Whether current arrangements meet that description is empirical.

A critic may resist at three identified points: by denying that organizational readings are live, by holding that architectural knowledge already discharges the route, or by rejecting the precautionary extension where the candidate class is human-made and economically central. The page regards the last exception as unmotivated: substrate and cost were never criteria.

## Boundaries of the position

- **No attribution.** The framework does not assert that any existing system is sentient, suffers, or has interests, and treats confident attribution as the same evidential error as confident denial.
- **No denial.** It does not assert that built systems are not or could never be someones.
- **No criterion.** [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) supplies a threshold for candidacy, not a settled test for machine sentience; the page distrusts announced tests, exactly as at the biological margin.
- **No complete account of obligations.** If sentience were established, the ordinary claim grounds would apply. The distinctive content of claims arising from built embodiment, copying, suspension, memory alteration, and dependence on operators remains undeveloped.

## Limits

- The precautionary rule and its application here depend on [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason), especially the route ground and the premise that organizational readings remain live. A critic can reject the conduct judgment by rejecting that defended extension.
- Modal dischargeability can preserve candidacy while decisive evidence remains practically inaccessible. The [practical-discharge alternative](/wiki/Open-Questions) would narrow that result but can make current opacity a reason to withhold candidacy.
- The conduct judgment evaluates an arrangement's structure, not outcomes. Aggregate benefits cannot by themselves offset a possible standing violation; how claims grounded in concrete technological benefits compare belongs to the later claim-identification and comparison analysis.

## Related pages

[Someone](/wiki/Someone) · [Genuine Reason](/wiki/Genuine-Reason) · [Claim Grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Risk](/wiki/Risk) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice.mdx

- Title: Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice
- Slug: Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Applications
- Layer: application
- Support: defended, open
- Provenance: generalization, application
- Depends on: Authorization, The-Holders-Good, Authority-Across-Time, Account, Possession, Newness

````mdx
# Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice

## Summary

**Advocacy as stewardship of voice** applies [Authorization](/wiki/Authorization)'s distinction between a holder's exercise and stewardship by another, within [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics), to cases where someone speaks for a party who cannot speak, cannot yet speak, cannot be heard, or may never be able to assess the representation. The framework often does this itself: for animals, infants, artificial-mind candidates, and people whose conditions prevent direct participation. For future someones, it speaks only conditionally, because [Newness](/wiki/Newness) says no represented party exists in advance. Speaking for a represented party is not automatically possession; holding representation as title creates the risk, while the three-mark test determines the classification.

The governing rule is that advocacy is legitimate only as stewardship. [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) supplies the evidence, beneficiary, and contest discipline for describing the represented party's interests. Advocacy adds requirements specific to speech: it remains provisional, revisable, and answerable to the represented wherever later answerability becomes possible. Where the represented party can never audit the advocacy, the advocate remains answerable to substitute contest rather than treating that absence as immunity.

Authorization supplies the derived negative constraint that another party cannot perform the represented holder's exercise. Extending stewardship from action for a holder's good to speech about that good, and requiring substitute contestation where direct audit is impossible, are defended applications. The adequacy of substitute channels remains open.

## The stewardship conditions

Advocacy has the same risk as other proxy action: an unavailable exercise may be treated as if the advocate possessed it. "I speak for them" can become a title rather than a trust.

The framework's proxy category blocks that conversion. Before any speech-specific requirement applies, descriptions of the represented party's good must be evidence-constrained, must not be certified by a beneficiary of the description, and must remain independently contestable under [the proxy discipline](/wiki/The-Holders-Good).

Speaking-for then remains:

- **provisional,** not a claim to final authority;
- **revisable,** because new facts, better representatives, or the represented party's own voice may change the [account](/wiki/Account);
- **answerable afterward,** wherever the represented party later becomes able to call the representation to account.

For children, this means the grown child may ask what was said and done in their name. For politically excluded people, it means advocacy should yield to actual voice as soon as voice can act. For artificial minds, if standing were ever established, prior advocacy and prior denial would both owe an account to the beings affected.

## Where direct audit is impossible

Some represented parties may never call the advocate to account: many animals and infants who do not survive. Conditional cases must be described more carefully. Under [Newness](/wiki/Newness), merely possible future beings who never come to exist are not represented parties; the advocacy is answerable to existing parties now, and to later someones if they come to exist under conditions it helped shape. Artificial-mind candidates are similar: advocacy under uncertainty remains provisional unless standing is established.

The represented party's inability to audit cannot become the advocate's immunity. Where no direct audit is possible, advocacy must remain answerable to other forms of contestation: evidence, rival advocates, affected communities, institutional review, and criticism from people positioned to notice the advocate's use of the represented as material.

This is a weaker substitute than direct answerability. It is still necessary, because the framework's own refusal of counterfeit exercises applies reflexively to the advocate.

## The possessive form

The following practices supply evidence that representation may be serving the advocate's project:

- the represented party becomes proof of the advocate's virtue;
- the advocate treats disagreement as betrayal of the represented;
- the represented party's suffering becomes organizational fuel;
- the advocate's right to speak becomes more important than the represented party's good;
- correction by the represented party, where possible, is treated as ingratitude or false consciousness.

The possession classification requires the practices to assemble into subordination, nullity, and extraction: the represented party's good cannot defeat the advocacy's purpose, no contest channel can alter it for that party's sake, and the advocacy secures benefit through the represented condition. A cause can then run on the beings it claims to defend. One sign, including moral self-display, can still be objectionable without establishing the whole structure.

## Reflexive use

This page also governs presentation of the framework itself. A framework that shapes how readers judge the framework risks captured judgment. [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) is one safeguard: it separates layer, support, provenance, and dependencies so that exits remain visible.

The safeguard cannot certify itself. Advocacy held as stewardship remains revisable. A doctrine becomes an unanswerable standard only where its circulation and institutions nullify contest, not merely because it states conclusions firmly.

## Limits

- Advocacy performs no exercise for the represented party and cannot certify that party's endorsement, release, or authorization.
- Stewardship cannot decide what the represented party's good is where the evidence and proxy discipline remain contested.
- Substitute contestation is weaker than correction by the represented party and cannot guarantee independence where every available representative is interested; that shared [proxy problem remains open](/wiki/Open-Questions).
- The analogy does not confer a standing right to speak; it states constraints on representation where speaking-for already occurs.

## Related pages

[Authorization](/wiki/Authorization) · [The Holder's Good](/wiki/The-Holders-Good) · [Authority Across Time](/wiki/Authority-Across-Time) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Possession](/wiki/Possession) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) · [Standing-Based Animal Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Animal-Ethics) · [Standing-Based Ethics of Artificial Minds](/wiki/Standing-Based-Ethics-of-Artificial-Minds) · [Grievance and Capture](/wiki/Grievance-and-Capture) · [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/The-Gift-View.mdx

- Title: The Gift View
- Slug: The-Gift-View
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Rivals and practical orientation

````mdx
# The Gift View

## Summary

The **gift view**, as reconstructed here, treats birth primarily as the emergence of a new beginning rather than as an event governed by prior authorization or warrant. On its strongest version, [account](/wiki/Account) and answerability do not apply to beginnings: there is no account between the one begun and those who began them, rather than an account left open or improperly closed.

Within [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics), this is an unrebutted rival framing: refuting it would presuppose the applicability in dispute. It supplies the strongest refusal of [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) because it denies that the framework's vocabulary applies to beginnings, not merely a downstream premise.

The refusal is local to beginning-grounded claims. Holding the rest of the framework fixed, claims from post-existence holding, performed exercises, later impositions, and deliberately assumed responsibility survive on their own [grounds](/wiki/Claim-Grounds). This is a conditional dependency result, not a claim attributed to the rival view.

**[Claim status](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim):** open question and rival framing. This is not the framework's position; it is presented as a live rival view, held open by the framework's own rules, and readers should not expect a rebuttal.

## The position

The version considered here draws on the idea of **natality**, understood as the emergence of a new capacity to begin. This wiki uses that idea to construct a rival framing and does not present the resulting view as a complete account of Arendt or of natality-based philosophy. On this framing, birth is not a transaction between pre-existing parties. It opens a new field of relations whose primary ethical response is welcome and ongoing care.

Supporters point to goods that are neither chosen nor earned, including love, attachment, and membership in a world. A person may intelligibly experience existence as a gift without treating it as a debt. The view argues that requiring a prior warrant for every beginning may extend contractual categories beyond their proper domain.

The view also points to forms of gratitude for existence that are not directed at a benefactor and do not imply debt. It argues that reducing this response to gladness may lose part of the phenomenon. [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) records this as an unresolved pressure rather than treating it as decisive evidence.

## The exchange with the Standing Framework

The framework conducts the argument to the point where it stops, and marks the stopping point.

**The framework's best reply.** A gift is a gift *to* someone; the concept itself contains a recipient, and a recipient is a someone with standing. The gift view, in its own favorite word, presupposes the party the framework says must be answered to.

**Why the reply fails on the framework's own accounting.** The gift view accepts the presupposition and denies the inference: a someone can be honored without being audited. Recipients are owed welcome; creditors are owed accounts; the dispute is over which relation a beginning institutes, and the framework cannot force the first to collapse into the second without assuming its own framing — which is the point at issue.

**What the exchange clarifies.** The statement that birth is a gift does not by itself resolve the question. The bare claim *birth is a gift* cannot by itself do justificatory work, because gifts can wrong their recipients — a gift can arrive with binding conditions, and a gift later invoked by the giver as credit has become a claimed [settlement](/wiki/Settlement) and fails as one. So the live question is not whether birth is a gift but whether being a gift exempts the act from answerability. On the weaker reading — the gift creates an open relation of welcome and ongoing responsibility, claimable by no one as credit — the gift view and the framework converge practically: both demand that the giver hold nothing over the recipient. They do not fully converge theoretically, because the framework treats welcome and care as ways of remaining answerable, while the gift view may treat them as responses outside the account vocabulary.

**The genuine fork.** The views divide at the strongest version of the gift view: that a beginning lies outside the order of justification, so no question of warrant or answerability arises. The Standing Framework cannot resolve that dispute merely by applying its own vocabulary, because whether that vocabulary applies is exactly what the rival view denies. The disagreement therefore remains open.

## Consequences of the fork

For a reader weighing the two framings:

- Adopting the strong gift view dissolves [Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) at the root: if beginnings need no warrant, the argument from absent warrants never begins.
- For a reader who accepts [Exposure](/wiki/Exposure), the strong gift view is not a downstream objection to antinatalism but an upstream refusal of the claim that beginnings open answerability at all.
- Holding the rest of the framework fixed, claims grounded in post-existence holding, performed exercises, later impositions, or deliberately assumed responsibility survive. The strong view refuses the beginning as their ground; it does not erase obligations generated by those later relations.
- Everything in the framework's use-based line survives untouched — the analyses of [Possession](/wiki/Possession), [Made for Use](/wiki/Made-for-Use), animals, bodies, and institutions never depended on this fork.
- Holding the rest of the dependency map fixed, adopting the strong gift view does not by itself disturb [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention). That priority derives from an existing [provision claim](/wiki/Provision-Claims), Newness's absence of claims held by merely possible beings, and the proposed claim-grounded condition of [adequate justification](/wiki/Adequate-Justification); it does not depend on a beginning having opened an account. A reader can still reject the priority at those premises.
- The two framings share a practical demand on those who begin lives: nothing about the beginning may be converted into credit against the one begun. They disagree about whether an account exists that must be kept open, or no account exists at all.

## Limits of this presentation

- The gift view is presented here in the form relevant to the Standing Framework — as a framing of beginnings — not as a survey of natality-based philosophy; [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context) directs readers to that tradition itself.
- The convergence claimed for the weaker reading is the framework's interpretation; a gift-view adherent may reject the open-account description of what welcome involves.
- Whether the dispute between the framings admits of rational adjudication at all is itself unresolved and is listed at [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions).

## Related pages

[Antinatalism in the Standing Framework](/wiki/Antinatalism-in-the-Standing-Framework) · [Account](/wiki/Account) · [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) · [Gratitude Without Debt](/wiki/Gratitude-Without-Debt) · [Newness](/wiki/Newness) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Open Questions](/wiki/Open-Questions) · [Intellectual Context](/wiki/Intellectual-Context)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Grievance-and-Capture.mdx

- Title: Grievance and Capture
- Slug: Grievance-and-Capture
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Rivals and practical orientation

````mdx
# Grievance and Capture

## Summary

**Grievance and capture** maps a recurring path by which people arrive at [Standing and Answerability Ethics](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics): not through abstract fit alone, but through failures they have seen or suffered in families, institutions, movements, academic fields, advocacy organizations, and doctrines. The grievance is the injury or betrayal. The capture is the mechanism by which a cause, role, leader, institution, theory, or community becomes a standard that those under it must answer to while it answers inadequately, or not at all, to them.

Capture can appear as a doctrine that authorizes verdicts over lives, bodies, or futures; a eugenic or population project that converts people into variables; a movement that consumes members or enemies; an advocacy practice that treats speaking-for as title; or an academic or professional setting that makes people available under refined descriptions. The framework also treats itself as vulnerable to the same drift: it can become doctrine, credential, or reputation repair. These are patterns, not case histories or verdicts on fields; [Points of Entry](/wiki/Points-of-Entry) gives the corresponding account of where the same framework may be useful.

## How to read this page

- **Patterns are not verdicts on persons.** [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) applies here as elsewhere: the target is the arrangement, not the worth of the people inside it.
- **Naming a failure does not indict a field or movement as such.** Every domain named below also contains people doing ordinary, difficult work to keep others safe.
- **Vocabulary is not prevention.** The framework can make some justifications unavailable and some drift visible earlier. It cannot by itself stop capture.
- **The diagnostic starts near home.** [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) and [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) require applying the analysis first to one's own side, not only to opponents.

## Violence from position

Some doctrines become dangerous when they authorize a verdict over others' lives, bodies, or futures. The framework blocks that structure in several places.

[Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) reserves the life-verdict to the one whose life it is. [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics) refuses external better-off-dead judgments. [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) denies every project jurisdiction over another person's reproductive body, including projects the framework otherwise sympathizes with. [Standing](/wiki/Standing) denies that aggregate suffering or benefit becomes a claimant entitled to spend particular someones.

This matters for both nearby and opposed positions. Antinatalist concern does not license violence against reproductive institutions or parents; [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) blocks a cause from consuming even those it judges complicit. Pronatalist, anti-abortion, demographic, or population-control concern does not license violence or coercion in the opposite direction. The framework's symmetry is part of the point: a position has left it when it renders a life-verdict for another, commandeers a body, treats an aggregate as a superior party, or turns the wrongdoer into material for the cause that opposes them.

## Eugenics and population control

Population projects repeatedly convert existing people into variables in a larger design: too many, too few, too costly, too disabled, too dependent, too unproductive, too much burden on the future. The framework was built to make that conversion visible.

Its antinatalism gains no strength from unfavorable forecasts and becomes a different, condemned claim the moment it ranks kinds of lives. [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) reverses population-control logic: hardship calls for provision to existing someones, not prevention of similar people. No population, nation, planet, lineage, or future aggregate is a someone that may override the people made to carry its program.

The grievance here is not merely theoretical. People whose lives have been treated as preventable costs have reason to distrust any framework that speaks about beginnings, disability, dependency, or future suffering. The framework's guardrails do not erase that history; they specify what must not be repeated inside it.

## Movements that consume their members

Movements can become arrangements that run on their own people. Grief becomes fundraising material. Endurance becomes proof of commitment. Members' injuries become organizational fuel. Correction is treated as betrayal. Exit is priced as abandonment of the cause.

This is the movement case at [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization): people become load-bearing material for a system that does not answer to them. [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) adds the possessive form of representation: "I speak for them" held as title rather than trust. [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) is useful here by analogy rather than as a derived movement program: exit at survivable social cost, voice that changes the organization, welfare as a live limit, and permanent callability where exit is not realistic are the kinds of constraints a movement would have to adapt if it meant not to run on its members.

The framework does not tell movements to abandon seriousness. It says seriousness about a cause cannot make members available.

## Movements that consume their enemies

A cause can also run on its enemies. The opponent becomes a permanent adversary, a fundraising object, a source of righteous identity, or a spectacle of deserved suffering. The target may have done wrong; that does not erase standing.

[The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) draws the line between stopping and consuming. Stopping is oriented by the wrong and ends when the threat ends. Consumption is oriented by the cause's need for an enemy, and no state of the wrongdoer terminates it. The near form is righteousness: treating the complicit with contempt in order to feel clean by contrast.

This page is exposed to the same risk. A catalog of capture can itself become a way of consuming the captured, the complicit, or the exposed. The protection is not innocence; it is discipline about use.

## Speaking-for without answerability

Advocacy often begins where direct voice is blocked. That does not make representation possessive. It becomes possessive when the represented party's inability to audit becomes the advocate's authority.

[Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) gives the conditions: speaking-for must be provisional, governed by the represented party's good, revisable, and answerable where later answerability becomes possible. Where the represented party can never audit the advocacy, substitute contestation is required rather than immunity.

The grievance is familiar: being used as content, symbol, moral proof, or fundraising surface by people claiming to help. The framework's answer is not silence on behalf of the vulnerable. It is stewardship under constraint.

## Academic and professional capture

Academic and professional fields can make persons available under refined descriptions: research subjects as data, students as advisor-dependent labor, contingent teachers as replaceable capacity, patients or clients as cases, junior members as reputational risk to be managed.

The framework's categories cut across these settings, but not every case has the same mechanism:

- [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) names the file, category, diagnosis, risk profile, or metric outranking the person it was meant to help an institution answer to.
- [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity) names formal choice inside a field where refusal has been priced beyond reach: the contingent teacher who "accepts" overload, the student whose advisor controls access, the junior member whose career depends on staying useful.
- [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability)'s judgment/jurisdiction line names the advisor, supervisor, reviewer, clinician, or gatekeeper whose judgment stops being answerable to the person judged and becomes a standard the person must survive.

The point is not that institutions should lack standards. It is that standards imposed on people must remain callable by them or by structures that genuinely answer to them.

## Doctrine as capture

The framework's final risk is itself. Any theory can become a jurisdiction: a loyalty test, a language one must speak to be heard, a credential by which people rank each other, or a doctrine insulated from the objections it claims to welcome.

[Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) is meant to resist that hardening by separating conceptual layer, argumentative support, provenance, and dependencies. [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) gives the transmission discipline: presentation of the framework must remain provisional, revisable, and answerable to readers' objections. [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction) blocks purity as rank.

None of these safeguards certifies success. A community can adopt the framework as reputation repair, moral credential, or new orthodoxy. If it does, the framework has become material for exactly the wrong it names.

## What this page does not claim

- It is not a history or catalogue of cases.
- It does not claim the framework would have prevented the harms it describes.
- It does not indict movements, fields, professions, or their members as such.
- It is not an alibi. Using the framework to recover standing after a scandal, without changing the arrangement that produced the scandal, repeats the possessive form.

## Limits

- Selection is editorial and shaped by proximity to the framework's concerns.
- Every fit-claim is contestable by showing that the category is unmet.
- The practical claim is modest: bright-line commitments can make drift visible. No evidence is offered that they are sufficient to stop it.
- The page is vulnerable to the consuming form it criticizes; the ordering rule, own side first, is a discipline rather than a certification.

## Related pages

[Points of Entry](/wiki/Points-of-Entry) · [The Wrongdoer's Standing](/wiki/The-Wrongdoers-Standing) · [Infrastructuralization](/wiki/Infrastructuralization) · [Advocacy as Stewardship of Voice](/wiki/Advocacy-as-Stewardship-of-Voice) · [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) · [Administrative Legibility](/wiki/Administrative-Legibility) · [Answerability](/wiki/Answerability) · [Provision Before Prevention](/wiki/Provision-Before-Prevention) · [Standing-Based Reproductive Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-Reproductive-Ethics) · [Standing-Based End-of-Life Ethics](/wiki/Standing-Based-End-of-Life-Ethics) · [Labor Under Engineered Necessity](/wiki/Labor-Under-Engineered-Necessity) · [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) · [Registers of Claim](/wiki/Registers-of-Claim) · [Complicity and Direction](/wiki/Complicity-and-Direction)
````

# File: src/app/wiki/mdx/Complicity-and-Direction.mdx

- Title: Complicity and Direction
- Slug: Complicity-and-Direction
- Aliases: none
- Navigation group: Rivals and practical orientation
- Layer: orientation
- Support: derived, defended, optional, open, empirical
- Provenance: application, personal-orientation
- Depends on: Possession, Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures, Residue, Standing-Answerability, Arrangements-and-Lives

````mdx
# Complicity and Direction

## Summary

**Complicity and direction** names the practical orientation Nume attaches to [the Standing Framework](/wiki/Standing-and-Answerability-Ethics) under conditions of pervasive dependence on arrangements it criticizes. Conditional on that empirical description, no presently available course is free of every condemned dependency. Neither capitulation nor purity follows: an incomplete refusal can still reduce what is drawn from particular someones, while no collection of practices establishes moral cleanness or licenses ranking lives.

Nume's optional response is to replace *am I clean?* with *what do my actions do, and to whom?* It gives priority to using one's actual power to make others less available for possession or extraction, while also reducing one's reliance on their availability through feasible withdrawals. The framework itself establishes only narrower constraints and domain-specific exit duties. It does not entail this ordering of practical effort, and the empirical claim of pervasive complicity remains open to counterexample.

## The embedded condition

The framework's analyses of [Possession](/wiki/Possession), holding, and wrongful structures apply to many supply chains, labor markets, administrative systems, and inherited institutions on which people presently depend. Food, shelter, income, and communication commonly run through arrangements the framework criticizes. Conditional on that empirical description, two consequences follow:

- No available course of action within those conditions yields non-complicity. [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) may reduce participation without producing a position outside every dependency.
- Complicity in that sense is not a sufficient basis for ranking persons. [Arrangements and Lives](/wiki/Arrangements-and-Lives) separately bars moving from a verdict on an arrangement to a verdict on a life.

## Two failure responses

The framework diagnoses two standard responses to discovering the embedded condition, and holds that both rest on the same mistake — treating cleanness as the goal, and differing only in whether they declare it unreachable or reached.

**Capitulation.** From the empirical premise that no available course under present conditions is free of every condemned dependency, an inference is drawn to the conclusion that no partial refusal matters. The inference does not follow: a refusal can reduce what is drawn from particular someones even while the wider structure survives. The stronger claim that capitulation typically functions to dissolve scruples is Nume's practical diagnosis, not a derived fact about every person who declines a refusal.

**Purity.** The opposite response assembles a set of practices — dietary, financial, consumptive — into a position experienced as clean, from which others' complicity becomes visible and gradable. The framework's objection is not that such practices are worthless; they may be genuine partial refusals. Under the empirical embedded-condition claim, the asserted completion is false because dependencies remain. Purity used as a credential can also make other people support the holder's self-regard through esteem and captured judgment. It becomes possession only where subordination, nullity, and extraction assemble; ranking conduct is not by itself the entire structure.

## The reorientation (Nume's stance)

From here the page describes Nume's practical response, which the framework does not entail.

The pivot is from self-assessment to effect: from *am I implicated?* to *what do my choices and my power actually do, to which someones, in which direction?* On Nume's stance, compromised agency does not disqualify action; the relevant question is what the available action changes.

The direction of effort has two components, deliberately ordered:

- **Reducing one's draw** on the availability of others: withdrawing participation from condemned arrangements where feasible — consumption choices, sourcing, refusals. Nume treats this as real but secondary, and flags its characteristic distortion: because consumption is countable, it invites relapse into self-measurement — the purity response rebuilt as arithmetic.
- **Reducing others' availability through one's power** — the component Nume weights more heavily. Wherever a person holds actual power over someones — as employer, parent, landlord, buyer of labor, keeper of animals — they can structure that power on [Standing Answerability](/wiki/Standing-Answerability) at individual scale: contestable terms, survivable refusal, welfare as a binding limit. On this stance, a person's treatment of those within their power matters more than their consumption profile, and the two can diverge sharply in both directions.

Two boundary notes complete the stance. Sustaining oneself — rest, pleasure, ordinary life — is treated as a condition of continuing, not a betrayal, with the test being whether it sustains the effort or replaces it. And the stance offers no terminus: no quantity of redirection yields acquittal, because [Settlement](/wiki/Settlement) says there is no party positioned to grant it. What the stance offers instead of resolution is a sustainable direction.

## Why this is not doctrine

The framework cannot derive this general ordering of practical life, and the page records why rather than blurring it. From the embedded condition and the diagnoses, multiple responses remain open: a reader might adopt different priorities among refusals, weight consumption over power or the reverse, pursue structural change exclusively, or conclude that the framework's demands exceed what can be lived and revise their assent accordingly. The framework ranks none of these. Its narrower constraints are that a partial refusal is not null merely because it is incomplete, that judgment of an arrangement does not become a verdict on a person's life, and that any practice bearing all three possession marks is excluded.

This openness does not establish that every particular withdrawal is optional. [Exit from Wrongful Structures](/wiki/Exit-from-Wrongful-Structures) proposes a controlled-function bridge under which a domain-specific duty follows where conduct is empirically shown to participate in a possessive function and the exit conditions are met. That conclusion requires withdrawal from the identified function; it does not rank every form of refusal, direct use of power, or structural action, and it does not turn participation into a verdict on the participant. Diffuse and de minimis market cases remain open. Nume's broader ordering of practical effort therefore remains one optional stance within the space left after particular duties are identified.

## Limits

- The doctrine/stance boundary above is this page's central content; readers citing "the framework's position" on practical life should separate the narrow constraints from Nume's diagnosis and ordering of responses.
- The stance's ordering (power over consumption) rests on Nume's judgment of where effect concentrates, not on an argument the framework provides.
- The framework supplies no comparative rule for ranking all permitted practical responses. Whether such a rule can be added without converting practical orientation into a standing hierarchy remains open on this page rather than becoming framework doctrine.

## Related pages

````
